The Selfish Gene

by Deliciouskeys

Summary

[COMPLETE] Homelander is really, really intent on having a child. Like, scarily intent.

Canon divergence where Ryan dies in the season 3 finale and the story sharply veers from canon from there. Homelander becomes desperate to have another child, but nothing works until he modifies his body to carry it himself. He asks the guy who’s also lived through the trauma of losing Ryan for help with that noble mission. “Asks.” Billy Butcher has many misgivings, but tries to make lemonade out of lemons and plots to use the situation to try and pry Homelander out of Vought.
Neither one of them foresees what they’re really getting themselves into.

Notes

Canon divergence around Season 3 finale. Also, no temp V illness for Billy or anyone else in this verse.

Basically pure shameless self-indulgence. More than the usual amount, even by AO3 standards.
Did you want to read about Homelander being pregnant?
Did you want to read some needless nerdy biology details of how and why and wherefore?
Did you want to read some scarily dubious consent?
No? Why not! >:|

OCs are named for random people who create the show, any resemblance is purely coincidental.

Chapter 1: Aug 28, 2022

August 28, 2022

Homelander is still in bed when the phone rings. He hadn't been asleep. It was nearly noon, and he tries not to stay in bed all morning anymore. But on a day like today, he wasn't about to demand anything of himself.

In the months right after it happened he spent entire days mostly in bed, often forgoing meals or basic hygiene. He moved the landline phone to his bedside table during that time, to spare himself the need to get out from under the covers for every minor inane call. Not that Vought employees pestered him too much lately. He hasn't done a single thing for Vought in the past twelve months, and they still maintained his penthouse apartment and brought him three meals a day. Early on they tried giving him officious advice about seeing therapists or trying pharmaceuticals to help ease the pain. They didn't seem to understand that this wasn't depression—this was grief. They were probably hoping he'd snap out of it eventually, and stopped pressing the issue.

Homelander reaches over on the sixth or seventh ring. "What," he snaps into the receiver, the gravelliness of his voice giving away that he hasn't used it yet today.

"Sir, there's someone claiming to be Billy Butcher calling, asking to get put through to you. We can refuse if-"

"Put him through," Homelander cuts the Vought dispatcher off, lying back on the pillow, holding the bridge of his nose and squeezing his eyes shut, his already sour expression souring further. The day was already awful enough as it was. A call from a man he hasn't seen or heard from in a year can't make it that much worse.

There's a click and then an awkward silence. Homelander isn't about to speak first, so he waits, staring at the ceiling in his bedroom.

"...'Lo?" William's voice comes crackling over the line.

"Why are you calling." It doesn't sound like a question.

"Don't rightly know, to be honest. Just the date and all. Been thinkin' about it again. Feel proper rotten about it. And then I thought of you. Realized you might be the one soul on this earth who feeling even more rotten about it than me."

Homelander closes his eyes, inhaling. "Yeah, I'm not sure if rotten is the word. I've been rotting away for quite a while now. I don't feel anything anymore."

There was silence on the line for a moment. "Look. I'm not sure I know what to say, but I had to try. Couldn't live with the guilt of what happened at first. Blamed it all on you, for bringing the lad to that confrontation. But it's on me too. Whole thing seems so petty now. I was so bent on finding a way to destroy you, right up until it happened. Now? Don't feel like it matters a jot."

"Well." Homelander sighs. "You certainly destroyed something in me."

"I know. And it weren't worth what it ended up costing. At all."

Homelander doesn't respond.

William continues after a pause. "Can't say I miss seeing you on the telly. But it's a bit disconcerting. A world without Homelander-- even knowing you're still there, hiding up in Vought tower somewhere."

"I'm not hiding," Homelander bites back. "I just completely lost interest in all the things that used to occupy my time."

William's voice drops quieter. "I know. That's how I know you've felt proper wretched the whole year. I... I never wanted it to go like this. I miss him so much. He's all I had left of Becca."

They stay on the line, both quiet. A tear slowly rolls out of the corner of Homelander's eye and down the side of his face into his ear.

"Anything else you wanted to get off your chest, William? Because I've got nothing to say to you." Homelander is desperate to get off the phone because he feels the grief surging back, threatening to disrupt the quiet apathy he's tried to cultivate to deal with the despair. He needs to get off the phone before William can figure out he's started crying.

"No, look... you take care of yourself. Shit. Never thought I'd say that to the likes of you.” William hangs up abruptly on that incoherent note and Homelander slams the receiver back into its cradle and curls up in a fetal position, pulling the bedcovers over his head.

He's tried very hard not to keep revisiting the day of the tragedy, but it's a lost cause today. He's replayed it so many times that the memories are probably distorted by now. It's hard to reconstruct what happened during the blast, but all he knows is his body moved faster than his conscious thoughts, avoiding the scorching heat of the explosion on instinct. One moment he was in Vought Tower facing off with Soldier Boy, the next he was hovering half a mile above Manhattan, well out of harm's reach, completely undamaged. Why he couldn't have grabbed Ryan on his way up out of Vought tower is something that will forever remain inexplicable and unconscionable to him, no matter how many people try to convince him that he shouldn't blame himself.

The memories of what comes afterward make him feel nauseous. He doesn't want to remember how he searched for Ryan, or what state his body was in when he found him, likely depowered by the blast before he plummeted the hundred or so stories to the pavement below. But those images are seared into his mind, ready for recall at any provocation. Homelander remembers the feeling of wanting to delude himself, about being frantic to take Ryan to the hospital despite knowing deep down that these were absolutely fatal injuries. Gathering up what was left of his son in his arms, yelling at staff at the Mount Sinai ER to take him in without any delays, thinking about lasering some innocent bystanders out of sheer frustration that no one seemed to be doing anything to help—it all felt better than facing the truth at that point. He knew he was in hysterics, and he knew every person in the ER was absolutely terrified of him. They took Ryan's body through the double doors on a gurney and tried to keep Homelander out in the waiting room, not a single doctor willing to be the one to tell him that his son was pronounced dead on arrival. 

Vought graciously paid every official tabloid to keep photos and footage from the hospital that day out of the public sphere, but of course a lot of it was still floating around online. Homelander has never watched any of it.

He didn't let them keep the body in the hospital morgue—took Ryan's remains to his Vought tower penthouse, and lay in bed with them for more than a day. He cried over his son, pleaded with the universe to let this all be a bad dream or some reversible curse, just some terrible cruel joke being played on him that would end any moment, until people finally convinced him to let Ryan be taken away. They didn't hold a funeral. Homelander stashed the urn of ashes on some shelf in his living room and never looked at it again. It provided no comfort.

The public was sympathetic. Fans wrote in condolences, and thanked him for ridding New York of the terrorist scourge, even though Homelander had nothing to do with subduing and putting Soldier Boy back into cryogenic storage. It must have been William and his team who dealt with that. Homelander couldn't care less about it, or about how the event got covered in the news.

He hadn't planned on retiring. He hadn't even planned on taking a long bereavement leave, but days turned to weeks and weeks turned to months and he has to admit a year is a long time to spend grieving.

He hasn't been lying in bed all year though. A couple of months after the tragedy, Homelander became consumed with the idea of having another child. Vought found plenty of willing surrogates. He never bothered to meet or screen any of them, outsourcing the entire endeavor to Vought's Reproductive Science Labs. It didn't matter who these women were at this point, only whether they could carry his child. He figured he could meet whoever won that lottery afterwards. And it did seem more and more like a lottery in terms of long odds, as months passed with no success. They had gone through more than fifty volunteers, with nothing taking at all or an early miscarriage, each and every attempt. They tried using rare supe surrogates, IVF, intracytoplasmic sperm injection, all to no avail.

Earlier, Homelander accepted his infertility as a simple fact of life, and part and parcel of how exceptional he was. He couldn't be satisfied with that now, though. The more failure he encountered, the more desperate he became, because it had worked once before, dammit! Why wasn't anyone able to figure out how to make it happen again? Now that both Becca and Ryan were dead, it was that much less likely they would ever learn how to capture that lightning in a bottle.

Homelander would demand explanations for the failures and would then regret asking, the doctors at Vought labs stammering on and on about all sorts of problems, eggs apparently unable to keep sperm at bay after one fertilization, unsettling descriptions of hundreds of sperm rushing into an egg and bursting it, single spermatozoids still managing to puncture eggs with such force that they would lose integrity before any division. Even when the researchers tried dissecting out sperm nuclei and inject them into an egg without trauma, some kind of aberrant epigenetic programming in his DNA would kick in once implanted. It seemed to interfere with proper development, making the embryo begin to overuse resources and then get rejected by the mother's body as something invasive. "Selfish genes" the scientists referred to the phenomenon in shorthand. Ultimately, it all came down to one thing: he couldn't seem to have a child with anyone, unenhanced human or supe.

The good thing about putting Vought on this case was that they always had top-notch scientists on their payroll, the most advanced knowledge of supe genetics, and were invested in figuring out how this biology worked for reasons besides his personal quest to have a child. The downside was that sometimes Homelander would get deeply paranoid that they wouldn't tell him if and when they succeeded. There wasn't much stopping them from creating a child without his knowledge and hiding him away again like they did with Ryan. He had no way to surveil every single thing they did in that lab on this project, but he eavesdropped on them frequently. He also took to visiting the lab, just to put the fear of god into them about working faster and not hiding their progress from him.

The one thing that can get him out of bed and put on his clothes today is deciding to take a stroll down to the reproductive labs floor. 

"Homelander!" the receptionist at the desk chirps as he walks past her without ceremony. He never signs in, or puts on scrubs, or jumps through any of the hoops he's supposed to before going into a regulated lab environment.

"Any progress since last week?" he asks the first familiar face he sees in a labcoat, adding his name after glancing at his name tag. "...Craig?"

The man startles as he looks up from the bench. He is one of the newer hires to join the project, young, full of ideas, but he also still blanches every time Homelander speaks to him. It might be because Homelander has been making less of an effort to put on a polite, cheerful persona. These people were working for him, as far as he was concerned, and it wasn't his responsibility to put them at ease.

"Oh. Yes. The team's been working on the idea to CRISPR edit some of the sperm DNA and change the methylation patterns in vitro. We're still in the process of testing out exactly which genes are causing the issue. It might just be one or two loci that need to be silenced to stop the genome from being so... aggressive."

"But then it won't exactly be my own DNA anymore," Homelander says, smiling to show he's not holding this against the young scientist, at least not personally. He still hears Craig's heartrate rise and his leg muscles beginning to shake a little bit.

"Yes, that's... that's an interesting point. It's something we need to consider. Whether those genes are responsible for any superpowered functions. But, fingers crossed, it will require only a few minor changes. In the scheme of things, it's still your DNA." Craig stumbles over his words a little bit.

"Have you tried thinking of ways that don't involve fucking around with my DNA that could solve this problem?"

"We..." Craig stammers, clearly searching for an adequate answer. "See if it wasn't sperm we were dealing with but oocytes with this kind of epigenetic programming, we probably wouldn't need to edit anything..."

Homelander raises an eyebrow. "What do you mean by that?"

"I'm..." The young doctor swallows hard. Homelander starts to find the fast, loud heartbeats annoying. "I'm... just thinking out loud here. It's not something we can do. But I was thinking the other day that the selfish programming would be less of a problem in general in a woman. No egg competition. And a female supe might have been able to just handle the unusual extra resource demands. But it's not going to help in your case unfortunately. Even if we could switch around sperm and egg nuclei easily, the key is the supe with the selfish DNA would have to be the one carrying the fetus."

"I see." Homelander's eyes narrow. They stand in an awkward silence until Homelander turns to walk back out of the lab without any other pleasantries.

"Thanks for stopping by!" Craig calls after him, voice trailing off.

Chapter 2: Sept 2&amp;15, 2022

September 2, 2022

"Didn't you go by 'Resecta' at one point?" Homelander asks as he sits down in a hard mahogany chair and examines Dr. Sonnenberg's wall, covered in diplomas and certificates.

"Yeah, terrible name, before I broke my parents' hearts and went to medical school instead of auditioning to join Vought's supe network." Homelander shakes his head, somewhat offended by her assumption and determined to thoroughly check how he looks in the mirror later on. But he doesn't have time to dwell on it now. "I've heard you do organ reconstruction on the side? Besides your vanity surgeries?"

Dr. Sonnenberg looks at him quizzically. "I'm only licensed to use my powers for elective, cosmetic surgery."

Homelander leans forward and lowers his voice since she seems cagey. "Look, this isn't a sting operation. I'm looking for a specific type of service and willing to pay a lot of money for it."

"I've done it for people who came out of accidents or had cancer surgery. Kidney renewals for people running out of time while still at the bottom of the donor list. But it's much more complex work. And people don't always survive."

Now here was a supe who was putting her talents to extraordinary uses without any of the Vought PR machine behind her, Homelander thinks to himself.

"Have you reconstructed female reproductive systems?" he asks, feeling a strange rush as he says it. He still can't quite believe how far he's decided to go to try to have a child.

"Yes..." Dr. Sonnenberg answers, sounding very hesitant. "Mostly for women who had unavoidable hysterectomies."

There's an awkward silence as Homelander mulls over how to phrase the next question. Before he can, Dr. Sonnenberg asks quietly "Have you seriously injured someone? I can be discreet, but I don't know if I'm comfortable with covering up for something where a police report hasn't been filed-"

"No," Homelander cuts her off. "Nothing of the sort. What I want to know is, have you built ovaries that actually function in transsexuals, or whatever they go by nowadays? You know. People born XY."

Dr. Sonnenberg shakes her head, still continuing to look at him askance. "I haven't dipped into that market. But I've built the entire system from scratch in women a couple of times. It's not a trivial procedure."

The doctor's eyes widen and she raises her eyebrows skeptically.

"No, I'm interested in the whole thing. Uterus that can carry a baby, ovaries that make viable eggs. It all has to be functional."

The doctor stares at him. "I have serious doubts I can get your body to mold at all," she finally says, still looking him up and down as if she's also having doubts that this is the real celebrity from TV sitting in her office, and not just some impersonator. But she invites him into the adjoining examining room, just to have a look as part of the consultation.

 

September 15, 2022

It's the fifth straight day of shaping surgery. It should be the last day, if all goes well. Dr. Sonnenberg said she was leaving the vaginal canal and outer anatomy for last, claiming that was the most trivial part and she preferred to start with the areas presenting the biggest challenges.

She tried to dissuade him many times before even starting, making no promises of success, emphasizing that even if she sculpted something that looked correct, it still had little chance of being functional in a man. She warned him that it would probably take multiple days to finish a project like that in a body like his. She warned him that she couldn't give him painkillers because his body appeared to swiftly inactivate and metabolize anesthetic agents, and that the surgery would likely hurt.

It does hurt, like an absolute motherfucker. The amount of pain makes Homelander's head swim. Nothing has felt this excruciating since childhood, when they were pressure-testing his limits. He's been spending four agonizing hours each day with his legs up in the metal lithotomy stirrups, hands balled into fists to prevent him from gripping and breaking the operating table, and a rubber mouthguard between his teeth that he would easily destroy if he bit down on it in earnest, serving more as a reminder not to grind his teeth. For those four hours, she sits between his legs, peering through his abdomen and perineum, her face always concentrated and frowning as she mentally directs his body to reshape itself to grow brand new organs-- only rarely breaking her concentration to glance at an anatomy book for reference on a particular detail. Money doesn't even seem to be her primary motivator. Homelander will pay her hundreds of thousands even if she doesn't succeed and millions if every milestone is met and he ends up with a healthy child at the end of all of this. But it seems more of a point of pride and maybe curiosity about whether she can do it. Homelander's glad. He was looking for a perfectionist to do this work.

Homelander wishes he could be more helpful. He tries not to just endure the pain but work with her, trying to put mind over matter and summoning all his willpower not to leap to his feet and fly far away, to be absolutely, perfectly still, and not put up any resistance despite what feels like being ripped apart below the waist. He mentally commands his body to give up the fight already and gratefully accept the changes being made. Even if that doesn't do anything in reality, it gives him something to focus on other than his pain. He tries to do breathing exercises, closes his eyes and visualizes not just a successful surgery but the endgame, the happily ever after, how it will feel to have a baby growing inside himself, how happy he'll be to bring him into the world and have an immediate, unconditional loving bond. He's not going to repeat the mistakes Vought made with him, and that he made with Ryan. He'll never expose his child to anyone he doesn't trust. Maybe they'll live alone, completely reclusive. They might become eccentric, but at least his son will be safe. When Homelander sinks deep into these fantasies about the future, he can almost ignore how much he's hurting in the moment. "I'm routing the vagina dorsally to your prostate. But it's pretty crowded. I'm making the muscle sleeve as elastic as I can, but sex might hurt. There's awkward angles."

He forgot that his lasers are still locked and loaded and unnerve her. He dutifully redirects his gaze upward. "As long as I can give birth through it, I don't care about pain."

"Yeah, that's a challenge I'm aware of. Usually I'd say just schedule a C-section instead of traumatizing contrived organs, but that may not be an option in your case. I'm doing my best."

Homelander gives a pained nod and puts the mouthguard back in, staring at the seconds hand of the clock on the wall ticking forward.

"You better want to have this child very badly..." she says after a long period of silent work. Homelander's not sure what she means until she adds, "You're probably risking serious injury and heartache if you try."

Another hour goes by and Homelander suddenly feels it, like his body down there pops open to the outside world. The doctor sits back and wipes her brow. ”Almost all done. You want all your male organs to stay functional?”

Homelander shakes his head.

Chapter 3: Sept 17, 2022

His skin actually looks younger and healthier, as if he's started up an intense moisturizing routine or something. He doesn't know whether to chalk that up to hormones or just a better mood than he's had in a long time.

Homelander quickly scrolls through his agenda for the remainder of the day but sees no other last minute additions aside from this infernal morning meeting. His inbox also has zero evidence that Ashley accomplished anything useful yesterday. Yesterday afternoon he summoned Ashley to his apartment and gave her official notice that he was pregnant. Instead of springing into action to cascade the news appropriately, she started stammering like an idiot, paling and reddening by turns. When she finally managed to ask him how he'd accomplished this, he kept it simple for her, just told her he'd modified his body to make it possible. It wasn't really any of her business. Ashley just continued gawking at him instead of taking action. This is why she got demoted back down from CEO almost as soon as he fell into mourning and wasn't there to hold her hand and yell orders at her about what needed to get done. The board didn't call it a demotion, of course. They pretended it had been an interim position all along, holding down the fort while they found a real replacement for Stan Edgar. She should be grateful they put her back in the vice president of Hero Management position and not just summarily escorted her off the premises, Homelander thought to himself, watching her stupid, scared expression. He rolled his eyes and started spelling out a list of things she needed to do, since she was apparently incapable of thinking for herself: plan out how and where he can break the happy news to the public (he could easily slip in the announcement into the Vought Christmas special if Vought marketing had no objections), inform Vought reproductive labs that they were going to kill all the projects involving his sperm, arrange for interview appearances for him with reputable networks, do proactive reach out to Gerber, Heinz, Huggies, Pampers, you name it, and start bidding wars between baby food and diaper companies for product placement and endorsements. Ashley was nodding at him the whole time but her eyes looked vacant, and the slow speed with which she was taking notes made Homelander suspect her mind was clearly focused elsewhere. She looked like she had a dozen questions on the tip of her tongue but mumbled something about needing to get a few other people into this discussion and ran out of the room with quick inelegant steps on her stilettos.

Homelander glances at the calendar invite to check the room again. At least Ashley booked the conference room on 99 and not some godforsaken fishbowl mid-building. There isn't even a title on the meeting, nor any other attendees listed. Ashley really needs to get her shit together—he couldn't keep covering for her. He looks through the doors of the conference room as he approaches them and suddenly sees this isn't going to be just him, Ashley, and a couple of her miserable underlings. No, what looks like the entire board of Vought is sitting around the V shaped desk. Bill Marsh is sitting in his chair and this grates on Homelander's nerves immediately, but he supposes the CEO is the one person he can't rightfully kick out of it. They're talking quietly but Homelander doesn't feel like listening in at this point, when he's already running a fashionable three minutes late.

He puts on a polite smile before opening the doors, feigning surprise. "Good morning everyone! Wow, Ashley. You certainly got the whole gang assembled for this one!"

Part of him is flattered that every important person in this company was convened. It reinforces just how integral he is to the company, even after his long absence. But another part of him starts to feel a bit cornered, because it feels like he's walked into some sort of intervention, and the fact that he hears several heartbeats pick up speed as he entered the room isn't helping. He's standing there, as if he's on trial, and now he wishes he opted to put his hands on his hips instead of behind his back, which somehow feels like defensive body language when they're all staring at him. He looks over at Ashley, all the way at the end of the table, in an extra chair that doesn't belong to the set and is usually not at this table. She's no help-- pale and glued to her seat, eyes darting back and forth between Homelander and the other people in the room. The silence is awkward, and Homelander begins wondering if they're somehow expecting him to start speaking. Maybe this meeting isn't even about his pregnancy... but many of them do seem to be trying to eye his midriff without being too obvious about it.

Marsh finally decides to take ownership of this ridiculous meeting. "Thank you for coming in early like this, Homelander. Please take a seat."

The only free chair is at the stupid little serif of the V, so he takes it, gritting his teeth, feeling like he's facing all of them from the opposite side of where he rightfully should be sitting. He remembers himself and smiles again, raising his eyebrows expectantly.

"Ms. Barrett relayed some news you gave her yesterday, but could you just explain it to us one more time?"

"No problem," Homelander says, hearing an edge of sarcasm slip through in his tone because it's ridiculous that they don't take her word for it. "I've been interested in having a child for a while now, so I opted to modify my body and got pregnant. The baby's due in June, and I figured Vought could help me coordinate announcing it to the public, and all those other logistics. I'm not asking to be relieved of superhero duties, at least for now. I'll be playing it by ear, but I feel great so far."

Just as he says this, a faint breeze in the room from the HVAC system carries over the smell of Pat Willis' breakfast sandwich that he somehow thought it was appropriate to bring in to a meeting, as well as several people's coffees and Homelander does his utmost not to scrunch his face from the queasiness those smells raise immediately.

"Now when you say 'modify'..." Marsh pauses for a moment, chewing his lip. He's nervous, somehow. "What exactly do you mean?"

"I found a means to add a female reproductive system to my body," Homelander says, careful not to sound exasperated with their slow uptake. "Look, I know it's unusual, but I figure that's all the more reason Vought can milk this into some high voltage publicity, right?"

"One of the things we really want to emphasize in this meeting is that we don't want you to announce anything about this right now," one of the female execs whose name Homelander can't even bother to remember says to him sharply.

Homelander stares at her, wondering who the fuck this woman is to take that tone with him, and briefly imagines the probably bad fallout of just lasering his head off right in that moment.

"Anne, it's okay, we're having a discussion here," Marsh says, maybe reading Homelander's face too well. "You see, it's a bit of a liability for us, what you did."

"What are you all talking about." Homelander can't keep the exasperation out of his tone now. "If you think this kind of thing will tank my ratings, sure, run it through the focus groups, figure out how to message it. I don't really see why it would be a problem, frankly. I'm not transitioning gender or anything bizarre like that. This just happened to be a way for me to have another biological child. People should eat that shit up."

"It's not about that, sir," Anne blurts out, also seemingly exasperated. "You modifying your body reveals that you have vulnerabilities. You need to tell our scientists about how you modified your body, and it needs to be kept a secret, certainly not announced publi—"

"You expect me to just not announce anything at all?!"

"Homelander, Homelander..." Willis tries to cut in, clearly trying to appease him. Homelander just winces at the smell of bacon wafting out as he speaks, even though he's two seats away. "All she means to say is, you can have your pregnancy, in private, and then reemerge in public, child in tow. That shouldn't pose a problem."

"Who's the fa—the other parent of this child?" Marsh cuts them all off. "If it isn't too prying of us to ask."

"An anonymous donor," Homelander says woodenly. His body is starting to vacillate between fight and flight at this unexpectedly adversarial meeting.

"An anonymous donor that you know the identity of, though, right?" Marsh asks. "And if you don't, we can probably figure it out for you. I hear Analytics can comb the 23andme and myheritage databases pretty quickly these days."

"I don't need anyone to comb anything. I know who he is," Homelander finally says to cut him off. Unbelievable. "Why does that matter?"

"Well, Vought needs to know who this anonymous donor is, because there may be huge liabilities and lawsuits in the future, if this donor ever finds out he's your child's parent."

"It's not going to be an issue. What in the world are you talking about?" Homelander asks, not caring if he's going to appear naïve or uneducated to these people anymore. He knows this is ridiculous. He has a right to have a child, a right not have to hide this fact from the public, and a right not to tell them who the other parent is.

"We also need to know where it was that you got your, uh, modification done."

"Why." Homelander bites off tersely.

"Because we need to know who has technology that can change your body, and probably buy them out so we can own the technology. Nothing out of the ordinary, no need to worry."

"It's not as if..." Homelander is so frustrated he can barely summon the right words. "It's not something that could have been done without my consent. It's not weaponizable or anything. It took a long time and a lot of cooperation from me."

"Nevertheless. We just want to talk to whoever has this tech."

"I don't really feel like disclosing that right now."

"Is it the clinic in Long Island that you've made several large payments to in the past three months?" Anne asks.

Homelander flinches. "Is it common practice for Vought to go through my bank account statements?"

"It's not really your bank account—" Anne starts saying but very quickly gets cut off by Willis.

"It's just standard procedure for large sums of money moving between banks. We're just doing due diligence."

So many people in the room are sweating, hearts racing, that Homelander can't really even hear himself think at this point, unable to block them out and really consider what's unfolding here.

Bill Marsh is calmer than the rest although his heartrate is still clocking around 90 bpm, but at least his voice is even and steady. "I'm sorry. We didn't mean to put you on the spot with so many questions at once. We can revisit this discussion later this week. Vought is completely supportive of everything you choose to do. We just can't disclose everything we want to the public. Like Pat said, we are more than happy to give you time off to have your pregnancy out of the public eye. If you've really modified yourself to be able to bear children, Vought can even offer you help in obtaining the best genetic material, and you can have as many children as you want..."

Homelander begins to hear his own heart start pounding in his ears. The fuck is this new proposition? They don't seem to be lying—they want him to have children, in secret, with some "best genetic material" they're helpfully picking out? This is a breeding plan. He feels a visceral revulsion arising in him, and it's visceral enough that, despite this being the last thing he needs at the moment, he gets up and makes his quick way to the small garbage bin near the door, gripping its sides as he kneels and vomits into it. He hears Ashley gasp. In fact he heard everyone's heartrates rise to a deafening chorus of about 200 the moment he bolted up from his seat. They're clearly afraid of what his reaction might be, but not afraid enough to be clever about this conversation. There's no Stan Edgars or Madelyns in this room to deftly shame or coax him into doing their bidding. He doesn't have to put up with any of this.

Marsh speaks up when Homelander's stopped heaving and wipes his mouth with gloved hand, trying to politely ignore what just happened. "First things first. We'll take you down to the medical floor, and they'll have a look at you, do an ultrasound and all that..."

"There's no need," Homelander says hoarsely, acid still in his throat, slowly standing up and resolving to leave the room instead of staying for any more of this.

"We just want—"

"I've already seen a doctor. It's all been checked," Homelander says more firmly.

"We understand but Vought also needs to do workup—"

"No," Homelander says and walks out the door fast enough that the cape billows out behind him. He hasn't been this angry since before his temporary retirement, and he also never saw this kind of reaction coming from Vought's higher-ups. This was going to be a lot more complicated than he anticipated.

"Quite a temper on him" he hears Marsh's voice even though he's already in his apartment, because he can't help listening in.

"Anne, we never, ever mention the money logistics to him."

"How am I supposed to know all these rules? He really has no idea that he's not earning a salary? He can't put two and two together?"

"Please don't discuss this in the building..." Ashley's scared little voice pipes up to warn them. She might be the only one who's aware of just how easy it is for him to eavesdrop on them. Her voice trails off because she probably realizes he can hear her just as well as the others.

"Ashley come over here rn" he texts her. Her gulp is so audible he can hear it from the conference room. He hears the hesitation in her step, but she comes to his apartment anyway.

"The door's open," he tells her, and watches her walk in, heart rate not even fast anymore. She looks like she's expecting to die any moment, and her body is starting to go into some kind of catatonia.

"I'm not gonna kill you," he says dismissively, and beckons her over to the couch.

She sits down slowly, far away from him and tortures her hair nervously, not even daring to look over at him. He sits still, continuing to listen to the others.

"You have to be gentle when you talk to him. He gets upset pretty easily," says someone who didn't speak up the entire meeting and Homelander is half tempted to walk back there and rip this patronizing man's head off, as soon as he identifies him.

"We can't fumble on this. I don't think we can just tell him 'your DNA is Vought intellectual property and you can only combine it with approved DNA'. That won't ever fly in a real court. We can figure out whose child it is later. We can make sure whoever it is is on board. It's not that different from the previous situation honestly. She agreed to work with us."

"The key is to get him on board with having more, and we're not going to do that by antagonizing him like this. Vogelbaum was trying to propagate that DNA for the longest time, and Reproductive Labs couldn't do it either, but he figured out some way. We have to be respectful."

"Maybe we should just let him have these pregnancies in public? He's not going to want to spend years in private just churning out babies."

"Sir?" Ashley finally says. Homelander's forgotten about her.

"Shh," he says, but gently. But the most interesting parts of the conversation have fizzled out as they sound like they're filing out of the room and heading their separate ways. Many of them don't even come in to work at Vought Tower most days.

"Sir, I am so, so sorry, I had no idea it was going to go like that, but I just wasn't sure what to do..." Ashley begins prattling on after another couple of minutes, clearly still afraid that she may not leave this room in one piece.

"No, Ashley, you're fine. I just want to ask you if you're still loyal to me."

Ashley's eyes grow round and scared. "Of course. Of course, sir!"

"What was that that they said about my bank account and salary?"

"I... I'm not sure about that part sir. I don't deal with the money," she says, almost crying. She is very likely lying right now. She was CEO for a brief blip there, and she always dealt very closely with Madelyn before getting canned and rehired. She must know what they're talking about. They all lie to him constantly. He should be more used to it by now, but it still catches him by surprise sometimes. No wonder they seem to think he's stupid.

"Alright," he says, weary of thinking of ways to get her to talk. She'd probably cave without any physical torture, but he's had enough negative feelings for one day. His stress and annoyance is not affecting just him anymore, he reminds himself. "Get back in there and report anything you hear being discussed about me by any of them, anything at all. And don't tell them I can hear them gossiping."

Ashley nods frantically and scurries out of the room when he jerks his chin up to dismiss her.

Homelander sits for a few minutes in silence, then stares down into his abdomen. He feels a strange urge to hold his child already, but makes do with stroking his own skin. "Causing so much trouble already."

He seriously contemplates calling Anonymous Donor, but then thinks better of it. In his paranoia, he opens his address book and changes William Butcher to AD, just in case Vought is going to pry into his cellphone records too. He has no idea what they can and cannot see anymore. He should probably assume they can see everything he does, to be on the safe side. He's still not sure what to make of all the talk about his bank account and salary. He certainly gets a salary. It's deposited in there monthly. Currently it's about $50k a month. It was more when he was working his ass off for the company. He certainly doesn't spend all that money, and periodically it gets invested for him. What the hell do they mean?

He suddenly realizes there's one person he should call. He dials Sonnenberg's office number and hears beeps. The answering machine picks up eventually, and he disconnects the call before the message starts being recorded. He realizes it's not even 8 am yet. He'll call her later, maybe give her some warning about the potential shitshow that's about to start with Vought Legal. He feels bad about it. She didn't have a high opinion of Vought, and neither does he, at the moment.

~~~

He calls Sonnenberg's office when it's almost noon, because he had some public appearances he had to do. Answering machine again. Maybe it's one of her days off? She had a receptionist when he set up the first appointment. He's trying to continue his day as normally as possible, although he's beginning to wonder why he's participating in anything Vought related after everything he heard that morning.

When he calls Sonnenberg's office again at three and still gets no reply, he decides to just fly over. The clinic doesn't have lights on. He sits on the roof for a while, and watches a car drive up and park near the building. A woman exits and walks up to the glass door and wraps her hands around her eyes to peer into the dark interior.

"You here for an appointment?" Homelander asks, realizing it was impolite to land softly on the ground behind her and start talking when he sees her startle.

"Yes..." she says turning around, then her eyes bug out as she sees who is asking the question. "Oh my god... are you... I can't believe it... are you her client?"

Homelander shakes his head noncommittally and even signs an autograph on a less than pristine napkin the woman digs out of her purse, more so to prevent further questions, but his mind is racing.

"This clinic is usually open on Wednesdays, right?"

The woman nods. "Rebecca's wonderful, I can't recommend her enough. She's touched up my face so many times, and it's noninvasive. Just the best in the business, but you're so handsome, my god, better than on TV, I don't think you need it, honey--"

Homelander nods and takes off before hearing the end of her babbling.

Did they really scoop her up between talking to him and when he called her at noon? They might have scooped her up earlier. Maybe Ashley had been busier than he thought cascading the news yesterday. They already knew about the clinic before he walked into that conference room. Homelander starts to feel a sort of panic. There's no one at Vought who can actually harm him physically, he's still certain of that, but did they just take away the one person he trusted to get him through this whole pregnancy and birthing ordeal? He's starting to feel cornered. Why did they take her? Because they seriously think her flesh-molding can be weaponized against him? Maybe because now they can dangle her as something he needs from them? His fists clench and even though he's close enough to be within sight of his landing platform he changes course and takes a sharp turn toward Queens.

It's been snowing all day, and William's balcony is covered in it. Homelander lands softly and looks in. He's stupid, it's not even 5pm, despite the sun having set, and of course William is out somewhere. Homelander considers his options of flying back to Vought Tower, breaking in and waiting for William in his living room, or patiently waiting on the balcony, out of sight of passerbys if he sits down. He opts for the last option. It's cold out, he doesn't want to break a window and make William's apartment uninhabitable for him. He's not going to fully admit it to himself but he's wary to go back to Vought Tower, lest they've thought of some creative ways to force his hand into doing everything they want him to do. He needs to think about how to find Sonnenberg and get her out of Vought's hands. He needs to think about what the fuck he's going to do in general. Vought pretty clearly sees him as a commodity they want to propagate. He's so immersed in mulling over all the possible moves he and Vought can make in this malicious chess game that he doesn't even notice William returning to the apartment.

"Straight up thought you were a bag of rubbish the upstairs neighbors chucked down. What the fuck you doing out there?" his harsh voice comes out of the apartment.

Homelander picks his head off his arms folded on his knees and realizes he's gotten covered in a layer of snow as it falls off of him when he moves.

"William, let me in please."

"What's happened to you, then?"

Homelander shakes his head in distaste. "Nothing, just let me in."

William just stands there with his arms crossed.

"I can break this glass without a problem," Homelander finally reminds him when he sees the other man is not moving to open the door.

"And why didn't you do it sooner then, you fucking ditz?"

Homelander approaches the door to the balcony, really wishing he didn't have to raise his voice to be heard through the thick glass. "I can't do this right now, it's been a really trying day. Just a complete clusterfuck."

"And you've come here for what exactly? I can't help ya, mate."

Homelander huffs, the condensation of his breath hitting the cold air making his exasperation all too visible.

"You were right, I was wrong. There. That what you wanted to hear?"

"Didn't wanna hear anything from you, to be honest." William's face is hard, unreadable. His heart rate is steady, but then it usually is in his presence. Homelander doesn't know what to say to get him to open the door, but he's not going back to Vought Tower tonight, dammit.

"Jesus fucking Christ," the other man groans and suddenly relents, unlocking the door. Homelander's face starts burning in shame when he realizes that tears he didn't notice have started rolling down the cold skin of his face, and that that's what finally moved William Butcher to let him in.

He brushes off more snow and wipes his cheeks before stepping inside.

"You sure it's alright bein' out in the snow like that with... you know," William gestures vaguely at Homelander's belly. "The one in there."

Homelander feels another pang of distress, when he quickly takes off his gloves and opens the front of his suit. His skin is cold. How far does the cold penetrate? He's warm blooded but he knows Vogelbaum tested him and saw his core body temperature could change. He doesn't even feel the cold as painful because of it.

He makes his way to the shower without asking for permission, tears now streaming down his face as he takes everything off and gets under a stream of hot water. He looks down and he can't see anything amiss, but then what does he know about hypothermia in the womb? And now that Vought has decided to abduct his doctor, it's not clear if he has anyone he can ask for an opinion.

"Here," William suddenly moves the shower curtain and hands him a cup of tea. "It's chamomile," he clarifies, rolling his eyes when Homelander examines the cup distrustfully. "No caffeine. Warm you right up from the inside."

Homelander looks up at him, studying William's face, the scar running down his forehead to his brow, the beard that he's let get a little bit unkempt compared to how he saw him last time.

"I can fetch you a mug hot water without anything in it if you're picky about it," he adds yet another suggestion, his eyes still looking judgemental, but the sentiment is a kind one.

Homelander shakes his head and takes a huge gulp from the mug, nodding his approval. "Thank you. I'm not thinking clearly all day. I'm sorry."

William leaves the corner of the tub and sits down on the toilet lid—Homelander can see his silhouette through the shower curtain even without penetrating vision.

"If I'd known what a pathetic little child you are, maybe I'd have just gone after Vought and not even bothered with you along the way," he says.

Homelander says nothing, still drinking the tea and making sure the shower stream is hitting his stomach.

"And see, today you've probably figured out they're just using you, but you must've worked that out a thousand times before. Come tomorrow or next week and you'll be goin' right back to them again. Damned if I knew why."

Homelander sniffles loudly enough that William must have heard it over the sound of the water.

"So what are you get choked up about now?"

"Because I don't know why either. I hate them. I'm scared of them. But I don't know anything else."

Homelander gets out of the shower and sees William steal a glance at his body. "Can I stay here? Please?"

"I told you, I'm not touching you 'til you pack it in with Vought. Officially. On the telly. So every fucker out there knows."

Homelander nods his head. "You don't have to touch me."

William lends Homelander some old t-shirt and sweats, kicking his suit into the corner of the living room. He makes him dinner, probably fancier than he was planning to make for himself. Homelander wants to tell him about everything that's led him to come here, because he really does think what they've done with the doctor is the last straw for him and he won't go back to them, no matter what William thinks, but he also doesn't want to relive the day and get agitated again. They eat in almost complete silence, and Homelander is surprised at how good he feels when William says "I can't cook for shit, can you pass the salt, John?", clearly testing his reaction. Homelander breaks out into a wide smile as he gives him the requested saltshaker. Now the name brings back more recent happy memories than his childhood. It reminds him of how much he was caressed and fucked during those couple of months before they parted ways. It makes him hopeful that William won't hold to his word, but when they lie down in bed, he's dismayed to see him roll up an extra blanket into a thin cylinder and divide the mattress in half.

Homelander lies there in the darkness, his back turned to William's half of the bed, hoping he can just fall asleep after a trying day. William is using him too, he has to keep that in mind. He wants him to break ties with Vought to destabilize them. For all Homelander knows, he might not even care about this child, and it's just a good way to drive a wedge between him and Vought. He shouldn’t count on anyone being kind, and he needs to learn to be more stoic and independent and not so reliant on other people's supposed good intentions all the time. But it's too much, too painful—he can hear William breathing, hear his heart pumping, even feel the slight electricity of a body being so close to him. It's just too painful to still be alone.

"William," he whispers. "Please touch me. I can't stand it. Not today."

"Please" he repeats when he hears William's breath hitch but doesn't hear him shift over. "I'm begging you, just a hug. That's all I'm asking for."

William sighs heavily and shifts over. Homelander hears rustling of sheets and blankets, and then William's body is right next to him, putting one arm around his chest and pulling him in closer until his back is pressed up right against the chest behind him and he can feel William breathing near the back of his head.

"Thank you," Homelander tries to say but it comes out as a sob that's barely recognizable as two words. And suddenly the floodgates open, and he's telling William everything that happened that day. He can't see William's face and doesn't want to see it. He needs to break up with Vought but he's terrified to do it.

Chapter End Notes

Named people on Vought’s board of directors were on it in S3. Except Anne who might be my favorite show writer based on the episodes for which she has head writer credits.

Thanks to Poizonsss for astutely pointing out the biggest pregnancy craving HL is going to have is touch starvation.

Chapter 8: Dec 15 &amp; 24, 2022

Dec 15, 2022

Butcher taps on the steering wheel nervously. It's very hard to stay parked near Vought Tower. He's planted himself in front of a hydrant, just behind the little church at the base of the high rise. He's got an unobstructed view of the main entryway, and thinks there's no way he can miss Homelander if the latter comes out wearing his flashy suit. There's a slight possibility he'll come out in a different outfit, Butcher supposes, but he doesn't think he'll miss him in any case. The problem is, he's been staked out here since 11 am, and it's not clear how much longer he might have to wait.

Part of Butcher can't help but wonder if he's naïve to wait and expect Homelander to appear at all. Maybe it's madness to think people at Vought won't just reconvince Homelander that his best bet is to stay with them. It's a sickening parallel, but he can't help thinking about how Becca refused to trust him at the moment of truth—how she chose to stay behind in the compound run by Vought rather than risk running away with him. What is it about him that makes others not trust him and throw their lot in with people that they already have proof positive are not trustworthy? The question has been eating at him ever since Homelander departed. He replayed their last conversation in his mind many times, mulling over what he could have said differently or perhaps not said at all. Ultimately, there was no going around it. He needed America's sweetheart to make a clean break with Vought once and for all, and that was something apparently very difficult to achieve.

Anger wasn't the only emotion Butcher experienced whenever he saw Homelander pop up on the telly, giving an interview here, doing a staged rescue there. There was also a panic that began to mount over time. That was his child growing inside this self-absorbed cunt, and if he didn't do something to get Homelander's head out of his arse soon, Vought would take ownership of his child. Yet some kind of misplaced pride in Butcher just wouldn't allow him to call and try to convince Homelander to switch sides.

 

"Can you believe this cunt is back out in public?" Butcher asked Hughie when the lad came over for an impromptu visit, and they were sitting on the couch watching news coverage of Homelander at a rally taking place in Central Park. His body was obscured while he was standing behind a podium, giving a short speech consisting mostly of bromides, flashing a megawatt smile between every sentence or two. Butcher stared intently when he stepped away, clapping for the next speaker, more of his body visible now. "He look any different to ya? At all?"

Hughie looked at Butcher skeptically. "You mean different from before? Looks about the same as always to me. Guess he finally got over what happened, huh."

"You don't notice anything different?" Butcher asked again. It was possible he was imagining things. Maybe it was subtle, but it was there, the suit's foam abs now slightly stretched, the belt more snug than usual. That was his poor child in there. Why had he let Homelander make it and then take it with him into Vought's open arms?

"You feeling okay?" Hughie asked. "I honestly came over to see how you were doing... you've been acting a bit weird. Is this all because he's back in action?"

"How am I acting weird then." Butcher's reply wasn't really a question, and Hughie looked like he was going to elaborate but only shrugged and shook his head. Butcher knew full well he wasn't in great condition. He was trying to work, but spent a lot of days at home, only nominally doing tasks for the FBSA. He was becoming consumed with watching Homelander's every move and public appearance, and never seemed to sleep well because of nightmares. Some nightmares involved Homelander suddenly perched on top of him in the bed, holding him down with force, grinning like some deranged succubus as he'd roll his hips. So if you're gonna claim Vought didn’t fuck you up all that badly and your childhood was all sunshine and rainbows, then it really is all on you, you selfish fucking monster. And I'm the one who has to live with ya, helping you fulfill this daft dream of bringing another kid into this world just to make you feel better about your life. You care how I feel?” Billy doesn’t pause long enough for any possible response. “Didn’t fucking think so."

Homelander stares for a while. The other man doesn't seem to have anything to add, maybe regretting some of his words.

"I figured we were over that, William..." he finally says.

"Over what? What's that even mean?" Billy lets out an unpleasant sounding mirthless laugh. "I ain't ever gonna be over it."

"I thought we forgave each other for the past."

"And where d'you get that bizarre notion?"

Homelander is frowning deeply. "I don’t know. Maybe when you agreed to have a fucking child with me?"

"Agreed is a strong word," Billy mutters angrily.

"What was that?"

"I'm sure you heard me loud and clear with that superhearing of yours," Billy says, louder now.

"I can hear you but I don't know what the fuck you're saying. You're gonna tell me you didn't agree to have a child, almost six months in?"

"Weren't my idea, was it."

"Oh. Terrific," Homelander says stomping towards the bedroom. "Just terrific. Get the fuck out of this apartment. I don't want to see your face."

"Then close your eyes. It's my apartment," Billy counters, and Homelander can hear the trailing off in his voice because he already realizes what the retort is going to be.

"Yeah, and only you're allowed to leave it, apparently! Because I need to be under home confinement! Because I'm such a menace to society that the FBI needs me to get on my knees and suck their dick just to keep them from pressing charges against me. That’s the amazing life you’ve gifted me, William."

"You are a menace to society though. Plain and simple."

Homelander was about to slam the door to the bedroom to put at least some separation between them but swiftly turns around at those words. "I SHOULD NEVER HAVE FUCKING TESTIFIED FOR YOUR SIDE!” His voice is cracking, but he can’t help it. “I’ve saved more people than you ever will, even if I don’t work another day in my life. Menace to society. Says the guy who straps explosives to women. You think it was so bad for me at Vought? I was allowed to do whatever the hell I wanted! I was allowed to fucking leave my apartment— imagine that!"

"Yeah that lab room sounds like a right laugh. They really let you do whatever you wanted. Someone came crying to my doorstep because they wouldn’t let him have a baby in public but wanted to breed him, but I guess that wasn’t you.”

Homelander shakes his head, jaw tightening painfully. He wishes he could stop the facial twitch he gets when he feels like he has no control over a situation.

Billy doesn’t let up. “You’d like the taste of the FBI's dick better if you took Vought's out of your mouth first, you know."

"Nobody at Vought would dare talk to me the way you’re doing."

"Well that’s likely 'cause their job description was to suck up to you and make you think your sad life was bearable. So you’d keep working your arse off for them."

"Or maybe it was because they knew their place and that I could fucking laser them in half if they got annoying."

"Nothing stopping you now either," Billy mutters under his breath.

"Don't you fucking—" Homelander presses his lips together, angry that the heart of the man in front of him didn't skip a beat saying it. "DON'T YOU FUCKING TEMPT ME!" Homelander suddenly feels a stabbing sort of pain and doubles over.

"Stop your yelling, we got neighbors," Billy says, but his face changes from that infuriating nonchalant expression to worry. "What's the matter with you?"

"Nothing." Homelander wheezes as he feels it again, on his knees now, clutching at his stomach. "I don't know. Something really hurts," he adds, looking down at himself, peering through the stretched out skin of his belly.

"She laserin' you or something?" Billy asks, tone completely changing, already at Homelander’s side, helping him up to his feet, bringing him over to the bed.

"No... feels like...." Homelander gasps again at another bout of stabbing pain as he sits down on the edge of the bed, and this time they both see a deformation in his skin. He can't finish his sentence, feeling like the air was kicked out of his lungs.

"Bloody 'ell, you ain't going into labor, are you?" Billy asks and now Homelander finally hears his heart thumping a mile a minute.

"No... she's just.... she’s just trying to move around. Fast." Homelander gasps again, looking inside himself. "She's ..." he lets out a teary laugh. "I think she worked out how to fly. But there's no room in there."

Homelander lies back on the bed, sighing, hissing every time the baby makes an assault on one of his organs. Billy;s face is still contorted with fear as he watches the dramatic belly deformations. "Lena, love, you better stop that," he says, pressing his hand down against the taut swell of Homelander's body. "You're hurtin' your dad."

"Let her do what she wants. She's amazing. Agh, fuck," Homelander curses as he feels another stab, twists his body to lie on his side, breaking out in a sweat from the pain. But he laughs again at the one pleasant development this entire day. "I didn't learn to fly until I was six. This is still only the second trimester. She's a prodigy."

"She's hurtin' you though," Billy says, brows still furrowed.

"I'll be fine," Homelander exhales, massaging his stomach. "Those new organs are just sensitive."

Billy lies down in the bed facing him. The baby eventually quiets down and stops practicing her new skill. The two of them lie in awkward silence, both clearly thinking back to the argument before, and afraid to say something and rekindle it. "How did you learn to fly, then?" he finally ventures to ask.

Homelander sighs. "They put me in a room with an electric-wired metal floor that would give me shocks. There was nowhere I could escape to except lift up in the air, and eventually I did. Guess I could have told them that story today."

Billy looks thoughtful. "You think I worked you up so much that she wanted out? To bail early?"

Homelander smiles. "That would actually make your bitching at me worth it, if that's the case."

"No, that's rank. I ain't doing that again if it's gettin' her stressed."

"Well she stopped, at least for now," Homelander says as he goes back out into the living room and comes back with the giant stack of paper and the bowl of cereal he was attempting to eat earlier. He puts the stack on his side of the bed, and walks around, cradling the cereal bowl while eating out of it. He’s starving if he’s honest with himself. They took one twenty minute recess for a sad club sandwich lunch in the lawyer’s office those entire eight hours, and they had a commute on either side. He’s gotten used to be able to graze throughout the day while sitting at home.

He notices that Billy is watching him intently as he paces around the room idly looking out the windows as he eats. “What?”

“You really didn’t mind it,” Billy mutters quietly. He still seems a little shell-shocked after the baby decided to make her presence known. “You were grinning through the pain like a maniac.”

“I’m proud of her!”

“Reckon Ryan wasn’t like that,” Billy says, still lost in contemplation. “Don't think that’s something Becca could have survived.”

Homelander shrugs. “Ryan didn’t have developed powers even when I met him. Maybe she’s being bathed in more Compound V from growing inside me.”

“Yeah, that, or she’s got two violent angry bastards for parents.” Billy’s face is pretty sour as he says it. He notices Homelander has walked back toward the bed, eyeing the tall stack of paper.

"You don't have to read all that if you don't want to," Billy mumbles. "It’s fine. They got it all on video if there’s any question about what you said. You gave 'em enough incriminating things about Vought. They don't really have a leg to stand on when it comes to your case. The fact you're listed as ‘John Doe’ already says loads about how they’ve treated you."

"The news was saying they're planning to sue me for breaking my contract early,” Homelander says through a mouthful of cereal, gesticulating with the spoon. “And for making money online using fame I got with my old name or whathaveyou."

"Your contract means nothing, since they never bothered to make you into someone who can sign a binding agreement. And as for your social media-- how much can they even sue for? How much money could you have made in the last month--"

"About forty thousand dollars."

"... Right. Well. That's- that's more money than I thought but there's no way it's worth it for them to sue you in the midst of a criminal investigation. Don't worry about it."

"Wasn't planning to worry about it," Homelander says, shrugging, finishing up the bowl of cereal and tilting it to drink the leftover milk at the bottom.

"Seriously? Forty grand? How many posts did you put up then?"

"Not that many. Most of the money came from kickbacks from advertising maternitywear brands with selfies and helping shill some super organic prenatal vitamins on Instagram. I actually have more sponsorships in place, so it should be more this month."

Billy whistles in disbelief. “The navy blue number from today?”

“Yeah, that suit came free from BusinessBump. Did you like it?”

“Looked pretty sharp I suppose.”

“Yeah people online liked it too. Gimmicky brandname, but I think it fit well and didn’t dig in anywhere and wasn’t too femme. Now Pea In a Pod want to do a whole collection based on me, but I told them to hurry up and give me prototypes if they want me to model it for them— the pregnancy will be over before they design the ready-to-wear line. The color swatch they ran by me was blue, red, white, gold, and I warned them they might run into license trouble with Vought over that… ”

Homelander trails off when he realizes he’s rambling about something Billy probably doesn’t give a flying fuck about, even though he looks like he’s listening, watching him pretty intently with an unreadable expression on his face. Homelander lies down on his side of the mattress, and starts to leaf through the double spaced monotype pages.

"Seriously, you don't need to read it. I'm sure it's fine as is," Billy says, trying to reach over and take the stack away, but Homelander blocks him with his shoulder.

"I'll skim it. See how stupid I sounded and what got you so riled up."

Q. Could you specify where you remember spending your childhood?

A. I was raised in a lab facility from at least age 2 through 18.

Q. So your entire childhood was spent in a laboratory?

Q. How do you establish you were there at age 2?

A. I remember the staff celebrating my birthday with three candles on the cake. My memories get clearer at age 4, but I have some memories back to age 2. 

Q. Were you kept in one lab facility or a series of several?

A. It was one lab facility.

Q. Please describe this facility.

A. Most of my time I spent in one room. The walls were reinforced and lined with zinc. That was to prevent me from seeing through the wall. There was a door with a glass window, where people could come and go. I had a bed, a desk, a chair, and, uh, there was a toilet, a sink.

Q. Where was the lab facility, if you can recall?

A. I had no idea at the time, but it was in Cold Spring Harbor. I only learned that later.

Q. How large was the room?

A. It wasn't very big. Maybe something like 15 x 15. Maybe a bit more. I can't say for sure.

Q. Feet? 

A. Yeah, like 200, 250 square feet.

Q. Did you ever express the desire to leave the room?

A. I don't remember.
