"See? I never said 'I never felt deprived of anything'," Homelander says as he brings a page up over his shoulder for Billy to see. He taps the relevant lines with his finger.

"Yeah, I misremembered." Billy's breath skims across the back of his neck as they spoon in bed while he reviews the text. "It's fine. Maybe better this way. No one's going to accuse us of coachin' ya, at least."

Homelander shrugs and rolls his eyes. "I'll do a second deposition, if you really want me to. I can give them some gruesome details about my childhood that we didn't get into."

"Might just take you up on that offer," Billy mumbles, one hand rubbing circles over the baby bump.

"Hey, William...?" Homelander asks, letting the words hang in the air.

"Yeah." Homelander can tell Billy’s voice is also tense. They know each other well enough by now to know Homelander is about to say something heavy.

"You want to, maybe, formally agree to have a child with me, out loud? So we don't have to have that particular conversation again?"

He feels Billy take a deep breath against the nape of his neck before saying "Yeah, I agree."

"No, not like that. I want to hear you say it. Were you serious when you said it wasn’t your choice?"

"Nah. Heat of the moment. Forget it."

"You can't say shit that involves her, even in the heat of the moment."

Homelander feels Billy keep breathing on his skin, but give no answer. "It’s one thing if you’re humoring me because I’m your golden ticket to taking Vought down. I’ll live with that. But are you going along with this because you're fucking pitying me?"

There’s a long pause, and Homelander begins to regret asking, dreading the answer.

Billy sighs. "It's definitely a piece of it."

"Well I don't want your fucking pity, William. Yours or anyone else's. Fuck." Homelander pushes the other man's hand off his body.

Billy returns his hand right back to where it was resting before and takes another deep breath before speaking. "You know what I pity in you? It's that you'll never fully comprehend just how much those cunts messed with your head," he says quietly. "The only way I can forgive—nah, forgive ain't even the right word here. Overlook. Overlook what you done to me Becca, and overlook what happened between me and you that made us lose Ryan, and overlook how you went about ‘asking’ for my help to have a child. The only way I can look past all that is if I consider what you really are.”

“And what’s that. What am I, ‘really’,” Homelander asks, but there’s no questioning in his tone. He doesn’t want to hear this. This is touching a nerve he’d forgotten he had.

“You’re a sad abused lab specimen. They raised you in some fucked up isolation, tortured you so you’d develop your powers, and then told you those powers make you better than everyone else on earth. Told you your most important task was to be liked by everyone, but at the same time that none of that ‘everyone’ matters. So given all that, Johnny, I for one think it's a bloody miracle we can even have a civil conversation at all. For all that, I can count you as a … let’s call it a victim of circumstance. Instead of the warped person they grew you into."

Homelander stares off toward the wall as he listens, irritation rising and falling in waves, but he’s sick of arguing. Maybe he should just let Billy call him a victim. Just let him sit on his high horse with his patronizing tone, thinking he's the only one who really understands what's going on with Vought.

“You ever notice you talk about me like I’m some sort of exotic pet? Like I’m dangerous, high maintenance, but mentally just beneath you? Is that why I need to stay in a box? Just a fucking product you can keep on a shelf? You and Vought aren’t as different as you think. You think I’m that stupid? That I don’t understand that they abused me? I’m not more stupid about Vought than anyone else in this society.”

“You are stupid about Vought. But nah, you ain't mentally beneath me. Your mind works differently, though, don’t ya think?”

“I don’t know what you mean.” Homelander grinds his teeth, because deep down he knows what Billy’s referring to. There is some kind of coldness in him, a value system no one else seems to like— not even the people who raised him!— and he doesn’t know where it originates from, but everyone recoils from him once they see it. He doesn’t like to think about it, he feels broken because it’s something he doesn’t seem to be able to change, and he’s dismayed that Billy seems so keenly aware of it. Is he really unable to pass for a normal human, emotionally? Homelander shakes his head in dismay.

"Are you upset that our baby has powers already?"

"We expected she would, didn't we?” Billy says.

“Do you expect-” Homelander wants to ask, but none of the questions end up said out loud. Do you expect her to have the same coldness as me? Are you still going to love her if she’s the same? 

“I was just getting nervous she’d bust out of ya, all preterm little alien creature." Billy’s tone is playful, not really aware of how much pain his earlier words are still stirring up.

"Don't call her that."

"I looked up some illustrations of what these fetuses look like before the third trimester. Just wanted to know what you're admiring in there. Humans are right weird looking when they're that small."

"She looks much better than any of those illustrations." Homelander sniffs in disdain. "Yeah, she's not ready for the outside world yet. She’s still cute."

"I just hope she don't work out how to use her lasers before the due date. For your sake."

"I don't care. If she wants to laser me, let her."

"You ain’t at all worried she'll make your water break or something? Accidentally boil herself inside you?"

Homelander shrugs, admittedly not having considered that possibility. No child of his would ever do something self-destructive, he assumes. He puts the stack of transcript on the floor and turns over to face Billy. “Can you hold me?”

Billy obliges, pulling Homelander’s body in until the bump presses up against him, and moving his palm over his shoulder blades and tracing his spine. Homelander sighs and closes his eyes, arching into the touch. The tears he held back just a little earlier suddenly breach containment.

“What’s wrong?” Billy mumbles into his hair, still stroking his back.

“Nothing, just tired after this whole day.” It’s a white lie. There’s definitely something wrong, but he hopes this feeling will pass by morning. The feeling that he’s utterly alone because even the person closest to him doesn’t seem to think of him as fully human. He’s defective in some way that he himself is blind to, everyone keeps noticing something off about him, and yet no one will articulate what it is that they find so off-putting. Part of him wants Lena to be just like him— to understand him completely and be a little bit disconnected from this world teeming with mudpeople, with their mediocrity and their judgements. And yet, he wants the best life for her. He doesn’t want her to feel this lonely and not understood by anyone except him— not if he can help it.

Billy’s hand slows down right as he falls asleep, breathing and heartrate slowing down with it, but Homelander remains wide awake, idly honing in on random conversations taking place among the people who are still up throughout the neighboring apartments. It's soothing, but not enough to lull him to sleep. The baby stirs and he looks down and watches her, gulping down whatever fluid she's floating in, and then sucking on her thumb while stretching her legs out. Are you going to be strange? he wonders. Liked by everyone, loved by no one except me? Will Billy love you if you turn out like me? He detests that this matters to him.

~~~

John’s eyes dart over to look at Vogelbaum over the shoulder of the lab tech who’s directing the flow of the cement mixture down his throat. John’s eyes are full of tears, gag reflex acting up because the mixture is so bitter, thick and slow to descend. The sludge is settling inside him— he feels like it’s clogging up everything.

“That’s enough for now,” Vogelbaum finally instructs, and they stop the flow. John squirms in discomfort, taking a deep breath after the many minutes of holding it.

“How does it feel?” Vogelbaum asks.

“It hurts,” John says cautiously, knowing they’re not going to be happy with that answer.

“Yes, I can imagine, but how does it feel? Can you figure out if your body is doing anything?”

John thinks for a moment, even though the pain is starting to become overwhelming enough that it’s hard to string words together. “It feels like… it’s turning rock hard inside me, and pulling everything together like glue.”

“Alright,” Vogelbaum says, accepting the answer as informative enough.

John looks down at himself, through himself, frightened to see how much concrete is actually inside him, twisting all his organs as it sets. There’s so much pain. He’s more sensitive on the inside than on the outside, and that’s the sensitivity the team is apparently trying to train him out of.

He looks up at Vogelbaum, and knows he’s not allowed to verbally complain about how much it hurts, because it makes the staff uncomfortable. Vogelbaum’s eyes are thoughtful, maybe even sympathetic. “Let’s just give it a little bit of time. See if your body can deal with it,” he says, almost kindly.

They sit and wait, the clock on the wall ticks, and some doctors are standing by in case they’re needed, but for now just taking notes on clipboards.

“I don’t know if I can get rid of it,” John tries to say, but his speech starts out as a barely intelligible sob.

“John, you’re twelve years old, you’re far too old to be crying. If you can’t get rid of it, we’ll give you something to drink to dissolve it. But then we’d have to note it down as a weakness, wouldn’t we. Another thing some enemy of the US could exploit. Can you wait just a little bit longer before we give up?”

John nods, sniffing back his tears, trying to will his body to crush or digest or do something he can’t even think of to get the concrete out of his system. His body clearly senses there’s something wrong, his heart is beating fast, and he feels every tissue that’s cemented together trying to separate away. The pain is starting to become excruciating, as if someone is stabbing him repeatedly in multiple places. John stays silent, and holds as stoic a facial expression as he can muster. Time goes by slowly, the other doctors seem to get antsy, and Vogelbaum sighs and asks if he’d like to chug some acid to help break the concrete up. But John shakes his head, determined not to give up and pass this test, visualizing his body successfully breaking the concrete down into dry dust. His intestines twist and turn with agonizing efforts to do just that, pulverize the substance clogging them and the pain is next-level, but John leans into it this time. Don’t be scared of the pain, he repeats in his head, pain means your body’s learning a new trick. It’s a mantra drilled into him since before he can remember.

Homelander stirs awake from the vivid dream, so vivid that the pain in his stomach still seems all too real. It’s then that he realizes the pain is not part of the dream.

He gets up and paces in the living room, trying not to disturb his bedmate, saying “shh, shh, shh” as if he’s soothing a baby who’s already born. He breathes deeply through his nose to avoid crying at every incredibly forceful movement she makes. “Baby… please. It’s the middle of the night,” he whispers. Pacing around and rocking himself seems to calm her down but she still tries to phase through him at what feels like supersonic speed once in a while.

He sits down and browses idly on his phone. If Billy can’t even admit to wanting a child together, let alone loving him, at least the internet connects him with an enthusiastic fanbase that is generous with their love in the form of likes, retweets and thumbs up. Homelander sinks into the comfortable glow, checking on the comments he’s getting. He was never a whiz with social media, but he’s doing okay by his own estimation. Vought’s handwringing about what a pregnancy announcement might do to his ratings seems off the mark. His fanbase hasn’t seismically shifted. If anything, he’s gotten wider female and Gen Z followings. There’s been no sniping with Vought, and he’s kept it civil by never going into the reasons for the rift, even though people speculate and ask all the time. He’s managed to rise into the top tier of Instagram moms with only a few baby bump selfies, none of which were particularly revealing or lewd. He sits down in front of the tower of cardboard boxes he’s stacked against the wall and holds his phone at arm’s length, to snap a couple of selfies in front of them. He makes sure the logo of the moving company as well as the maternity wear he’s wearing today is adequately highlighted.

‘Ready for the big move.’  he captions, then pauses, mulling over whether he should add one of the tired emojis. People get tired packing right? Complaining about packing makes you relatable right? It’s his first time doing something like this, and he isn’t tired physically, but he has to admit there was something mentally fatiguing about putting everything away while minimizing space and maximizing organization.

He decides not to put anything negative into a sponsored post and opts for a safe exclamation point emoji to express excitement. Is he really excited about this move? He’s gotten strangely attached to this particular apartment, in all its shabby glory. Although it was only minutes’ flight from Vought Tower, it felt like a different world living here.

Homelander’s not even sure if he’s just read about nesting instinct enough that he’s willed himself to feel it, or if he genuinely feels a pull to get a crib, mobiles, toys, and things to plaster up the walls. But Billy told him pointblank that they need to move to a two bedroom, preferably away from prying eyes, if he’s going to do babyshopping. Homelander found a nice apartment opening up in April in an upscale high rise on the Upper West Side, six times the rent they were paying now. Billy raised his eyebrows but didn’t protest it—just asked if he was sure he didn’t want to move out somewhere with an actual front yard, instead of facing into Central Park.

Homelander flips on the TV but quickly turns it off again. Every news channel has been talking about the government’s investigation into Vought since it was made public a few days ago, when they formally subpoenaed Vought for a copy of all records kept going back decades. Homelander’s defection from Vought suddenly became part of a bigger picture and he had to turn down invitations for interviews with the New York Times and Wall Street Journal to avoid discussing the investigation. There’s likely nothing being discussed on TV that he hasn’t heard about. Billy’s still heavily involved with the FBI’s efforts to gather and sift through the evidence, so Homelander figures he’ll be privy to any interesting new developments before anyone else.

He still feels that old feeling of unease bubble up at the mere thought of the hearings—are they really going to make him testify before Congress, how many days is he expected to be in DC, will they schedule them after he already has his baby, is he going to have to be away from Lena just to give this stupid testimony, is he going to have to incriminate himself,... He realizes he needs to stop thinking about it when he feels Lena stir inside him.

He settles himself on the floor cross-legged, plugging his ankle monitor to charge while he’s at it so it stops the annoying blinking warning light. He fires up a guided meditation on his laptop, follows the video’s instructions to close his eyes, tries to do whatever it is they mean when they say “ground your breath”. He inhales and exhales, and follows the guidance to withdraw his senses. He never knows if he’s doing it right, but at the very least he tries to ignore the sounds he can hear everywhere around him. In some ways, he’s had to learn to do this sort of ‘withdrawal’ at a very early age. Not to partially ignore some of his senses would have driven him mad and made him unable to focus on anything at hand. He sighs deeply and focuses even further inward, listening to his breath, listening to his blood pump through his body, even though the video doesn’t instruct to do so, and smiles when he hears Lena’s small heart beat about twice as fast deep inside him. His even breath hitches when he feels her little elbow gliding along his inner wall as she turns. He’s not sure if it’s these meditations  helping, or maybe Billy has been extra careful to not say anything upsetting, but he’s been able to maintain his calm and Lena hasn’t done her sharp flying attempts in a while.

His phone vibrates against the floor, and all the withdrawal of the senses is instantly undone. Homelander reaches over to see the message, knowing it’s from Billy.

told you to leave the packing alone. ill come home and get it done.

Homelander smiles. Billy must have not only downloaded the Instagram app but turned on notifications for his account, it seems. He flips over to his latest post and sees there are already many comments, the majority asking him where he’s moving to, some speculating he’s moving into the suburbs, others wondering if he’s moving to DC for the upcoming investigation. He replies to a couple of innocuous questions, confirming he’s not moving outside of the city, and specifying they’re moving into a 2 bedroom to have a nursery. A few crumbs like that and the post will keep getting more comments hoping to be answered, and Perfect Moving and Pea in a Pod will be happy their sponsored post is getting engagement

I have time to kill, Homelander texts back. When are you coming back?

soon as i can. got some news i think youll like.

Homelander’s heart skips a beat. He dares not hope, but he knows Billy’s been petitioning to end his home detention, among a lot of other things that have been put into motion now that the investigation of Vought has become official.

Oh? He texts back, knowing Billy probably won’t elaborate over text.

Homelander puts the phone down towards his chest and catches himself grinning like an idiot. Billy won’t ever say the words he would most like to hear, he knows that, but seeing the endearment written out as actual text makes his heart speed up just a tad.

When Billy finally comes in through the door, Homelander is in the midst of his prenatal yoga routine. He tried it as part of all the new agey earthy-crunchy methods of calming down, but truth be told he only does it when Billy’s around to see it and today is no different—he can easily pick out the distinct sound of Billy’s car when he’s still blocks away, and arranged himself to face away from the door for maximum impact.

“Well there’s a sight for sore eyes.” Billy chuckles as he closes the door behind him, watching Homelander move through the cow-cat pose motions.

Homelander sits back on his heels and looks over his shoulder. “So what’s the news?” he asks, sounding impatient in spite of himself, especially when he sees a bottle of Martinelli’s sparkling apple cider in one of Billy’s hands.

“Mostly good news,” Billy says, walking into the kitchen area and getting out two whiskey glasses from the cupboard.

“Mostly?”

“I’ll start with the good.” Billy opens the briefcase he’s started to carry around to his dayjob, and hands over a sheet of paper.

Homelander already knew what it was, but still can’t suppress a yelp when he sees the words ‘lift’ and ‘cessation of electronic monitoring’ with a retroactive date of the day before.

“Fucking finally,” he mutters as he throws his arms around Billy’s neck, but almost unbalances him with the attack.

Billy hugs him tight, stroking his hair. “So you’re free to go now. If you don’t wanna stay.”

Homelander leans back for a moment, shaking his head at the stupidity of the joke, then presses himself back into the embrace.

Billy pours out the cider after he unlocks and deactivates the ankle monitor.

“Most people probably have champagne flutes for this kind of thing,” Homelander comments idly after they clink the thick whiskey glasses.

Billy narrows his eyes before turning his gaze away. “Most people probably got more occasions to celebrate than I had the last decade,” he mutters as he downs the entire glass, and Homelander instantly regrets saying anything.

“We’ll get some for the new apartment,” he offers quietly, voice shaky, upset that he’s ruined the moment.

“It’s fine, I’m just fucking with ya.” Billy chuckles but his face changes when he looks back at Homelander. “Oi... I was kidding.”

Homelander realizes with a measure of horror that there’s tears in his eyes and starts wiping them away violently. “Just hormones.” His voice is all sorts of raspy and sad-sounding. “Fuck.”

“Oi... seriously I didn’t mean nothing by it,” Billy says, approaching him again and picking up his chin even though Homelander is trying his utmost to stare at the floor. “Johnny... come on now.”

Homelander’s mortified that it’s that easy for Billy to bring him down and feel low and a new flood of tears comes on.

“Johnny,” Billy’s tone has turned to pleading and he pulls him until they’re both sitting on the couch. Billy runs his hand through his hair, scratching the back of his head at the undercut. “Seriously now. I don’t hold it against ya. Not anymore anyway.”

Homelander sniffles, stifling a sob. “I’m fine. Just give me the bad news already.” He dips his head down to sip more apple cider. In all honesty, he doesn’t actually like the way sparkling beverages tingle across his mouth, but he’s not about to make a stupid ungrateful comment again.

“Well,” Billy says, taking his free hand and rubbing his thumb against his palm. Homelander takes some pleasure in idly noticing that Billy’s worn his fancy watch ever since Christmas. “I think this is still good news from your perspective. People did manage to scrounge up your actual birthdate.”

Homelander’s breath hitches. “Did they find documents about who my mother was? Was she a surrogate?”

“They might stumble on it eventually, if Vought didn’t shred all the juicy evidence. It’s a bleedin' mountain of papers they’re still digging through. They’re digitizing a lot of the older stuff from the 80s over at Quantico, but it’s slow goin'. But no, not much about the circumstances. Just the date so far.”

Homelander has a strange mixture of emotions, as if part of him is afraid to know more about his past, and terrified that other people are sifting through information he might not know about himself. But he’s also suddenly very curious to know. “So what is it?”

“May 25th.”

Homelander sits there digesting. It’s just a date, it shouldn’t change anything about his self-image or reveal any grand truth. But somehow knowing the real date makes him feel emotional. “1981?”

“Yeah, they weren't lying about your age. My question is, why’d they move it to fucking February 22nd in the first place?”

“Slow season for TV,” Homelander mutters. “They wanted some tie in with President’s Day. I don’t know.”

“Isn’t Memorial Day right around your real birthday?”

“Probably didn’t want that because everyone’s off barbecuing and no one sits around at home on Memorial Day,” Homelander says, although he’s staring off into the distance.

Billy gives a short incredulous laugh. “So you want something for your birthday, then? Seeing as it’s the first proper one you’re going to celebrate?”

“Maybe some actual champagne flutes,” Homelander says and then alleviates the tension he sees on Billy’s face by grinning. “Actually... Lena’s due in June. Maybe just have the baby shower on my real birthday. That’ll make me happy.”

“Hang about—you want a baby shower?”

Homelander tilts his chin up. “Yes. Why not?”

“That might be the most American thing about you. Who're you planning on inviting even?”

Homelander purses his lips. “I don’t know. I could always announce it online and get a bunch of strangers to show up. But I’d rather it be people you and I know.”

He sees Billy start to sweat just a tiny bit. “I don’t—I barely know anyone.”

Homelander sighs. “Don’t you have your friends... your Boys or whatever you call them?”

“You want my mates to show up to your baby shower?”

Homelander rolls his eyes. “It’s your baby too, you know. Or are you still ashamed of this whole thing.” He knows full well he’s putting Billy in a tough spot, but he wants it, he wants to push it, he wants full integration of Billy’s separate lives that he’s trying to lead right now.

“Alright. Alright, let’s say I invite mine. Who the hell are you inviting?”

“Nobody, probably. I’ve got a faceless sea of followers on social media and not a single actual person I’m close to that I’d want there. So no one. Not like anyone from Vought is gonna pay me a visit right now.”

Billy stares at him, looking almost comically bemused. “So let me get this straight. You want to celebrate your birthday, and your baby shower, with my circle of friends. People you hardly know.”

“I know Starlight plenty well enough,” Homelander says dismissively.

“Okay...” Billy nods his head, still looking lost in thought and uneasy. “Okay... I’ll see what I can do, if that’s what you really want.”

They sit in silence for a beat.

“I assume that wasn’t the bad news?” Homelander finally asks.

Billy snaps out of his train of thought. “Nah. The bad news is Vought put in a formal request to get their suit back.”

Homelander’s laugh is one of relief that that’s all it is. “Fuck them. I haven’t worn that thing since I took it off. I had ten of them hanging up in my closet in my apartment, and they need the one I have?”

“They said it’s got proprietary tech inside it and that you don’t have ownership of it.” Billy shrugs.

Homelander looks down at his hands. “I kind of want to keep it. For old times’ sake, nothing else.”

“I actually agree with you there,” Billy says, chuckling. “I asked how much they wanted for it, and they came back with 800 grand, which was a bit too rich for my blood, but maybe you feel different. Didn’t realize you were waltzing around in a fucking Bugatti.”

“A little rich for mine too,” Homelander replies, sighing. “I just wanted to see if I could fit back into the thing after this is over.”

“Not because I wanna go back to Vought or anything,” he adds hurriedly when he sees Billy smirk.

“You really think you can’t squeeze into the thing right now? I bet you can still pull it on just fine. The front bit probably won’t close anymore, but you’re talking like you've doubled in size or something.”

“I don’t think you understand how form-fitting it is. It’s like a hard shell.”

“Where is it? You already packed it away?”

“Yeah, but I can find it,” Homelander says, shrugging. “You want me to dig it out and show you you’re wrong?”

Billy laughs. “Sure. Gotta return it anyway. Also, cheers for doing my packing for me. But can I ask you to be a dear and label the boxes since I can’t see through them?”

“Yeah, I’ll do it later.” Homelander stands up, surveying the boxes until he sees the one with his suit folded up neatly, and the one that contains the red boots. He pulls out the boxes and tears off the tape. His heart starts racing as he pulls out the cape he carefully folded up, and then the suit itself. It’s been months since he’s put it on, and even though it’s something he’s worn every day for two decades it still feels foreign in his hands now. “I don’t have the belt on,” Homelander retorts but he can’t suppress a smile. He walks over to the mirror in the bedroom to see what it looks like on him in this state, and he sighs wistfully at the familiar but distant sensation of the cape billowing out behind him as he moves.

“Does it feel good to put it on?” Billy asks as he follows him into the other room, standing in the doorway.

“Sorry,” Billy rasps near his ear, leaning over him. “Lost me head for a bit.”

 “I didn’t put this on so you could get violent with your fantasies,” Homelander grumbles.

When Homelander exits the building on Billy’s arm it doesn’t take half a minute for someone on the street to do a double take and take a picture, even though it’s dark out, and even though Homelander is dressed in entirely civilian clothing, probably a bit too nicely dressed for where they’re going, frankly. Homelander smiles broadly. “Of course.” He catches the cashier throw a quick glance at the middle of his body when he comes up from around the counter, and there’s a huge swell of pride in his chest. He missed this, certainly. Social media just never lives up to real interactions with fans. When he and Billy come out together, the flashbulbs start going off like crazy. People are looking at the street out of their windows, cars are stopping to stare at the procession. New York is usually calmer about celebrities going about their lives, but Homelander has never gone out casually in public much, and nowadays, with all the media swirl about Vought, it's inevitable that people will be all agog.

Homelander looks over at Billy who looks none too happy to be surrounded by all this. Homelander has to remember that he’s not used to it. What feels like home to him feels alien to most people. Chapter 13: April 14, 2023

Coming out of the hair salon, Homelander feels renewed. Roots retouched, undercut shorter, crisper, his hair side parted for that softer look he prefers right now. He’s greeted by a small mob gathered on the sidewalk, summoned by social media posts with hazy, murky pictures of him sitting with foils in his hair taken through the glass of the salon. He saw them popping up under the #Homelander tag while waiting for the bleach to work, and encouraged them by acknowledging and waving to them occasionally. The picture snapping gets even more frenzied now that he’s come outside, black nylon cape no longer obscuring his 7-months-along belly.

Homelander smiles amiably and promises he’ll sign a few autographs, but gets annoyed as everyone jostles in towards him, eager to be part of the lucky ones he signs for. He crosses his arms protectively over his belly. “Please stay back. I’ll only sign for people who don’t touch me.”

People veer backwards, trying to give him the space he’s asking for, despite people in the back still shoving everyone else forwards.

“You look fantastic!” some female voice yells from the crowd.

“Well thank you!” Homelander says loudly back in the general direction of the voice, beaming as he continues signing what’s mostly still Vought memorabilia being thrust in front of him. A lot of these people came prepared. The Homelander merchandise was now all limited edition and was skyrocketing in value. He doesn’t care if some of these people are probably autograph hounds looking to resell items on eBay—everyone seems genuinely enthusiastic to see him at least. After cloistering himself away in grief, then being forced to stay inside one apartment for months, he’s missed adoration from a crowd more than he realized, and can’t get enough.

“Are you going back to work as a superhero at some point?”

“TBD,” he replies, even though he’s not sure whether being a professional superhero outside of the auspices of Vought is a thing that can be done. He’s certainly not going back—not unless something really takes a turn. Not unless Vought gets out from the trial unscathed, and Lena manages to accidentally kill Billy, and he has no one to turn to, and has to come crawling back to his old handlers and give Lena up to them because it turns out he can’t raise her by himself... he cuts off that train of thought, grimacing before smiling harder.

“Will Vought still let you inject your baby with Compound V?”

“I don’t have any ongoing relationship with Vought and I don’t need anything from them.” He stops just short of saying anything else and smiles when he hears someone else in the crowd yell ‘the baby’s already super!’, the tone sounding annoyed that not everyone has been keeping up with his Instagram.

 “Is Vought going to get broken up by the government?”

“Can’t comment,” he says with a quick nervous chuckle, which makes it sound like he knows the answer to that question, but better safe than sorry. He’s still not sure he can really imagine Vought not existing.

“Is Vought suing you?”

“No questions about Vought, sorry. I’m no longer with them, that’s all I can tell you.”

“Have you picked a name yet?”

“Yes but not sharing until the baby’s born,” he says, smiling amiably in the direction of the young woman who asked.

“Sorry, I actually meant for yourself?”

He can feel his smile falter. “Oh that’s just a common misconception. I’ve always had a name,” he says, surprised that he bristles now at the suggestion that he never had one, even though he’s wanted nothing to do with it all these years. “It’s John.”

He’s relieved they don’t press for a last name, even though that would be the logical followup question. Another woman thrusts her half-dressed infant towards him, asking him to sign the diaper, and he takes that as a cue to end this fan encounter. “That’ll be it for today,” he announces before gently lifting off into the air to disappointed sighs.

He’s feeling on top of the world and decides act on it, flying up beyond most of the rooftops and perching on the edge of Central Park Tower’s roof. It’s a building that’s gone up so recently that he never bothered to land on it before. It’s got a very nice view for miles and miles in every direction out from Manhattan Island. If he looks down, he sees Central Park laid out in a neat rectangle beneath him, the trees just beginning to grow their leaves back. He takes his phone out, lies down on the edge, and gets a selfie managing to fit both his maternity shirt and the dizzying view of the hundred story drop below him to the street into the frame. He’s gotten adept at these Instagram ads.

He sits up again, letting his legs dangle off the side of the building while he composes the text to the post. Once he’s done he stares at the streets far away below, at his white Vans slipons that he’s taken a real liking to ever since it got harder to lean down and pull shoes on or tie laces, and at his shirt pulled taut over his baby bump. He’s carrying high, so the belly just barely touches his thighs when he’s seated. He watches people milling about below, some jogging along the main path in the park, jaywalking between the sluggish traffic on the roads around it. He turns to face the other way, taking special care to avoid looking into Vought Tower, gazes beyond, scanning to see if he can espy Billy, really testing his range for penetrating vision. Not in the Flatiron building. He looks even further south, and has to squint and strain but doesn’t see him all the way in FBI headquarters either. That’s where Billy usually spends his days now—there seems to be a lot of evidence gathering to wrap up as they gear up for the public investigation, even though there’s still no date set. Homelander resists the urge to scan wider until he finds him. He’ll give Billy his privacy. He has a surprising amount of trust in him, and he’s sure Billy is out and about doing something related to the investigation. Homelander also resists the urge to listen in on conversations in Vought Tower which is much closer and requires hardly any effort. He’s asked Billy if he and the FBI want the inside scoop on what’s being discussed in the executive team offices, but Billy flatly refused, saying it might compromise their case if they used any intel gathered that way.

She’s pressing her face right up against his inner wall, and he has to laugh because he swears it looks like she’s studying the outside world from inside her bubble. “See something interesting out there?” he says, chuckling, but startles when Lena shifts in response to his voice. He has the uncanny sensation of being watched—like she’s staring straight at him through the veils of amniotic fluid, tissue, and skin.

Homelander has the odd sensation of his shirt sticking to his back, and realizes he’s broken out in a cold sweat. By human standards it might be chilly and windy where he’s sitting, but it doesn’t register as uncomfortable and sweating isn’t something his body ever does to regulate his temperature anyway. It happens when his nerves are frayed—or he’s close to orgasm. What is he so nervous about?

Lena seems to lose interest now that he’s silent and turns back to viewing everything around them.

“Maybe we won’t tell your other daddy about this just yet. He might get weirded out,” Homelander says to her, conspiratorially, as if she can understand him, mostly thinking out loud. Ever since her flying in confinement got her tangled in her own umbilical cord, Homelander has gotten more wary of anything out of the ordinary about his pregnancy, and found himself actually hoping the rest of her powers would wait to manifest until after birth. He pets his own belly. “You like this view, huh?” He looks over the rooftops, over the river and ocean stretching out below, the afternoon sun casting everything beneath him in a warm yellow glow, and the oceanwater looking crystal blue, except for a few white waves, looking like small stripes near the shores from this height. “I always loved this kind of view too.”

Homelander’s penetrative vision didn’t develop until much later in childhood, and he never expected hers to manifest before birth. He distinctly remembers the experiment where he first harnessed it. They locked him into a metal safe, which was airtight and allowed absolutely no light in, and no room to stand up or stretch any limbs. His eyes were supernaturally sensitive, so he could always see well even in very low light settings—certainly better than any of the scientists testing him. But that was the first time in his life that he was plunged into complete darkness and no amount of opening his eyes wide or blinking improved anything. He didn’t start panicking right away. The scientists were conversing with him calmly, telling him to try to force his way out. The safe was made of reinforced steel thick enough that he could only dent it with his fists, especially in the awkward space where he couldn’t even wind up properly. The researchers probably expected he’d get more motivated to break out of a cramped container and build strength, but he couldn’t. Fear began setting in and his strength always seemed to ebb when he was afraid. He started begging to be let out, overwhelmed with claustrophobia for the first time in his life. The researcher running the experiment in Vogelbaum’s absence told him flatly that he needed to try harder to make his way out. Rubbing the tears out of his eyes, John began to make out light. He thought he was just imagining moving shapes at first, wishfully thinking he could see, but soon realized he really could see the scientists behind the steel, standing around the safe, shuffling around, using messages scribbled on their clipboards when they wanted to communicate and avoid being heard by him. The people started as hazy blobs, but eventually he could see in more and more detail, until it was almost as if the steel wasn’t there at all, until he could read one of the researchers writing “Why is he so quiet? Maybe open it?” and some of the others shaking their head. Seeing beyond the confines of the safe reduced his claustrophobia, and calmed him down enough that he finally managed to find a way to rip the steel open by using his entire body—pushing one side with his feet and the other with his shoulders and head.

He had to have been at least eight years old by that time, because he even remembers wondering if he should tell his caretakers about this new power or keep it to himself—something he wouldn’t have considered at a younger age. He told Vogelbaum soon afterwards, of course. Every time he tried to keep a secret from his caretakers, he never managed it for long.

Homelander’s lazy outdoor afternoon comes to an end when he starts feeling an urgent need to piss. Once upon a time he might have just done it on the roof of this building and been done with it, but he doesn’t want any security camera installed somewhere getting footage of that. He’s pretty sure Vought used to deal with his minor misbehaviors so that nothing ever ended up online, but he’s without that protection now. If pressed, he might even concede it’s an antisocial thing to do whether he’s caught or not. He drifts down from his high perch, towards the Upper West Side, alighting gently on the balcony of their 24th floor apartment. Not quite as spectacular a view as from the top of the other building, but Billy would never have agreed to live in a gleaming glass skyscraper like that. For his part, Homelander likes having the balcony, and that’s not something you find on the soaring tall buildings anyway.

***

“Making chili again?” Billy asks first thing when he walks through the door.

Homelander shrugs. “I was craving beef. You’re welcome to order takeout.” He’ll be the first to admit that he learns to cook one thing, then tends to latch on to the dish, and repeats the exercise until he perfects it or suddenly gets repulsed by what he previously craved.

Billy shakes his head. “You really think I’m gonna pass on a homecooked meal from my private celebrity chef?”

“Your celebrity online recipe follower maybe,” Homelander grumbles, but obligingly pushes his ass back into Billy's body when he comes to stand right behind him at the stove.

Billy’s arms twine themselves around his body, hands raking over his belly. "Cut your hair?" he plants a chaste kiss right where the fresh undercut starts.

"Surprised you noticed," Homelander mumbles, focused on the bubbling saucepan in front of him, but also glancing down to see if Lena is looking around at the hands groping him. She's asleep most of the time, but he can't help checking constantly now. He wonders if he’ll be able to keep this new development a secret from Billy for long. Finally he notices Billy's strange tense heartbeats. He seems more touchy feely than usual for just coming in from work, and Homelander has the strange feeling that he's keeping something from him too. Homelander wants to ask where he was all day today, but that would reveal that he checks up on him. He wants to ask why Billy didn’t see his Instagram post and scold him for taking glamour shots on top of buildings that don’t technically allow trespassers on their roofs.

The feeling that something is off only mounts as they eat dinner at the dining room table, one of the new pieces of furniture Homelander took the liberty to buy to fill the bigger space they had now. Billy seems unusually quiet, and his thoughts seem far away. He hardly responds when Homelander brings up that he went public with his “real” name. Social media has been spreading the clip where he answers the question, and now legitimate media outlets were starting to retweet it as news.

“Thought you’d be more happy about it,” Homelander says, staring at Billy, suspecting that he hasn’t listened to a word he’s said.

“Huh?” Billy looks back at him, tearing his eyes away from the big window. “About what?”

“Me embracing my generic name. What’s the matter with you?”

“What. Nothing. Just tired.”

“You just seem distracted,” Homelander says, gesturing with his spoon. “And upset, I’d say.”

“Quit peeking at my vitals,” Billy says, his smile wan and half-hearted.

Homelander’s almost done with his bowl and trying to decide if he wants seconds. He gets up to put away leftovers into the fridge and load the dishwasher, attempting to take Billy’s only half eaten bowl, but Billy wrestles it back.

“I told you you can order out. Don’t pretend to like my cooking if you don’t.”

Billy eats an emphatic big spoonful as a response. “Your cooking’s scrummy. My shit mood has nothing to do with you or your cooking. I just... I learned something today that’s still botherin’ me.”

“Oh?” Homelander says, returning back to the table after depositing his dish in the dishwasher. He hears Billy’s heart thumping loudly and feels his own start to speed up as well. “Something from the investigation?”

“Yeah. Look, I don’t think it’s worth telling you. It’s just upsetting but it doesn’t really matter, and there’s nothing that can be done about it at this point.”

Homelander smiles. “Trying to spare me?”

“Don’t see the point in getting you all upset. It’s going to get brought up during the trial, but that won’t be for a while. I’ll tell you before then so you don’t have to hear it on TV.”

“Just fucking tell me now if you’re going to preface it like that,” Homelander mutters, growing impatient, but is surprised to see that Billy’s on the verge of tears, and his tone softens. “Come on, you can tell me.”

“Nothing new. Human experimentation bullshit. Just... personal in this case.”

Homelander feels a pang of protectiveness. “What did Vought do to upset my Billy?”

His eyes widen when Billy asks if they can lie down in bed together and hold each other, but he hesitates only for a moment, before getting up and scooping Billy up into his arms with one smooth motion. He glides into the bedroom, laying Billy out and then lying down beside him to face each other. Billy would have usually protested being manhandled, but he’s acting strange, almost clingy as he fumbles to embrace. He reaches down almost automatically and Homelander lifts up the hem of his own shirt inviting the other man’s callused hand to land on bare skin and pet his belly in circles. Homelander finds it strangely gratifying to hear the thumps of Billy’s heart slowing down, and he’s soothed by the touch too. He’s still waiting for Billy to say something, but there’s just uneasy silence between them.

“If it’s just something about my past you’ve uncovered, I ... I doubt I’ll get upset. How much worse can it really be than what I already remember?” Homelander looks at Billy to speak but he’s still quiet, hesitating. “If it’s about how they started with dozens of babies and killed all of them in their trials and I was just the hardiest one that survived, I already kind of knew that was the case.”

Billy shakes his head. Homelander starts to feel slightly nauseous, dread still mounting. “What. Does it have something to do with my pregnancy?”

“No! No, nothing about that.” Billy leans his head closer and kisses him.

Homelander glances down but he can’t tell if Lena’s asleep from the angle he has. Good for her if she can sleep through the adrenaline surging in his body. He racks his brain for what else it could be. Could it be something from his past that Billy finds absolutely abhorrent and it’s making him regret everything they have together? Homelander doesn’t have the courage to ask whether that’s the case. “Can you just fucking tell me? If your goal is to avoid freaking me out, you’re failing.”

“I was pretty upset when I heard about it. And then I saw it with my own eyes. But it’s irrational to be angry about it now. Just... promise me you won’t work yourself up over it. It ain’t worth it.”

“I’ll be the judge of that,” Homelander mutters.

Billy sighs heavily, hugging Homelander in close. “There was a whistleblower who came forward. A lab tech or something. Low on the totem pole. Revealed that Vought has another whole facility, not in the Tower, and not the one in Cold Spring Harbor where you were raised. This one’s in Connecticut. They... had Ryan there.”

Homelander’s body goes rigid. “What do you mean?” He sharply turns his head to peer through the bedroom wall into the living room, at the urn with Ryan’s ashes that he placed on the mantel above the gas fireplace. It’s the only object he requested to be returned to him from his Vought Tower apartment—the only thing that wasn’t bought with Vought money—the only thing that was really his. “What the fuck do you mean they had him there.”

“They hid his body there. We drove up there and raided the whole place. They had no idea we were coming, so there was plenty of evidence. I-“ Billy sighs heavily. “I saw it all. He was being kept in some kind of cryogenic storage tank. They were trying to clone him, managed to grow some stem cells in petri dishes and 'immortalized' them or something. I don’t fucking know what I'm talking about. The FBI is doing a whole detailed forensic investigation on what they were doing there... but I don’t know. It makes me sick thinking about it. I shouldn’t have driven up there with the team. It was too personal. I can’t unsee it now.”

Homelander is breathing hard through his nose, still processing. “So then what the fuck is in the urn?!” his shout comes out hoarse and shrill, trembling all over. “Huh?!! They just gave me someone’s random ashes?!”

Billy sighs. “We’ll turn it in for analysis. Not sure they can always tell who it was after cremation.”

“But it’s not Ryan...” Homelander mumbles, still somehow having a hard time believing the level of duplicity Vought was treating him with.

Billy simply shakes his head. Homelander says nothing, and he can feel his expression turn completely stony.

“I told you. There’s nothing that can be done about it now. I can’t even tell you why I’m so fucking livid. If they had managed to do it, to clone him or whatever the hell they were up to, I’d have part of Becca back again. Maybe I’d even be happy about it. But... I saw it. His body, all banged up, the way he must have died. You saw it before, I didn’t. And they carved into him like a piece of meat. It’s just not right. Feels like I’ll never unsee it.”

Homelander still says nothing, jaw clenched to the point his teeth are starting to hurt.

Billy hugs him tight, and Homelander can feel him trembling. “If they’d managed it, they’d have raised the new kid in secret, in any case. No way either of us would have known that child existed. Just another little project for them. To have another mini Homelander, like you’re some kind of thoroughbred. But that’s Becca’s kid too. That’s Becca’s kid they didn’t bury and dissected like some fucking... piece of meat. That’s his DNA they were collecting all over the lab, his cells they were growing in petri dishes. The whole thing is just sick.”

Homelander can’t say a word, can’t breathe. He can feel himself shaking but can’t stop it. He starts feeling faint. He starts thinking about Ryan, alive and well, when he first met him, those idyllic few days when he was getting to know him, the couple of days when he stole him out of the Vought compound but quickly found he was in over his head, the last day he saw him alive, when he found him after such a tenacious, long search, how the boy rushed towards him hugging him like he really truly needed him. And these nice memories are still inextricable from the horrible image of how he found him among the rubble after the blast, bleeding, bones protruding, internal organs smashed and not all inside. And they kept him like that? Preserved him, floating slowly through cryofluid, eyes pale and veiled? Taking pieces for experiments and cloning attempts? Homelander gets up and stumbles to the toilet, feeling like his entire dinner is about to come back up.

Billy walks up to stand behind him. He puts his hand on Homelander’s shoulder while he’s heaving, throat slightly burning, accidentally cracking the bathtub while grasping its edge.

“Have some water...” he says offering him a glass.

“That’s why.” Homelander barely hears anything beyond the blood rushing in his ears, gritting his teeth. “That’s why they were so fucking pushy for me to let them take his body away when I was lying there with his corpse, mourning. That’s why. I thought they were worried about me, but they were just worried I was using up their precious stem cells’ clock. And they were going to keep it a secret from me. I’m so fucking naive. Every single fucking time. Fool me ten times, shame on me,” Homelander slowly gets back to his feet, hands clenching into fists, but there’s nothing in his vicinity he can punch that wouldn’t shatter from the impact. Certainly not Billy, who puts his own hands over his fists and tries to get him to lower his hands down.

“There ain’t nothing we can do right now. We can lay him to rest once he’s out of the FBI morgue. Give him a proper funeral.”

“A proper funeral? You want an open casket and everything?! That way at least I know it's really him they're letting me bury this time? You saw him, right? How bad was it?”

Billy shakes his head, grimacing. “Just forget I said anything about it. I don’t wanna talk about it. I don’t wanna even think about it, alright? I could tell it was him. It felt like seeing him die again. Sick bastards.”

It’s so tempting. The idea becomes more and more alluring by the second. Homelander wipes his mouth, finally taking the glass of water Billy is still holding for him, gulping it down before heading over to the balcony.

Billy grabs his wrist. “Oi, where do you think you’re going?” The grab has absolutely no power to stop him but Homelander whips around anyway.

“Where do you think?”

“To do what.”

“To... fly over and... just start going to town on the entire building with heat vision. That house of cards is made of glass and steel. I can melt it and have it fall into rubble in... a couple of minutes. Tops. Before the fucks in the upper offices even know what hit them, before they even think to run for the elevators.”

“Sounds like one of my fantasies,” Billy says. “But it won’t kill Vought, just maim it. And the investigation will get postponed because now the FBI’s got a superpowered homegrown terrorist on their hands. You won’t be able to live in the US. There might be very few places you can live and maybe not the way you’d want to after doing something like that. Think about Lena if you don’t want to think about yourself, Johnny.”

Homelander is breathing hard. He knows what Billy’s saying makes perfect sense. But he needs to kill someone, sooner rather than later. He feels a movement deep inside, but it’s like he’s switched gears, there’s so much pent up rage in him right now that he can’t even pay attention to the life growing inside him that he’s been so excited about. He’s angry because he somehow didn’t expect it. And why didn’t he? Vought kept Ryan from him for all those years. Vought tried to steal Ryan back from under his nose and make it look like someone else had done it. Vought never told him about what a dangerous piece of shit his own father was so he put Ryan in harm's way without realizing it. Vought tortured him into having superpowers and he loved them for it, worshipped them, honestly, if he cares to admit it. Has Vought ever done anything for his own good, when it wasn’t already primarily in their interests?

“Let’s go lie down,” Billy says.

“I don’t need to fucking lie down!” Homelander shouts louder than he intended.

Billy rubs his elbow. “Maybe I’m asking ya cause I need it. I wanna lie down and hold you in my arms and feel the baby move, and not think about what I saw today for one fucking minute, alright?”

Homelander didn’t even realize his lasers had powered up when his temper flared, only noticing his eyes power down at Billy’s words. Maybe this was just Billy’s way of manipulating him to avoid doing something stupid and regrettable. But he seems genuinely upset. He seems genuinely eager to hug Homelander closer. Homelander feels himself slowly coming down from the roiling boil of anger he’d reached, but he still feels sick to his stomach, and still wants to hurt someone badly. He just prays he doesn’t take it out on Billy at some point during the course of this miserable evening.

Although it’s nice to lie there and cuddle and feel like he’s useful to Billy, Homelander—no, he’s not going to call himself that. Vought might have given him both names, but only one of them is an actual registered Vought trademark. Although it’s nice to lie there and cuddle, John gets restless, sits up and starts speaking quickly. “You know what—can, can I still add to my testimony? I can, right? Because I was holding back before. Don’t ask me why. I mean, you know better than anyone. You yelled at me about it. And you were absolutely right. I’m an idiot. Why the fuck am I sparing them? Just- Just because I’m embarrassed about how I was raised, and what I went through? Well I don’t care anymore. I don’t give a fuck. I really don’t. Everyone in the world can talk about it and judge me and laugh at me, but I’ll go on record about everything now. Everything. I don’t give a fuck.” John’s hyperventilating with how upset he’s getting. “Can you record me or something? I don’t know if I can go in order.” His nose twitches reflexively, pulling back the suppressed tears flowing into it.

“Let’s do it tomorrow.”

“No, let’s do it right fucking now. Didn't you want me to give the complete picture of how Vought raised me?” John asks.

“I just don’t want you getting all worked up. Get Lena upset.”

“Oh I’m all worked up, to the max. I need the world to know. If you don’t record me, I’ll go and record a Facebook Live and get it off my chest.”

Billy relents and starts up a voice memo recording on his phone. John starts to recount everything as it comes to mind, all the methods the Vought team used to develop many of his powers. Billy convinced him to at least lie back down, and he’s staring up at the ceiling like a blank canvas, trying to recall everything he’s systematically tried to forget over the years. He tries to move chronologically but the memories he’s dredging up are not all connected, and they don’t all come to mind in succession. It takes a long time to run through it all. 

How his skin didn’t start out as tough as it is now, and how he went through rounds of being burned with direct flames, immersed in strong acid and liquid nitrogen, compressed with heavy machinery.

How the researchers later bemoaned having started with his skin, because it made it difficult to even reach his internal organs to inure them to damage. How he had everything from molten tar to dry ice to combustible fuel and explosives put inside him from either end so they could build resistance along the accessible parts of the digestive tract.

How he got so damaged and then thoroughly resistant at first that he stopped being able to absorb any nutrients from food, and the researchers all panicked and thought that was the end of that because they couldn’t feed him through any other means like IV because no needle could puncture his skin or breach his bloodstream. How they decided to let it play out, and watched him try to eat and not absorb anything for weeks. How he remembers watching himself growing gaunt and lethargic over that time period, seeing the changes in his face in the mirror, overhearing his caretakers discuss how long it might take him to die of starvation. How eventually his body relented and adapted again, at which point they began only doing intermittent damaging training to strike a happy medium between invulnerability and viability.

How he spent hours “training” in a cell with an electrified metal floor, getting shocked until he eventually developed the ability to hover above the floor. How at the end of one of these sessions—where they’d been zapping him for hours and he hadn’t managed to defy gravity and escape the pain—he was so tired and angry that he simply lasered the first researcher who opened the door to escort him out and felt zero remorse despite being scolded harshly.

How killing people wasn’t consistently followed by punishment during his childhood. How if he had well-meaning intentions like snapping his tutor’s spine while hugging her, it was treated as an accident. They did punish him when they deemed that he did something through malice or apathetic carelessness. He’d be kept sequestered alone in a bare cell with nothing in it, the zinc coating on the walls not allowing him to see anyone through them. It was four reflective metal walls, so he saw himself in an endless number of reflections, and it used to scare him and he’d sit on the floor and shut his eyes to avoid feeling like he was alone in an infinite universe of scared looking boys. The Bad Room. He dealt very poorly with being in there, and even though he probably never stayed in there longer than a day, he’d be hysterically remorseful by the end of it. Which is why they probably kept using it as a method of punishment. How eventually he started to have dialogues with himself when he was kept alone in the room which helped soothe the terror. He started out mumbling quietly, eventually learning to do it silently inside his own head, even when he wasn’t inside the Bad Room.

How they used his meals to introduce poisons into his system, some of which had quite painful effects and made him dread eating. How his sense of smell evolved greatly during that time until he could always detect which foods were poisoned even with the most scentless agents. And how he’d be punished if he refused to eat the foods he knew would cause him pain. They’d put him into the Bad Room with just the plate of food he refused to eat for company until he’d relent.

John could see Billy’s face swing from sad to sickened to eventually just frowning when he moved on to the sorts of things Vought tasked him with when he was operating as a superhero. John was talking about all the incidents he could think of that resulted in needless fatalities: all the times that he killed criminals instead of just stopping them, every instance where he recklessly killed victims or innocent bystanders. It was hard to remember them all, some incidents blurring together in his memory. He didn’t get too far into these before Billy cut him off with “alright, alright, that’s more than enough to work with.”

“If I didn’t know any better, I might think you don’t want to hear about my crimes,” John says.

“You can’t go to court confessing all this and expecting to get full amnesty. And I don’t think your adulthood is all that relevant here. But the childhood... it was worse than I thought, let me just say.”

They lie in silence for a while. John’s rage has dissipated a bit. Talking about everything so frankly was enervating but also feels cleansing.

“You really don’t want me going to prison, huh,” John finally says, rolling over on his side and watching Billy intently.

“No shit I don’t.”

“You don’t think I deserve to for the things I’ve done?” John puts his chin on Billy’s shoulder.

“I don’t really want to talk about you deserve or not. You probably deserved a normal childhood and you never got that either.” Billy pauses. “I’m at the point where I want what’s best for Lena. And I don’t know if I can take care of her on my own.”

“You could just ask ‘Aunt Grace’ or someone,” John mutters under his breath, for some reason eager to argue, because he wants to hear why Billy’s defending him, but at the same time he dreads that he’ll use up Billy’s goodwill and he’ll turn on him.

“I want to raise her with you, alright? As long as you’re not planning to do more of that violent shite in the future, I don’t care about the past anymore.”

“That’s not the way the justice system works,” John mumbles.

“Are you eager to get prison time or something?” Billy asks in exasperation.

“No.”

It’s gotten dark outside while they were talking. John’s compressed bladder makes itself known again, and he reluctantly rises from the bed to make a trip to the bathroom. When he comes back, he sees Billy propped up on a pillow against the headboard, reviewing the recording, checking quality. John slides back into bed next to him.

“This is big, Johnny. These kinds of details are going to change the tone of this whole thing. Their crimes against a person are gonna carry much more weight than the details of all their tax fraud.”

“You sure about that?”

“With Congress and the public. I didn’t say with the IRS.”

John props himself up on one elbow. “It’s not like I’m the only witness in this whole thing right?”

Billy shakes his head. “No, but the people Vought tortured more than you are dead. So yeah, it’d be nice if you gave everyone the full scope of how they really raised you and made you their golden-boy.”

“Yeah, well, that was the idea. Fuck them.”

Billy sighs. “I’ll have to go through it and write this up as notes. Then the lawyers will write it into questions. And we’ll have to do another deposition. You realize that Vought’s lawyers will be present again,right? You sure you won’t lose your nerve this go around? Not going to say it 'didn't really hurt' or whatever the fuck you were claiming last time?”

“I don’t give a fuck anymore. Vought never treated me like a human being, so why should I have any pride about it. And why should I care if everyone gets to laugh at me. I’m barely a real person anyway. I just... didn’t want Lena to know that’s the kind of pathetic past she comes from, but no one’s going to treat her like a human being either, the way things seem to be going. If I don’t watch out she’ll end up taken to a lab and tortured or cut up in pieces too. So I might as well lay it all out there.”

Billy watches him, waiting to make sure he’s really paused before speaking, slow and measured. John feels self-conscious and rolls over to turn away.

“You do know that no one in their right mind is going to laugh at you for what you went through?”

John sneers. “You don’t find it a little funny? That the most powerful man on earth grew up afraid and fucking... I don’t even know... submissive? Doing everything they asked me to do?”

“No, Johnny, not the least bit. It’s a fucking tragedy is what it is.”

“Fine. Alright. If you say so. But I’ve never wanted to be pitied either. I didn’t want people to know Vought raised me like some sort of- I don’t even know what this qualified as. Like something powerful and dangerous but subhuman. I thought Lena would have a better life if I never went into any of those details. What’s done is done, I thought. It’s in the past. But it’s not fucking done! It’s never fucking done. They keep doing the same things. And I am probably subhuman anyway. They just taught me to hide it well from the public-”

“Alright, just stop using that word.” Billy cuts him off this time, attempting to pull him back to face each other, to no avail.

“What, subhuman? You said so yourself, that I’m different. Have a fundamentally different mind. That I lack something that makes people human.”

“I never said that,” Billy protests.

“You don’t have to apologize. You were right about Vought. You’re probably right about me too. I probably lack something. How would I even know? You’re never gonna love me because they raised me to be a product and a weapon, not a loving person. They sure taught me to want to be loved, though. That was the cruel part. Why the hell did they bother teaching me that? Probably harder to control an animal that’s satisfied, so they kept me hungry for it, kept me tame because I always wanted their approval so much.”

Billy finally sits up, clearly getting more agitated, the volume of his voice rising. “Look, I don’t care how Vought treated you. I sure as hell don’t think of you that way.”

John sniffs back his unshed tears again. Maybe he’s starting to wallow in self-pity now, but he feels so betrayed, so alone and it all comes spilling out of him. “I just pray you’re going to be kind to Lena and love her. I just want her to have a better life than me. She’s done nothing wrong. Promise me you’ll love her, please. Even if she turns out just like me, promise you’ll still love her.”

Billy sighs, rubbing the back of his neck before reaching over and finally managing to pull John into a spooning embrace.

“I do love you, Johnny. Very much,” Billy mumbles into the nape of his neck, barely intelligible.

John is aghast at how quickly the tears start spilling down his face when he hears those words.

“But I’m not gonna lie, listening to you ranting and raving about being less than human is making me feel ill. Can’t you just be quiet a minute and hold me?” Billy asks, and John immediately obliges, twisting around in his embrace, twining his own arms around, stroking Billy’s face tenderly, pressing in close, Lena wedged between their bodies. There are very conflicting emotions roiling in his chest—the rage at Vought is all still there, but also an incredible, overwhelming wave of anxious affection which temporarily drowns everything else out. “Ever.” John is trying to sound upset, but he’s barely suppressing a laugh. “Or at least until my jawline decides to make an appearance again.”

“Eat it yourself.”

John stares at the photo of them he took blindly—Billy giving him a big kiss on the cheek, while he’s cracking up and squinting his eyes shut, big toothy grin. It’s all very candid, and there’s none of that studied self-awareness that usually plagues even his best photos. “It’s already dark.” John protests, but even he’s not sure how that’s a counterargument.

“No. In fact, it’ll be secluded, where it’ll be no one but us.”

Billy shakes his head looking annoyed. “Just because I trust you, doesn’t mean I’m gonna enjoy it.”

“I know,” John cuts him off. “I know that.” He swallows hard. “Did they ever end up setting the congressional hearing date?”

“No, they’ve been dragging their feet, no set date yet. Probably sometime in September. Unless they uncover more shite between now and then, which is a definite possibility the way things have been going so far. But pencil in September.”

“Well, she better be out by then.” John’s joking because he doesn’t want to cry about it. In the back of his mind he does worry about what this whole investigation will mean for everyone who’s ever been exposed to Compound V, let alone someone like him who was bred to no longer depend on it. Will it be a category denoted on IDs? If Vought no longer tracks and organizes supes, will the government take over and make every supe register? So much of his life is not under his own control, but John supposes it never really was.

“You don’t think this Vought investigation will lead to every supe getting detained or something crazy like that, right?”

”Don’t see how it could ever lead to that. If that happens, guess all three of us are leaving the States.”

John can’t help but smile at hearing ‘all three of us’ dropped so casually by Billy. He’s not sure the other man understands that this is his first time feeling like he’s part of a family, and not a family found and assembled for him by Vought. He feels another mild cramp coming on, and wrinkles his nose. From what he’s read about it, this could be the beginning of labor. But he’s had so many wishful thinking false alarms that he’s going to wait before he tells Billy.

They stand up and take the walk they allegedly came here for, but at some point John just takes to drifting above the ground, not really enjoying the feeling of swelling building up around his ankles when he puts any weight on his feet. His body was trained to withstand all sorts of damage, but somehow the pregnancy is bypassing all of those defenses and causing him all sorts of discomfort he never thought he’d experience.

“Why are you nervous now?” John asks when he hears Billy’s heartrate speeding up again.

“Just about having to go back the same way we came,” Billy says, sounding none too happy about being observed so closely.

“We have to trust each other,” John says.

“Is this your trust fall exercise for me? Cause I’ll tell you right now I wasn’t ever any good at those. Nothin' personal.”

It bothers John that he’s trusted Billy enough to leave his entire life behind whereas Billy can’t seem to get over this inane fear that he’ll drop him.

But Billy’s tone softens, as if he suddenly decodes John’s meaning. “Look, it’s probably a phobia. It’s not rational. You could say I had a phobia about having kids, and I got over that one, didn’t I? So just give me some grace and maybe I’ll eventually get over this one too, you know? John relents and smiles. “You ready to go back home?”

It’s somewhere mid-flight when it happens. John startles to feel wetness quickly spreading along the fabric of his shorts. He can’t really see over his belly. He grimaces as he starts to feel cramping again.

“Alright, just... stay calm. Just get in the shower for now. I’ll... call... “Okay, Lena. Let’s do this nice and quick,” he says, taking deep calming breaths. There’s no pain between contractions, but he’s still in a mild panic now that things are in motion.

Billy comes back in, this time mopping up the wet trail John left in his wake.

“Sonnenberg’s driving over. She says you’ve probably still got many hours to go, but she’ll spend the night here. She should be picking up the midwife she arranged for before on the way, so that should be all squared away. They said to just take it easy and time your contractions until they get here. You doin’ alright?”

John shrugs, trying to look composed, but he knows he looks like a mess. He’s broken out in a cold sweat and breathing hard.

Billy stares at him, his confident devil-may-care façade peeled away completely. He’s looking pretty spooked. He remembers himself though, and pulls John’s shorts and underwear off him and wrings them out in the sink.

“Okay... okay... you just stay put and I’ll get the bed ready.”

As Billy moves about the apartment, John still listens to his heart pounding loud and clear, and watches him through the walls as he strips the bed, lays down a shower curtain they bought just for this, before putting soft bedding back on top of it. John tries to get into a more comfortable position, feet planted against the tile wall. He sees the change inside him—now that most of the fluid around Lena is gone, his uterus looks different. He watches as another contraction hits, but turns away.

“Another one?” Billy asks as he comes back in and sees John’s legs tensed.

John nods wordlessly, grimacing.

Billy picks up the phone and restarts the timer. “That was nine minutes between. They said when it’s five or less, then it’s close.”

When the contraction eases up, John’s on the verge of tears.

“What’s wrong?”

“Just seeing her getting squeezed by my own body. She looks unhappy. It’s kind of messed up.”

“It’s how it’s supposed to be,” Billy tries to reassure him. “Stop looking in there. Just focus on yourself.”

Billy escorts him out of the tub to the bed, laying an absorbent pad underneath him and then covers him over with a warm blanket, because even though it’s July, John has started to shiver. He’s not cold, it’s the nerves, but he wraps the blanket around himself tightly anyway.

“I’ll just go set up the air mattresses for the two birds in the nursery. You need anything else right now?”

“I’m hungry,” John says. “I was going to have dinner after we came back. You think it’s bad to eat now?”

Billy is probably not the best person to ask for advice about this but he tries to answer authoritatively. “I- I doubt it’s gonna hurt anything. They said it might take a while anyway.” Billy rushes off to the kitchen. “You want yogurt?!” He yells, apparently forgetting that John can hear him just fine at any volume.

“Yeah that’s fine!” John yells back.

Billy hurries back in and hands him a whole quart container of plain yogurt and a spoon. John doesn’t have the energy to ask for a plate, and just starts eating straight out of the container, soothed by the taste and distracted from his panicked thoughts. He hears Billy fiddle around getting the air mattresses inflated.

“Shh, sorry baby. It is very loud,” John apologizes when he feels Lena squirm in the very tight space she still occupies inside him at the loud sound of the vacuum pump in the next room.

Billy finally stops doing various chores and joins John in the bedroom, kneeling by the bed.

There’s still some water coming out of John in fits and starts. He wonders if it was supposed to stop by now.

Billy shakes his head as he switches out the absorbent pad for a new one. “You dripped all over Manhattan, didn’t you. I’m sure someone felt it rain.”

John snickers, but it’s a pained sound because he feels another contraction starting up.

Billy watches him intently. “They’re almost five minutes apart. I just hope the doctor gets here before... you know.”

“You’ll figure it out if she’s not here,” John says through clenched teeth. “I trust you.”
