July 5, 2023

Everything is hazy and blurry. There’s been so much pain over so many hours that John has no idea how long it’s been anymore. The sun has come up and come down, fireworks happened in the background, and now it looks like it’s almost evening of the next day. He hasn’t slept. Skipping sleep for a few days didn’t use to affect him so adversely. But he’s drained. Exhausted isn’t even the word. It’s as much a mental as a physical collapse. He’s drifting in a world where vision and hearing and sensation are no longer adding up to a coherent whole. The contractions barely ever let up. He started out so brave. Tried pacing around the room the first night, squatting in the bathtub, kneeling on all fours on the bed, but at this point he can’t push anymore, he can’t do any of that Lamaze breathing bullshit. He can’t do much more than lie on his back and pray for an end to this. He doesn’t even care how it will end anymore. If someone had a means of euthanizing him, he’d probably take them up on the offer. He scans the room. His eyesight is playing all sorts of tricks on him at this point in time. The midwife has called in reinforcements and has another assistant fussing around the room, so they can switch off. His doctor is still by his side, peering into him, still trying to figure out what’s gone wrong. They’re all fatigued. Maybe not as tired as he is. They’ve all taken a break now and then to eat and sleep, whereas the only thing he’s consumed is ice chips and been painfully awake for it all. But they’re exhausted too, and have exhausted all their ideas for how to try and help. The midwife tried to use forceps a couple of times, to no avail. Sonnenberg tried coaxing his cervix to open by molding, but that doesn’t even seem to be his main issue. His body clearly wants to push the baby out but can’t do it. If he was a normal earthly mortal they would have given him a C-section many, many hours ago. But if he was a normal earthly mortal he probably wouldn’t be in this predicament in the first place. The senior midwife was supposed to have experience with supes giving birth, but she insists his case is exceptional and impossible, that she’s never seen anything like it, and that there’s nothing in the playbook about these kinds of circumstances. None of the babies she’s delivered were super-powered. At least part of the problem is his super-powered daughter actually moving backwards in the birth canal and fighting back against his contractions.

Where the fuck is Billy? He was by his side through this ordeal, but he’s been gone for... John can’t really tell time. It’s probably only been fifteen minutes. Maybe he finally gave up and went off to get some sleep? John knows it’s a lot to ask of people to stay at his side for this many hours straight. He’s already had one complete nervous breakdown which seemed to cause Billy to lose all hope and cry quietly in the other room where he thought John wouldn’t hear him. He can’t stand the pity and the fear in all their eyes. The only one who doesn’t seem to have fear or pity for him is Vogelbaum. The man is sitting in a chair right near the door of the bedroom. John knows he can’t possibly be in this room. He’s dead, and he hasn’t had a headful of salt and pepper hair for decades. Deep down, John knows that this is Vogelbaum from his childhood memories and that his brain is conjuring this up, but this hallucination is actually soothing in these dire circumstances.

“John, you’re far too old to be crying,” he can hear Vogelbaum’s voice distinctly in his head, and he wishes he was back in the lab, back in the safety of undergoing horrible physical ordeals but always having full trust that he can survive all the tests they throw at him. He’s far from sure he can survive this test, and he never had to worry about losing someone else back in the lab days either.

“She’s just not having it,” Sonnenberg says somewhere near John’s right ear. “I can literally see you lose ground whenever you stop pushing. And I don’t know what to do about that.”

“Maybe there’s a way to sedate the baby?” one of the midwives asks, clearly fearful of the whole situation.

“This is Homelander we’re talking about, it’s impossible to sedate either of them.” John hears Sonnenberg’s voice as if it’s off in the distance.

John has half a mind to kill everyone in the room just to stop hearing them talk about him as if he’s not there.

“You still with us? Have any ideas?” Sonnenberg asks and John shakes his head no, wishing to god he wasn’t conscious anymore.

Billy returns from somewhere, smelling like fresh air and cigarettes all at once.

“Did you-” John would sound angry if he wasn’t delirious. “Did you just decide to go back to smoking?!”

“I needed a ciggy. Tea wasn’t cutting it. I couldn’t do this anymore,” Billy says, sounding tired and indifferent, although he looks absolutely wrecked when John looks up at his face.

“You can’t do this anymore?! What the fuck are you even doing!? I’m the only one suffering and no one’s doing anything to help me!” John knows he’s saying something cruel but can’t stop himself in the throes of pain.

“You’re right,” Billy replies and John can tell there’s sorrow on his face, but John only gets angrier at seeing that. “All I can offer you is a cigarette at this point. Tea if you want it. I don’t know how to help.”

“Fuck you! Fuck you! I never should have done this! I never should have asked you to do this with me! I never want to have sex ever again!”

“Fair enough,” Billy says, tone flat and defeated.

“Nothing is worth this pain!” John glances at the door, verifies Vogelbaum isn’t there anymore, and bursts into tears, not only because of the pain, but because of what he just admitted out loud.

“I swear if I could take your pain on, I would,” Billy mutters under his breath. “I wish I knew how to help. Talk some sense into her, tell her it’s time to come out. Fucking hell.”

It wasn’t fair of John to say he was the only one suffering, of course. He’s watched Billy grow more and more haggard as this ordeal has stretched on and on, and it’s clearly taking a toll. But John’s panicking. He’s terrified to see that no one in the room has control of the situation. Billy falling back on a nicotine habit only makes John realize how out of control everyone feels about this birth. Sonnenberg told him not to panic, because his stress is making things worse, but it’s easy for her to say. Her own heartbeat has been a tick fast the entire last day or so, once it became clear this wasn’t going to be a standard birth scenario.

John feels like he and his baby are stuck in a cursed limbo. That they’ll die like this, and even though you could say it’s Lena being stubborn, it’s his own fault for not knowing how to fix this.

He’s reached the breaking point.

“Billy...” John sobs, realizing the gravity of what he’s asking for. “Take me to Vought Tower. They have a medical wing. They made me. They’ll know what to do.”

Billy blinks at him, expression stony, but his eyes give away how he feels.

“I’m sorry!” John sobs again. “I’m just... I don’t know what else to do. I feel like I’m going to die if I don’t get help.”

“Alright...” Billy says. “Alright, we can do that.”

Sonnenberg sighs. “You two are on your own. I’m not setting foot in there.”

“That’s fine,” Billy repeats woodenly. “You want me to drive you there in my car, love?”

“I’m sorry!” John sobs again, and it’s getting hard to get his words out between sobs. “It’s not fair! It’s just not- it’s not fair!”

“What isn’t fair?” Billy asks wearily.

“All I wanted was to have a child – Why does everything have to be so complicated for me! I don’t want to go there... believe me, I don’t want to go back to them.”

“It’s alright. I understand,” Billy reassures him. “You don’t gotta apologize. I’ll take you. Just let me figure out the best way to get you down into the garage.”

“We can work it out later,” Billy interrupts him. “I don’t want anything to happen to you.”

“Since when do we give up so easily, John?” John turns his head trying to figure out who said those words. There aren’t any other men in the room except Billy. It’s something like his own voice, but without any of the sobbing and fear, cool and collected. John glances at the door and sees Vogelbaum is back at his post, watching him with the familiar unimpressed expression he used to see through the glass door of the bad room, but it’s his own voice in his head.

“You’re in charge here. Stop expecting everyone else to help. You’re the only one who can push her out.”

“What if I can’t,” John whispers under his breath rhetorically, hoping no one else in the room notices him talking to himself.

“If you expected this to be some kind of cakewalk, well then... maybe you just weren’t cut out to be a parent.”

John winces at the harsh words and his inner voice softens a bit.

“You’ve come so far already. It’s just strange to give up and risk losing her now. You’re so close. You’re not weaker than your own child.”

Billy approaches the bed. “Love, I don’t have a great way to carry you besides in my arms. We just need to get over to the elevator and then find the car downstairs... I think I can carry you if you need it.”

“Wait- wait,” John whispers. “Let me just try one last time.”

Billy looks on somberly as John tries to sit up and pull his legs up again.

“I don’t want to go back to them.” John breathes in and out, scrunching his eyes shut. “I don’t want to give my baby up to them. I’ll push... I’m not going to stop pushing until she’s out or I pass out... Take me to Vought only if I pass out.”

John hates himself for being so scared of death, but it’s less his own death than something going catastrophically wrong and losing Lena that he’s afraid of. He’s already experienced the death of a child. He doesn’t know if he can live through another one.

John glances down when he feels the bed dip and sees Billy poised to receive the baby. It’s the first time he’s taken that post—the midwives standing off to the side, happy to cede responsibility.

“You’re not gonna pass out,” Billy assures him, rubbing his thigh. “You’re gonna have our beautiful baby right here. Come on.” Billy flicks his fingers and it’s a ridiculous come-hither motion, like John is being asked to pass him a football or something, but it’s comforting to have Billy there instead of off to the side, and it’s comforting to hear him say that he’s going to do it. He takes a deep breath and starts to push again, his entire body trembling with the effort and he feels the dull pressure start to turn into a burning, stinging pain again. But this has happened before, and as soon as he becomes too tired to push continuously and takes a rest, their baby pulls back up to the safety of the womb.

“Just push, push, don’t stop,” Billy babbles words of encouragement.

John wants to ask if she’s visible, but he can’t spare the energy for words without risking going back to square one. He pushes on, staring at Billy between his legs, but starts crying when he feels like he’s going to lose this battle yet again. He’s just too tired, whereas their baby seems to have endless energy to fight back against him.

“Sorry,” he says, flicking his eyes away up at the ceiling when he realizes his lasers have powered on from the distress and pain.

Billy shakes his head. “It’s okay. Honestly kinda glad you can still power them up after all this.”

John cries when he can feel the baby sliding right back up inside him, pushing right into his ribcage when he stops pushing for only a moment.

Billy sighs. “Lena, this is fucking inconsiderate of you.”

As John lies panting, trying to recover, he suddenly feels a new strange sensation inside him, like a pop. His head shoots up to look at what happened.

Blood gushes out of him, Billy not entirely escaping the spray.

“Oh, that’s not good. The placenta’s detached now...” Sonnenberg mutters, stepping closer and peering inside as well. “It’s really just do or die.”

“What does that mean?” John asks.

“The placenta usually only detaches once the baby is out. She’s not going to be getting oxygen exchange anymore.”

Billy clambers up the bed to touch John’s face, ignoring the pool of blood under his knees. “John. She said do or die. You gotta push her out, right now, or we’re losing her. Right now.”

Maybe the lack of oxygen finally made their baby relent. Maybe Lena was put off by the sudden torrent of blood all around her. “It burns!” he mewls, not proud of how his voice sounds at the moment.

One of the midwives chimes in. “It’s normal, it’s just called ring of fire when the baby is stretching-”

“No, it’s not fucking normal,” Billy cuts her off as he peers down. Something is happening, and John realizes there’s a red glow underneath his skin when he looks down.

Everyone but Billy moves across the room to the door.

“You are just winning all the lotteries,” Billy says shaking his head. “What a time to unlock that power…”

“You should move away,” John moans, tears starting to flow as he feels his own sensitive insides sizzling.

But it’s as if Billy’s gotten a second wind seeing this grotesque sight. “Just push. Just keep pushing. I’ll watch out for myself. She’s facing down. Don’t you worry about me. Just push her out. You’re doing it. Almost there. You've got this.”

John does keep pushing, more or less in time with Billy’s stupid little phrases, amazed and grateful for his partner’s suicidal bravery staying near him. The lasers thankfully power off before her head emerges out of him. John has no idea what’s going on below the belt anymore. There’s a lot of blood rushing out of him all around her, and he’s not even sure what sounds he’s making. He’s vaguely aware of everyone in the room panicking. The baby’s shoulder is snagged on his pelvis, so nothing past the neck is coming out. He can hear the midwife direct Billy to manipulate his lower half into a different position, although she herself won’t move any closer to help. John allows everything without protest, limp as a ragdoll at this point, watching Billy almost as if he’s in a dream. Billy who’s caked in blood, all over his arms, face, beard, clothes. Billy who doesn’t seem to flinch at any of it, even though John can’t imagine it’s a pretty sight down there. Billy who’s probably risking his life handling a baby who just discovered how to deploy lasers and may do it again any moment. John’s laid out on his side, leg raised, and he cries when he feels Billy finally manage to pull Lena out of him.

When John imagined how this would go, he thought he wouldn’t let anyone else handle her, that he’d catch her himself and hold her close and protect everyone else from any possible danger she might pose. But instead it’s Billy holding her up against his chest, rocking her up and down, rubbing her tiny back, trying to get her to cough or cry. She’s coneheaded, a little bit blue, and John is upset she looks so much worse for the wear after being born than how she looked in the womb, and that that’s how her other parent gets to see her for the first time, but at least she’s out, and at least there’s no lasers in sight.

John doesn’t know how long everything took from the moment of crisis. He doesn’t know if she got injured during the rushed delivery. He feels a lot of afterbirth sliding out of his body, followed by more and more blood flowing all over his thighs, and the bed, and he sees one midwife fussing over him, packing towels between his legs, while the other one is wiping the blood off of Lena’s face to allow her to breathe. He’s starting to get tunnel vision, sees that Sonnenberg is peering into him, looking concerned, apparently trying to mold his organs to try and stop the hemorrhage and heal the internal burns, sees Billy standing over him looking worried even as he rubs Lena’s back to stimulate crying. 

Despite all the pain and distress, John breaks into a tearful laugh when he hears Lena’s quiet first cry. He begs to hold her, and once Billy lays her out on his chest, even while they’re still toweling all the blood off of her, he leans down to inhale the scent of her before he succumbs and passes out.

Chapter 16: July 8,9,17, 2003

Chapter Summary

Dropping this before the season completely airs.
I'm glad anti-supe legislation is now canon as of season 4, since I for some reason wrote that in earlier, but now am not sure it was actually mentioned in season 3 or not. It all works out.
Thank you to everyone who has been reading this feverdream!

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

July 8th, 2023

Butcher cracks open one eye just to see that it’s still pitch dark. Hours have lost all meaning in their current existence of fussing over a baby who is fed on demand, about every three hours. Homelander sleeps between the two of them, and is the first one to respond to her, but Butcher has to help out after she’s fed. He can’t complain. After seeing the birth, there was definitely a moment where he pictured having to raise Lena as a single parent.

“You can go back to sleep, she’s still feeding,” Homelander tells him.

“She’s usually pretty quick,” Butcher says, propping himself up on an elbow to watch the scene.

“Well she’s not very hungry. More like comforting herself.” Homelander winces right at the end of the sentence.

“She biting ya or what?”

Homelander shakes his head. “No, just start to feel everything down there contracting when she's sucking.”

“They said that was supposed to happen, right?”

Homelander nods. “Yeah, it just feels like cramping. It’s not that bad. Go back to sleep, I’ll wake you when she’s done.”

Despite being tired, Butcher isn’t sure he wants to drift off to a light sleep. He still relives the birth in his nightmares sometimes. The sight of his daughter’s head emerging, the flesh around her strangely aglow, the sound of something sizzling and Homelander’s plaintive, fatigued cries of pain-- it’s all seared into his memory. It was the smell of burning flesh that almost made Butcher heave, but luckily he hadn’t eaten in quite some time. He swallowed down his saliva and ignored every instinct telling him to get the fuck out of the area. He had to stay and help as much as he could. Clearly no one else would. Once Homelander saw his daughter was safely delivered and breathing, felt her laid out on his chest, something that had buoyed him up all that time seemed to release. Butcher watched as his head fell back, his pale face relaxed, mouth hanging slightly agape, and eyes rolling up, whites still visible because his lids never fully closed. ‘Is he alright?!’ he shouted at the midwives who were still keeping their distance, staring at him with wide eyes. There was so much blood that all the bedding below Homelander’s waist was soaked through with crimson. ‘This a normal amount of blood to come out?!’ he shouted at them as he picked Lena back up, paranoid that his partner was about to stop breathing, staring at the way the blood was still flowing out. The placenta was a mass of amorphous red flesh, umbilical cord pulsating occasionally, still attached to the infant in his arms. There’d be no way for any of them to cut the cord, Butcher realized, unless Homelander woke up and did the honors. He laughed at the thought, maybe to keep himself from crying.

Homelander was still breathing, but Butcher’s sleep-deprived, addled mind immediately went to the darkest places. Maybe he got what he wished for, he thought morosely. Fate wouldn’t let him enjoy a victory over Homelander when he was struggling to kill him, of course. No, it would take Homelander’s life now, when Butcher least wanted it to happen. Butcher always figured a supe like him would survive just about anything, but bleeding out from a new organ was not a vulnerability he had considered on the list of potential ways to try to kill his nemesis. 

The midwives approached cautiously, still looking askance at Lena. They were worried Homelander had gone into shock. Testing his blood with the blood type kit, it reacted with everything, so even if Sonnenberg managed to mold skin and a vein to accept a needle, he couldn't take an O negative transfusion. She pulled up a chair to sit beside the bed, working to patch up where the placenta had been attached and where Lena scorched him with her lasers on the way out. Just to stanch the blood flow, she said. No, she couldn’t move the blood back into him, she told Butcher when he asked. She could build conduits for blood but not move blood against physics.

Butcher tried to rouse Homelander as best as he could, tapping him lightly across the cheek and shouting ‘John’ a few times to no avail, feeling self-conscious using what felt like a secret name between them in front of strangers. Butcher wasn’t about to hit his long-suffering unconscious partner across the face even if he knew he couldn’t do any real damage. It just felt wrong. Homelander came to eventually when Butcher started wiping his face with a damp washcloth. It was probably less than ten minutes that he was out for the count, but it felt like hours. Butcher sat there beside him, holding Lena in the crook of one arm, wiping him off with paper towels. The midwives started plying Homelander with isotonics and water non-stop, to at least restore blood volume and salts if not the blood itself.

A lot of that lost blood had ended up on Butcher. Their bedroom looked like a crime scene. Butcher had to wash himself off for a while, and continued to find random stray splatters of blood on the floor and walls of their bedroom. The shirt he wore during delivery, all the sheets, and the towels they wadded up and packed between Homelander’s legs once the placenta was delivered were lost causes and he just threw them away rather than bother to clean them.  They’ll probably have to repaint the bedroom because Butcher still can’t scrub it out of the plaster in some spots.

“Okay, I think she’s lost interest,” Homelander says as he tries to switch her over to the other nipple and Lena doesn’t even bother latching on. He hands her over to Butcher. Butcher was afraid to handle her the first few times she was in his arms, but he’s already gotten used to it. It’s his job to pace around with her upright, patting her back, feeling her rut her nose into the soft burp cloth he drapes over his shoulder, waiting to hear her spit up a bubble of mostly air with a little bit of milk. Once that's out, he switches her over to lie in his arms, rocking her gently while pacing back and forth.

Butcher thinks about handing her back but sees that Homelander is still fussing with the nursing pads and custom made bralet he has from some company that made him a whole set in his size. He hisses and curses before flinging one of the pads down. Although his milk supply has been adequate, Lena had a hard time latching on and sucked aggressively to the point where Homelander’s nipples became cracked and red.

“You really don’t gotta put those on if they hurt.”

“I leak,” Homelander retorts. “You want the whole bed damp with milk? Besides, I’ll have to go out in public some day, you know.” And the waterworks start. Over not much, as usual, Butcher sighs.

“So let the bed get wet, love, it’s not worth crying over.”

“Not to you maybe! I want to be able to go back to public life at some point!”

Butcher sighs, making sure not to roll his eyes, because Homelander will see it, even in the dark. “Then just keep all the pads and bras and shit on during the day. Let them rest during the night, maybe they’ll heal. I can lay a towel under you if you’re worried about lying in a damp spot.”

“You don’t think a towel will feel like fucking sandpaper on these?” Homelander flings the nursing pads away in frustration and points to his nipples. Butcher thinks he’s probably supposed to see how badly inflamed they look, but he can’t make much out in the weak ambient light from the moon and the city coming through the window..

“Under your back, I meant. You lie on your back, nips out. If you leak, you leak.”

“Everything’s going to smell like milk,” Homelander says, sniffling. 

Butcher can’t help but tilt his head and raise a skeptical eyebrow.

Homelander seems to finally catch on that his is probably not a normal reaction. “Am I being hysterical?”

“Just a little. Over theoretical spilled milk, no less.”

Homelander wipes at his eyes. “I don’t have the baby blues. I’ve just been through a lot.”

Butcher shakes his head. “I’d never dispute that, love. You can cry if it makes you feel better.” He’s fairly sure it’s the baby blues. Homelander’s mood was better right after delivery, despite how truly incapacitated, how dazed and delirious he was. But maybe it’s a slow onset depression that has more to do with being bed bound than giving birth.

“My head hurts,” Homelander sniffles. “My head hasn’t hurt since childhood and now it hurts all the time.”

“The doctor told you, it’s the low blood pressure. Lie back and and rest.”

It’s a funny thing, or maybe a sad thing, watching Homelander struggle to come to terms with having lost so much blood that it’s affecting his ability to function. The first time he tried to stand up and walk to the toilet instead of pissing in a bottle like Butcher had offered, he nearly fell over, breathing hard, heart working overtime. He needed Butcher to escort him and piss sitting down. ‘Orthostatic hypotension’ Sonnenberg told them, even as she was packing up her stuff to finally take her leave while Homelander was holding on to Butcher’s shoulders to steady himself. ‘You’ve lost a lot of blood. You really should stay horizontal for a while, regain your strength, take some iron supplements.’ At least Homelander took the advice and has stayed in bed almost the whole time since. Lena stays near him at all times too, on his chest, skin to skin, or sometimes on the mattress beside him. Homelander nurses her, naps with her, and talks to her all in pretty much the same pose.  She doesn’t cry very often– not like Butcher expected of a newborn—usually only to signal that she wants to eat or be burped or changed, and thankfully none of these scenarios are accompanied by any eyelasers.

As the up-and-about partner, Butcher mastered changing her diaper and dressing her in tiny onesies. He worries, of course. Worries that she’ll start flying around the room once she remembers what she used to get up to earlier in the pregnancy and realizes she has more space to work with. Worries that he might get lasered in the face unexpectedly, but the only damage he’s suffered from her so far is getting peed on during a diaper change. 

He still helps Homelander with every trip to the bathroom, and he tries his best to cook nutritious food to help his partner get back on his feet. It’s been more than a full-time job, but Butcher has probably never felt this much purpose in his life before. He feels some level of guilt at seeing his partner having such a difficult time because Lena is a pleasure Butcher never expected to experience quite so viscerally. As soon as she gave that first weak bleating newborn whimper in his arms, and just as he felt immense relief that she was going to make it, he started to feel an overwhelming sense of attachment. Was his fate really to become one of those insufferable parents who see their child as god’s gift to the world? It certainly feels like he’s headed in that direction. Lena looks perfect to him. Homelander seems genuinely upset that she came out coneheaded and with a few burst blood vessels on her face, which Butcher hadn’t even noticed until Homelander pointed it out to him. 

“I’ll just wait for her to recover before I take a picture for social media,” Homelander told him that first day. Butcher gritted his teeth but said nothing about how he felt plastering their child’s face online. For better or worse, Homelander seems to have clean forgotten about posting on social media as his own recovery stretches longer than he expects.

To Butcher’s mind, all babies looked pretty similar, and the fact that Lena can squirm her way up Homelander’s body, lift her head up and attach to a nipple right from the get-go is much more remarkable than her appearance. He’s filmed video of this feat. Homelander is determined to nurse her, and so far things were going smoothly even though Butcher had his doubts about what kind of milk supply he might have when his chest barely changed through the pregnancy. It seems miraculous that he can barely stand but still producing milk.

Lena, who had fallen asleep in his arms, starts grimacing and crying, writhing her limbs. Homelander immediately perks up and extends his arms out. Whatever depression he’s in, it hasn’t affected his focus on their new child. 

Butcher shakes his head. “She’s taking a poo. I’ll change her nappies and then bring her back.”

They have a changing table in the nursery room next door that Lena has yet to sleep in. Butcher takes her there only to change her, knowing full well the gaze of his partner is following him through the wall.

“Alright. Let’s see what you’ve made for us this hour…” he mutters as he paws around on the shelf underneath for a new diaper.

"It's yellow, right?" He hears from the other room.

"Sure is!" Butcher shouts back. Then he leans over her as he’s changing her, cooing stupid baby talk about being so glad she doesn’t seem to get diaper rash. She’s staring at him wide-eyed, too young to have reasonable facial expressions that convey her mood, but clearly interested.

“Stop leaning over her,” Butcher suddenly hears from the other room.

“Why?”

“And stop turning away from her. Pay attention!”

Butcher rolls his eyes and finishes changing her before bringing her back into Homelander’s arms and then going back to the other side of the bed. “What do you think is gonna happen if I lean over her?”

“You know very well what. It just makes me nervous,” Homelander mutters, turning on his side to face her.

“I change her, what, ten times a day? What do you think’s gonna happen?”

“I just had a dream that she killed you. Happy?!” Homelander answers sharply and Butcher can tell he’s started weeping silently again. "You can't just do it for my sake?"

“Alright, alright. I promise to be careful,” Butcher says, spooning up behind him and nuzzling the nape of his neck. “Don’t scare the baby.”

“Why don’t I feel happier?” Homelander sniffles. “This is everything I wanted.”

Butcher bites his tongue to avoid saying ‘baby blues’ and asks “You’re not happy with her?”

“No, I am! She’s a dream.”

“Maybe you’re just taking on too much, trying to nurse her and all-”

“No, I love nursing her!” Homelander snaps, and Butcher is beginning to see that this is not going to be a very productive conversation.

“Maybe you’re just not feeling well, love. Happens to all of us, but you seem real impatient with yourself.”

“Maybe,” Homelander finally concedes.

“You’re still bleeding. You lost a lot of blood. Give yourself some grace.”

“I need you to do so many things. I just feel usele–”

“Give me a fucking break. You’re doing an amazing job. You gave birth without drugs, no medical care, to a baby who was not eager to come out. You’re feeding her day and night. Look at what a calm, happy baby she is. She’s perfect. That’s all on you.”

Flattery finally does its job, and Homelander doesn’t have a ready retort. Yes, preen away, Butcher thinks. You deserve it, even as he falls right back asleep, exhausted.

 

July 9th, 2023

“It’s another great morning with Vought & Friends. Let’s start with one of the topics that’s been trending on social media this week. The search for ‘John’ or the super formerly known as Homelander.”

“Is he really missing or is this just people online freaking out over nothing again?”

“So it is true in the sense that there really has been radio silence on his social media accounts since July 2nd, and the #whereisjohn hashtag started trending the day before yesterday.”

“He was due to give birth around this time though, wasn’t he?”

“That’s what people have been speculating, that something went wrong.”

“We should add a blanket disclaimer here, that if ‘John’ or his baby are really having any kind of health issues, we are very sorry.”

“But I wish these famous supers would realize that it would be helpful to release some kind of statement to let the public know.”

“Last time he disappeared for a while it was a mental health issue, but at least Vought Superhero Management had the courtesy to tell people that he was going to be away, grieving.”

“And even then, it was a bit of a cover, wasn’t it? He emerges a year later with transition surgery, a pregnancy announcement, and then breaks ties with Vought. It’s been a spectacular implosion.”

“Did he ever come out and say who’s, uh, been collaborating with him on this?”

“I don’t think so, but he’s been photographed together with the guy… what’s his name. God, I can’t remember names anymore, it’s on the tip of my tongue. The guy who blew up that Vought executive, Madelyn Stillwell and her baby.”

“Wait, him ? I never connected that that’s the same person.”

“No, it definitely is. Billy Butcher. That’s the name.”

“Well that’s just bizarre.”

“He never served time in prison because I guess he got acquitted. Or maybe pardoned. He works with the FBSA, so I think that might be part of the reason Vought canned Homelan- I’m sorry, the super formerly known as Homelander.”

“Oh you think he got fired?”

“Of course he was. That whole announcement for TV was him saving face and the FBI trying to claim a win. But it was Vought who didn’t want anything to do with someone that volatile.”

“But I think he announced the pregnancy after already leaving Vought. If I recall.”

“I am 100% sure people at Vought knew. And I’m sure they were worried. What was he going to do next? He seems to be living together with the felon.”

“Oh yeah?”

“Yeah, upper west side, right on Central Park. It’s not much of a secret. You just watch, he’ll emerge after this absence crossdressing and named Jane.”

“Stop it. Haha!”

“I’m sure they allow the supers some leeway, but you can’t just go off the deep end like that. They have an image to maintain.”

“Someone that powerful but emotionally unstable is an unsettling thought.”

“And what do you make of the rumors that he left Vought because they were controlling him and had raised him since childhood?”

“I mean that’s just- that’s probably the funniest rumor yet. Why would they raise him? Just because people can’t find much online about him? Newsflash: people born before 2000 don’t usually have a giant digital footprint from their childhood.”

“I think it was people speculating because in the leaked court documents he supposedly doesn’t have a last name.”

“You mean that he was listed as ‘John Doe’? The PDF I saw was only the first few pages, and it’s not clear if those are even authentic. Looked like someone’s overactive imagination to me. But even if those are real pages, the FBI are probably just trying to keep him anonymous.”

“I’m just telling all of you what the evidence being cited online is. Don’t shoot the messenger.”

“But let’s just think logically. Even if they did raise him, why wouldn’t he have a last name? And let’s just say, if they raised him and if they didn’t give him one, couldn’t he just take one as an adult? Conspiracy theories have to make a little more sense than that, right?”

“That’s true.”

“And if they adopted him from an orphanage, that would honestly be a philanthropic gesture, wouldn’t it? Imagine the amazing connections you could make before your career even starts. This John guy probably has the most reason to thank Vought out of anyone they’ve employed if that's true.”

“And he did have an amazing career while things were good.”

“It’s true, they gave him a lot of support until it was just too much to explain away, I guess.”

“Anyway, we still love you, John. Make a social media post, people are worrying about you.”

~~~

Butcher has been shaking his head the entirety of the clip. “What a load of steaming hot rubbish. Don’t know why you had to watch that whole thing. Didn't I tell ya to stay off social media?”

“That wasn’t social media, that’s live TV on VNN in a top morning slot!”

“Oh! Well now I see why you care. All those grannies who were awake at that hour watched it.”

“No, it’s being shared by everyone on social media. And #whereisjohn really is trending.”

“What’re you doing now…” Butcher asks wearily as he sees Homelander typing away furiously on his phone.

“I’m going to arrange to do an interview with a high end network that's not VNN, and then I’m gonna pick out the cutest onesie Lena has and take a picture of her in her crib to prove everything’s fine with me.”

“The crib she’s never used? John, come on. You have to be able to see that this is just Vought baiting you to do exactly what you’re doing.”

“And what’s that,” Homelander mutters, largely distracted by what he’s doing on his phone.

“They want you to come out and start talking about Vought and why everything they’re saying is wrong.”

“So? What am I supposed to do? Not respond? Just stay off social media and not talk to anyone? Let them say Vought was so kind to me?”

“They want you to clap back. You say a thing about Vought in an interview with anyone, and they’ll bring it up as you enriching yourself off of a sobstory. And then they’ll try to prove that means you fabricated the story, I guarantee you.”

Homelander pauses and chews his lip in contemplation for a moment. “I can still talk about Lena, can’t I? Why can’t I share how happy I am with the world?”

“You sure you want them to see you like this?” Butcher asks, hoping to appeal to his vanity to dissuade him. 

“Like what,” Homelander snaps. “Hm? Like what? Are you saying I look bad?”

“I’m just saying you look like you’ve been through something.” Butcher doesn’t know why he has to have an argument with someone who can barely stand up about not doing public interviews.

Homelander turns on the front camera to stare at himself. He doesn’t spend too long on it before throwing the sheet off his body, and bringing his phone down, angling it awkwardly.

“What the hell are you…” Butcher can’t help but blurt out before realizing. “Checking the undercarriage are we?”

“Just trying to see what I look like down there,” Homelander says, frowning, lifting up his leg trying to get a better view. “And I look terrible.”

“You look fine,” Butcher mutters and pushes his hand against the phone to bring it back upward. “Careful now, you gonna snap a picture and upload it to your social media with one clumsy swipe. That’ll be quite the return to public life.”

Homelander rolls his eyes.

“Seriously, you look good down there! Much better than I dared hope.”

“Oh yeah, I’m sure it looks great ‘for what I’ve been through.’ ‘For my age.’ ” Homelander tears up again. “I can’t believe you think I don’t look good enough to go out in public.”

“That’s not at all what I said. Fine,” Butcher says, throwing his hands up in surrender. “Fine. Go ahead, arrange these interviews, take these photos, I don’t care. Just don’t fall into the trap of defending yourself against attacks that no one cares about except the Vought executives. Don’t say anything that’s going to let them off the hook later.”

Homelander sniffles, shrugs, and keeps scrolling through the new hashtag dedicated to him.

Butcher wants to forbid it, but he never managed to wean Homelander off of social media, or seeking public approval. In some ways, he wonders if his partner is even capable of being fully happy when there’s no one to show off his happiness to.

 

July 17th 

Butcher watches with a certain amount of dismay as an entire film crew from NNC descends on their apartment and sets up shop in their living room, mounting lights and reflecting umbrellas around two chairs semi-facing each other, and positioning several cameras to point at the chairs and avoid having the boom microphones suspended overhead in the frame. Homelander eventually emerges from their bedroom with Lena in his arms. She’s managing to sleep through all the commotion going on around her, even as an assistant fusses with adjusting Homelander’s shirt, and wiring a small backup mic under the collar, and another fixes his already perfectly coiffed hair to be just slightly more perfect.

It’s hard for Butcher to fathom why, but Homelander had been determined to get himself into fighting shape and doing publicity within a week of the whole ordeal. He might be smiling and easily holding court with the journalists. They’re overjoyed to have snagged this prize interview from what they think was a winning bid against VNN. Homelander looks genuinely pleased with the attention and the fuss, and Butcher won’t blame him for that, but he knows how much Vaseline Homelander put over his nipples before putting on the nursing pads, how he squeezed himself into shapewear to reduce the pooch in his lower stomach and keep a pad firmly in place so that blood wouldn’t leak through. He watches as Homelander sits down, gingerly, haltingly. Ostensibly to avoid waking the infant in his arms, but some of it must be because of the damage that’s still healing. His whole public-facing image feels held together by duct tape and sheer willpower.

“Want me to hold her?” Butcher offers, a little dismayed to see the makeup artist still touching up Homelander’s face, which is already covered in a thick cake of foundation that will probably look more natural after it gets balanced in post. “Don’t need our daughter getting dusted with the stuff they’re glamming you up with.”

Homelander remembers himself and looks down frantically, relieved that he can’t see any powders on Lena, smiles and hands her off. “It’ll just be a minute while they prep me. Do I look okay?”

Yeah, they covered up the dark circles under your eyes so you almost can’t tell you’ve been at death’s door recently , Butcher thinks, knowing not to say it out loud with others around. “Looks like your usual complexion, yeah.”

Homelander looks like he’s waiting for an addendum.

“Radiant as ever,” Butcher adds. Homelander rolls his eyes, but he’s smiling and it’s clearly the sort of flattery he wanted to hear.

Lena makes a noise and Butcher looks down at her. She’s staring at him. He has a suspicion she’s particularly intrigued by his beard moving when he’s talking. “You ready for your debut? You better behave. Don’t embarrass your daddy now— he’s worked so hard for this.”

“I can take her back,” Homelander reaches out once the makeup artist scuttles out of the way again. He casts his gaze down at Lena. “Don’t listen to him, you can behave however you want.”

“You still sure she needs to be on camera?” Butcher asks as he passes her tiny swaddled body back Homelander. 

Homelander gives him a weary, chastising look. Well, Butcher can’t help it. Yes, they already had this discussion earlier, but he’s still uneasy with his partner’s insatiable drive to put himself– and by extension his daughter– on public display. ‘She’s my greatest accomplishment,” Homelander declared, as if that was reason enough to display her. ‘Besides, it’s not like her face will be on camera. You won’t see anything but the blanket and the baby hat.’

“You gonna be okay? What if she gets cranky?”

“It’s not a live interview. We can pause any time,” Homelander says nonchalantly. “If you’re really worried you can stay and watch.”

“I am gonna stay and watch, thank you very much.”

Homelander raises his brows. “To make sure I don’t say anything about the Vought investigation? I told them everything about that is off-limits.”

“I wanna make sure they don’t pester you and end on time,” Butcher says, then gets closer and says quietly enough that no one in the room can hear, because he knows how jealously this supe guards his weaknesses in front of the public. “Listen, you get dizzy, you just look at me and say you need a break. I’ll come get you. No one will see you wobble.”

“I’ll be okay. I feel great.”

Butcher believes him. Once he set a date to go on camera, Homelander was stubborn and determined to get back his strength that he’s a different person than he was a mere week ago. Butcher has to concede– having this deadline was probably the best way to get him out of his depressed ennui. He finally let Butcher serve him what Aunt Judy recommended over the phone for recovery: cooked spinach, kidney beans, beef and chicken liver, bone broth, and fresh pressed carrot juice from a vegetable stand down on Amsterdam Ave. Homelander held his nose while eating and complained nonstop that this was some old wives' tale nonsense British people invented, and that Lena would start refusing his breastmilk because it would taste so bad, but even he had to admit that he started regaining his strength faster with that regimen. He started walking around the apartment, and worked himself up to have the stamina to stand in the shower. His headaches were still there, and his face still looked pale and sunken in, but there was a determined energy in everything he was doing, and he was looking forward to things again. Butcher will probably never understand this part of him, the part that gets excited to be in public and feeds so hungrily on approval. He just needs to give Homelander space to live that way.

Homelander looks at him, a little concerned by the faraway look and repeats “I’ll be fine, I promise.”

“Well, I’ll be here. And they better not make you cry.” Butcher says very quietly, out of everyone’s earshot again and kisses him on the cheek. “Vile stuff they put on you.”

“Don’t smudge it,” Homelander says, chuckling, looking back down at Lena who’s fallen back asleep.

Butcher moves back towards the far back wall when he notices that the crew seems to be waiting for him to step out of frame. Even as he watches Homelander arrange Lena more comfortably in his arms, making sure her face is not in the line of any of the bright lights, one of the camera crewmen approaches Butcher. “You’re the father, right?”

“What’s it to you,” Butcher grumbles, but feels Homelander’s piercing gaze land on him, even before he looks to meet it. Of course this supe hears everything in the room. Butcher’s not sure if most people are privy to that. “Yes, I’m the other father,” he corrects himself, and Homelander looks away to start bantering with Andrea Canning, who's now seated in the chair across from him, preparing to start.

“We just need your signature for using some of the photos that Homel- John has put out on social media that include you.” The crewman hands Butcher a clipboard with a form.

“Well if John wants it.” Butcher takes the clipboard, and realizes he’s not sarcastic despite how he may sound.

Andrea throws Homelander a bunch of feel good softballs at the beginning, and gives him a chance to talk about what it was like to finally be a parent. The birth itself is glossed over in a couple of questions, and part of Butcher can’t stand watching him smile and say it was a breeze and “done at home for less fuss”, but another part of him smirks and admires him for this level of denial. 

The interview is slated to run about twenty minutes in the final cut, and it’s a legitimate news channel which means they are looking for substance, clearly hankering for something newsworthy.  Despite the supposedly clear guidance that no questions about the Vought investigation will be answered, Homelander deflects a couple before finally relenting on one, which threatens to open the floodgates. Butcher grits his teeth, wondering if he should intervene, but decides to listen until it gets worse.

“I know you’re not at liberty to talk about the investigation into Vought, but can you confirm you’re a witness for the prosecution?”

Homelander blinks, and pulls his smile tighter. “I can confirm I’m a witness, and I can confirm I’m being called by the prosecution, yes.”

Andrea clearly mulls how to phrase the next question. “It’s pretty well established by now that there are human rights violations that some individuals at Vought are going to be charged with. Are those the reasons that you left Vought?”

Butcher coughs, and sees Homelander glance his way before turning his gaze back to the camera.

“I left Vought over irreconcilable differences. They were not directly related to any charges.”

“Irreconcilable differences over…”

“Over the vision for my future life.”

“Did you want out of the superhero life?”

Homelander pauses again, throws a glance at Butcher, before recomposing himself. “I never wanted out of the superhero life. I won’t rule out returning to it at some point, if such a job exists in the future.”

“But not under Vought?”

“No.” Homelander says emphatically enough that Butcher can’t help but feel some pride. It still hasn’t gotten old hearing this rejection.

“In the event that Vought is broken up or goes under, do you feel like the rights of supers like you and your daughter might be in jeopardy, given that some members of Congress want to put limitations on the types of jobs supers can occupy?”

Homelander visibly hesitates. “I'm not an expert on the legislation being discussed. I'm obviously against it, and I think it's very strange for the liberal side to be proposing it. But I think losing the Vought lobby will affect much more than just that piece of legislation.”

“Is it true that Vought patented your DNA and wanted to claim that any children you have are illegal copies but then dropped the lawsuit–”

“Could we stop talking about Vought?” Homelander cuts her off, but smiles amiably enough. “They were a very important part of my life for a very long time, but not in the past year. They are playing no role in my life right now.”

Andrea moves right on to what’s usually been a landmine subject, and Butcher starts wondering if they shouldn’t have granted this interview to VNN after all.

“It was quite surprising to see a celebrity whose brand was so distinctly masculine opt to have a child this way,” Andrea says, gesturing vaguely at him holding Lena. “How would you characterize the decision to abandon the masculine image?”

“Just to be clear, I don’t think having a child changes anything about my image, and I do not consider myself anywhere along the gender dysphoric or transgender spectrum,” Homelander starts saying, but pauses and slowly turns to the crew and asks if they can redact the answer and if he can start over.

“So…” Homelander swallows. “I have never experienced gender dysphoria. But I experienced dysphoria about not having another chance to have a child. I haven’t talked publicly about this before, but I made many attempts to have children in the traditional ways. When those failed and I realized I could try this unconventional route, I didn’t think much about any of the… ramifications, shall we say. I didn’t think about it as fundamentally changing who I am, or my gender, or my orientation, or any of those things. I was just solving the problem of how to have a child. At the time I considered myself straight as well, and it’s strange to think about now, but I sought out what I thought was just a practical arrangement.”

“Does that mean that you weren’t interested-”

Homelander cuts her off. “Being honest with myself, as soon as I considered whom I might ask for this arrangement, only one person instantly came to mind. William Butcher and I go back aways, and not in very good ways I should admit, but… I have to be honest with myself. There was an element of attraction there from the beginning, at least for my part, I can't speak for him. Maybe an element that I didn’t fully acknowledge at the time.”

“And now you consider yourself…?”

“Oh, bisexual all the way. It sounds strange given how much I’ve ended up enjoying a relationship with a man, but I just never considered the possibility earlier. And hey– I don’t know if this is "fit to print" on your Dateline show or whatever– but getting myself new ‘equipment’ opened up a whole world of pleasure and … I guess I’ll call it self-expression. It’s changed my life. I’ve never felt so fulfilled with my body and my emotional life, and that was even before becoming a parent. And William had the patience of a saint for so many reasons, still has the patience and forgiven me so much. No one has ever treated me so well in my whole life, and he owes me absolutely nothing. Less than nothing. When I proposed having a child, I had no idea how much more I would get. William opened my eyes to a lot of flaws in the way I lived and I would never have been brave enough to do what I’m doing right now without Vought’s support.”

What the hell are you going on about? Butcher thinks in a panic, and can’t even cough to try to stop this turn of the interview because his mouth has gone completely dry and his lips feel clamped shut.

“So William Butcher... you said you knew each other before? He's involved in the Vought investigation, right?”

“I can't talk about Vought,” Homelander interjects. “Go to a different question.”

Andrea has a little bit of a deer in the headlights look but isn’t at a complete loss for words. “Wow, that sounds complicated and sweet all at once. So you'd consider yourself cis and bisexual?”

“If you have to put a label on it,” Homelander says shrugging. “But what I wanted to say is that I think people should be allowed to express themselves however they want, and feel liberated. I’m not a spokesperson for the trans community, because I don’t consider myself trans, but I don’t think I’ve been supportive enough vocally. I can completely understand wanting a certain type of hormone mix in your body. Honestly, I miss being pregnant right now.”

“Oh, has it been a letdown since?” Andrea asks.

“It’s been a rollercoaster for sure,” Homelander says, with a sad sort of chuckle. “I loved being pregnant. I think I have withdrawal.”

“I remember that. I’ve had six children myself,” she says, laughing and looking relieved after probably feeling like the interview was getting away from her.

“Six?” Homelander asks blinking. “I have to admit, I’m thinking about having another one, but right now it’s too overwhelming to plan.”

Butcher hears his heart thumping in his ears, and tries to will it to calm down, not wanting his partner to get distracted.

When things were mostly wrapped up with the birth, and Lena was nursing consistently, Homelander paid the two midwives a very generous sum for being on the house call for so long, but made them sign an NDA to avoid gossiping to any news outlet or TMZ about what they saw. Sonnenberg waved him off when he apologized profusely for being unable to pay her the originally agreed upon milestone payments of millions of dollars, and said she looked forward to seeing how he was going to live his post-Vought life. What Homelander doesn't know is she texted Butcher privately saying she wasn’t sure if some of the injuries Homelander sustained during birth might affect fertility going forward. Butcher figured they can worry about that bridge being burned if they ever even revisit it. 

The rest of the interview feels much more congenial, like the ice is broken, and proceeds smoothly. Lena starts to fuss right towards the end of the questions and they decide to wrap up rather than wait for a feeding before resuming. As the crew is packing up, Homelander goes into the bedroom. Butcher follows, seeing if he needs help, but Homelander is just quickly undressing. Lena is crying on their bed, indignant at having been abandoned just at her time of need.

Butcher picks her up and tries to soothe her by rocking but she's inconsolable now that she's hungry, and doesn't stop crying until she's handed back to Homelander.

Butcher checks that everything has been taken out of the apartment before coming back in.

“Did I say anything I shouldn’t have?” Homelander asks him without looking up, still watching Lena working hard at eating.

“No, I suppose not,” Butcher says, shrugging and lying down beside Homelander.

“Didn’t break down crying even once,” Homelander mutters, rearranging Lena to latch on left side, because she seems to have drained him on the right one. “But I heard your heart start going a mile a minute when I talked about you.”

“Just can’t cope with sap,” Butcher says, chuckling. “My problem, not yours. Those were nice things you said.”

“Well I won’t say them to you if you’re going to have a heart attack.”

“‘Sfine,” Butcher mumbles, kissing Lena’s head. “She’s so warm and red with the effort!”

“Oh I know,” Homelander says, sighing, stroking her tiny shoulder. “Think my milk comes slow and she gets frustrated.”

“She hurting you?” Butcher asks, kissing him on the temple.

“Just intense. It’s gotten better since my nipples healed. Maybe I should start pumping. We could freeze a reserve for her if she’s not getting enough. Trick my body into making more.”

Butcher watches as Lena passes out mid-suck, detaching and falling back against the crook of Homelander’s arm. He respositions her to lie on her stomach against his chest, tiny legs flexibly curled up under her diaper, tiny ribcage visibly moving in and out with each quick breath.

“How the hell do they make ‘em so tiny,” Butcher says, leaning over and kissing her again.

“Didn’t feel tiny on the way out,” Homelander grumbles, still studying her. “Do you think she’s not gaining weight fast enough? Am I starving her?”

“No, I don’t.”

“Why are you so sure?”

“Because I don’t know that much about infants, but I do know they cry when they don’t get enough.”

“What if it’s enough volume but not enough fat or something.” Homelander isn’t going to give up fretting.

“She’s fine.”

Butcher blinks as Homelander cups his hand around the nipple Lena just detached from, and starts expressing milk into the palm of his other hand for a few squeezes, then brings it up to his mouth to sample. “It’s like… watery,” he says, licking his lips.

“Johnny. Did you just… test if your milk is good by tasting it?”

Homelander turns to look at him, frowning. “And how else am I gonna know what she’s getting?”

Butcher shakes his head. “Think you should trust your body and trust her body to know what’s what.”

“Her eyes used to light up red when she was feeding. Doesn’t happen anymore. Maybe she doesn’t like it.”

Butcher remembers that all too well. The first night after the birth, after changing all the bedding, Homelander was still groaning in pain periodically, and Butcher was in a delirious half-sleep half-waking state next to him. He’d wake up and just see eyes glowing red in the darkness and the quiet sound of sucking while Homelander made suppressed moaning noises because the nursing hurt him more in those early days.

“What if she’s just less powered now.” Butcher says, watching her tiny face, her nostrils flaring, and her long eyelashes twitching as she’s clearly dreaming something. “No more compound V from you, no more precocious powers.” He catches himself, realizing he’d be relieved, but also realizing Homelander probably won’t be happy with that explanation.

But Homelander only mumbles “Let’s hope so,” patting her back gently.

Chapter 17: October 18, 2023

Chapter Notes

Sorry for the delay, but at least it's updated!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

John lands down in front of the Hart building to hundreds of camera clicks, his public smile already locked and loaded. Doors are supposed to open at 7:30 am, but he must be a bit early because there's still a stanchion in front of the glass door and a security guard peering through at the crowd of people already gathered outside. There are a lot of reporters and photographers behind a metal crowd control barrier. 

Quite a few non-press staunch supporters have dragged themselves here at this early hour with handmade posterboard signs with messages of support ranging from 'Vought lied People died' to 'Homelander is a name not a trademark'. He flinches when he sees one poster emblazoned with 'End human experimentation' across one of the blurry grayscale CCTV images taken from overhead that leaked online. He must be all of five years old, sitting against one of the walls in the bad room, hugging his knees.

"We love you Homelander, with or without Vought!" one of the younger fans screams.

John recovers his smile and waves.

"You don't gotta look so chipper about this." Billy's voice cuts through the cacophony of camera shutters and general crowd noise. John hears him before he spots him in the crowd, blended in and inconspicuous, even more so than usual because he decided to go clean shaven for this occasion suddenly. Nobody else can hear him mutter under his breath, but he knows John will. John reduces his grin every so slightly. Maybe they don't want him to look cheerful before heading in, but he'll have plenty of time to look somber during the hearing.

The FBI wanted continuity, after all. They wanted him to look as much like his old self as possible, and that old self would certainly smile for the cameras. His hair's been bleached fresh a few days ago, styled slicked back, exactly the way he had it at Vought before leaving. There was no reassuring feeling of a weighty cape draped across his shoulders fluttering behind him as he landed, but at least he's wearing a blue suit and a red tie. Of course the suit is navy, and much darker than the cobalt blue he favored so much, and the tie is more of a burgundy than crimson, but the color scheme is an unmistakable reference to his old Homelander brand, and that's what the investigator side wants.

Some things have changed very noticeably though. He slightly readjusts the way Lena is sitting in his arms. She's staring at the people gathered behind the barrier, sucking on her fist. He could have sworn she had a pacifier in her mouth when he left the hotel room.

"Did you spit your pacifier out somewhere?" he says to her in that mock-scolding singsong voice that comes out of him automatically because she pays much more attention to him that way, but it's not enough to distract her from the crowd. He picks up the edge of her bib to dab off some drool on her chin and attempts to separate her hand from her mouth, thinking it will make for nicer photos for the press. He thought wrong, because Lena is immediately upset and erupts into tears. John tries not to panic. All babies cry at inopportune times. But he doesn't want to see photos of himself with her crying in his arms all over the evening news.

He bounces her up and down gently, mulling over whether he should just retreat to the door and  beg to be let inside the building early. He knows reporters expect him to answer at least a few questions, but shouting over a crying baby is something he doesn't want to do. Some of them have press passes and will be at the hearing itself, but he guesses that the TMZs and National Enquirers are only here for the couple of words he'll say before heading in. And now they get to witness him looking like an incompetent parent instead.

"John."

John looks up just in time to see a clean pacifier whiz through the air and catches it with his free hand. Lena immediately quiets down and vigorously sucks on the pacifier as soon as he puts it in her mouth. 'Lifesaver' he mouths to Billy. 

A few of the reporters turn to look back briefly at who's throwing baby paraphernalia but all their interest is ultimately with John and they resume bombarding him with questions.

"How does it feel to finally be heading into this hearing?"

"Given how long this one kept getting postponed? I just feel relieved that it's finally happening." John pauses as a light chuckle runs through the crowd. "But it's sad of course. Sad to be testifying about my former employer, and the people who raised me."

"Are you scheduled to attend more than just today's hearing?"

"Senate Judiciary Committee's going to question me today, and tomorrow I'll be in front of a couple of House committees over at the Rayburn building."

"And nothing beyond that?"

"Nothing scheduled beyond that in DC, no. Thankfully I'm only being called in for the human rights prong of the investigation, not the accounting scandal and the anti-trust pieces. Fingers crossed." 

There's light laughter in the crowd of reporters, and John wonders if Billy's going to give him an earful later about the tone of his answers. But he can't help it– he's nervous, and if he doesn't laugh about the situation he finds himself in, his nerves are going to show.

There's zero chance these hearings will be the end of it for him, of course. The DOJ is preparing to file three separate cases against Vought. John just hopes to God he won't need to show up for anything involving the accounting irregularities because his eyes glaze over just reading the case outline. Lena might be old enough to go to school by the time that entire thing gets wrapped up.

But these congressional hearings are a really important appearance for him. They'll be televised publicly in their entirety, and his testimony is the event the public at large is most interested in. It will also involve a lot of off the cuff questions, the FBI warned him as they coached him through potential questions. Given how much money Vought pours into lobbying and how many members of congress they have in their pocket, the questions here could be more hostile than anything he faces in the courtroom later.

"Do you think Vought International will still be around by the time this is all through?" shouts one of the reporters.

John shrugs. "I can't possibly speak to that. It's been around for a long time." 'The house always wins,' Maeve used to say and he wonders if he's about to find that you should never bet against Vought.

"What's your preferred outcome here?"

"You don't have to answer every question you know," Billy tells him. 

John ignores him. "I have no preferred outcome. My preferred outcome is that no other child goes through what I went through."

Lena has amazing timing at losing interest about her surroundings. He feels her head rest on his shoulder, and there's an audible murmur of 'aw' in the crowd. He pats her back gently and pulls her closer in.

"Are you planning to take your baby into the hearing with you?" 

"I can try," John says, shrugging his shoulders innocently. "But there's a green room setup of some sort in there, as far as I've been told."

"Must be hard to get a sitter for a child with powers like hers?"

John smiles wider to hide the fact that he tenses, but mercifully the glass door behind him opens, and a security guard motions everyone in, just in time to save him from having to answer. "Thank you all, I'll see some of you inside."

John doesn't care for the implication of the question, but of course it's true. There are only a handful of people whom he'd entrust Lena to, and it's not clear if any of them would survive a lasering to the face. John thought about enlisting Kimiko's help for these couple of days. But Billy said he could handle Lena, however long the hearings took, instead of making a pregnant woman travel. 'Kimiko might be indestructible but her lil tyke ain't.'

That conversation got John into a recurring gloomy spiral, where he starts wondering who Lena might have as a friend growing up who'd share her… John almost says 'predicament' instead of 'abilities'. Sometimes he finds himself wishing he could shut Lena's powers off temporarily. Times like now, when he worries about how long the hearing will take and how she'll behave. Maybe he should have left Billy with her in New York and made the commute alone. Maybe the entire idea of coming to DC together was a bad idea, but he can't stand being that far away from her.

He's so lost in thought he barely registers that he's set off the metal detector while walking through it.

"Sir, can you remove your jacket? Sometimes it's just the buttons or the cufflinks."

John gives the security guard a tired incredulous look, but protocol is protocol. He starts taking off his jacket– awkwardly because he's still juggling Lena in his arms– but Billy finally catches up with him by cutting through the line, and takes Lena off his hands. 

"I'm so glad they checked that I'm not bringing in anything dangerous like a gun," John says, rolling his eyes as they're walking down the hallway, buttoning his jacket back up and redoing his sleeves.

Billy chuckles quietly.

They're shown into a small room with a couch and a TV screen that will be showing the live proceedings going on just down the hallway. Billy sits down and seats Lena on his knees, bouncing her up and down slightly, before letting her slightly fall through between them, setting off a nervous giggle from her.

John watches them with a sour expression. "I hate it when you play with her like that."

"Why?"

"You're startling her."

"She'll be alright," Billy says bringing her closer and kissing her forehead even as she starts touching his face.

"I'm not worried about her," John mutters under his breath. He's getting more and more nervous and paces around the tiny room. "You have the bottles I pumped this morning?"

"Yeah. And some extra from yesterday."

"And diapers?"

"Yeah."

"More than one, right?"

Billy gives him a look. "Yeah, we’re all set I think."

"I packed wetwipes. Looks like there's a diaper changing station in the bathroom all the way down the hallway if you don't want to do it in here. Did you bring her some toys?"

Billy sighs. "I brought her favorites."

"Sometimes she just wants water. Did you bring a bottle of water?"

"Yes Johnny, as a matter of fact I did, because you already told me to bring it three times this morning," Billy says in a tone that is very clearly aggravated with all the questions but John isn't convinced he has everything he needs.

"Did you bring a separate bottle head? Sometimes she doesn't like when there's a little bit of milk in the water bottle."

"Yes I have extras in the bag somewhere."

"Well let me take everything out so you don't have to rummage through," John says, laying out various ziplocked parts on the small coffee table.

"Love."

"What! She's started to get fussy a lot, really randomly too. I think her teeth are starting to come in. If she gets cranky and nothing else is working, try going under the zinc blanket with her. I think she gets overstimulated by seeing everything sometimes. She woke up around 6 so she'll probably get tired around 10. But I don't want you watching this thing unfold and getting all riled up. She hears your heartbeat and all that. She won't fall asleep if she can sense you're–"

"Love. We'll be alright. And if we're not, I'm sure you'll hear her loud and clear. You can excuse yourself and come to my rescue. I ain't worried."

John finally sits down, and he sees that his knee is shaking. But he also sees Billy's knee shaking, even now that he's not bouncing Lena up and down on it. They’re both on edge, apparently.

"You are worried." John says in a more accusatory tone than he wanted.

"Worried for you, yeah," Billy says. "Worried about you."

"I already know they're planning to grill me." 

"Yeah, there's a good number of people on that committee who probably got elected because Vought contributed to their campaign. So buckle up."

"I know. I know all that. They're going to question why I didn't leave the fold earlier. They're going to ask why I lied about my origins before and why they should believe me now. They're going to say I'm just a disgruntled former employee. I know all that."

"They might get nasty about your relationship with someone on the FBI roster in the investigation."

"Yeah, well, I'll answer all that as best I can."

"Do you have your opening statement printout?"

John rolls his eyes as he reaches into his jacket pocket. "Yes, I have it right here."

Billy chuckles. "You can't roll your eyes at me after you interrogated me about damn near every single thing in that diaper bag."

John shrugs, looking over the printout briefly before folding it and putting it back in his pocket.

"Just don't lose your cool. Don't laser anyone, even if they're being a complete bellend."

"Can't promise anything." John shrugs. "Are we sure we need all hundred senators, really?"

Billy smiles. He leans over and kisses him and a lot of John's worries thankfully melt into the background hum of worry, the background hum of being able to hear people gathering in the hearing room a few doors down.

"She's watching us like a hawk," Billy says, laughing, as he breaks away from the kiss. "Look at her, all serious. 'The hell are you two doing?' seems to be saying"

"She's probably still disturbed by your lack of beard," John says. "As am I, if I'm being honest. Feels weird"

Billy laughs again, swiping his hand across his chin. "If you two really dislike it so much, it'll grow back in no time."

John dives back in for another kiss, a little too eager, to the point that he pushes Billy down to lie underneath him. Maybe it's the nerves but he feels a frantic urge to do more, despite Lena being right there, also lying on the couch, Billy's arm still protectively guarding her from the edge.

"Love, you'll be called to go out there any minute now," Billy warns him, no doubt feeling the John's hips grind against him.

John nods, clambering off and taking deep nervous breaths, trying to recompose himself.

"Does my hair look okay?"

"You look amazing. Real sharp."

"Yeah? Despite the Homelander colors?"

Billy chuckles. "I never said I didn't like the Homelander colors."

"Pretty sure you did. Pretty sure you didn't let me wear the suit inside your house."

"I don't want you wearing the suit. But the colors suit you."

"Well I didn't put Lena in the same colors at least," John says.

"No, she was a pretty speck of yellow on ya. They already got some photos up on the AP website." Billy shows him his phone and John can't help but smile. He's never completely happy with the way he looks but Lena looks picture-perfect perched on his hip, her tiny yellow dress contrasting nicely with the navy of his suit. 

"Surprised you're not annoyed that her face is in the news."

Billy sighs. "I know the FBI asked for it. Maximize your likability and all that." 

"You didn't argue with them when they asked for it," John points out, doing some last minute adjustments of his hair in a tiny mirror he found in the room.

"It's a lost cause anyway. I know you wanna show her off at every opportunity. Just don't raise her to be a snot-nosed little celebrity, is all I ask."

"I think that's up to you as much as it's up to me," John says, although he's not sure that's true, but he doesn't have time to think about it because someone knocks on the door before opening it and telling him they're ready for him.

 

***

The hearing is contentious. Every single senator is running over the time limit, so it's threatening to run long. Majority and minority senators keep switching off, so the questions keep ricocheting in tone – highly sympathetic to John and highly critical of Vought, or vice versa. Photographers and reporters are crouching on the floor near the dais in front, just out of view of the main camera. They're incessantly taking pictures and video of him as he answers, so John has to make sure he looks respectful and earnest and there's not even a moment where he might be caught rolling his eyes at a question.

It makes John uneasy that he can't see much of the green room through the walls in detail. He sees that Billy still has Lena in his arms. She's asleep by the sound of her even breathing, but she'll probably wake up from her nap soon. His chest is starting to feel uncomfortable with how much milk has built up over the last few hours, and he can feel that he's leaking slightly into the nursing pad on one side. Instead of looking down, he quick-checks the big screen projecting the camera pointed at him, satisfied that at least there's no sign of wet spots on his jacket. Lena makes a soft noise and his attention is directed completely towards her for a moment until he's satisfied she's still asleep.

"Mr. Doe." Sen. Grellong says impatiently and John realizes he missed a question entirely while focusing on Lena's breathing.

"He must've told you about Becca? It was such a big part of his life for a long while," Judy says. "Or maybe he's crossed that part of his life out completely?"

"I'm aware he was married before. But I don't know that much about his life before then," John says, watching Lena making squeaking noises as she makes the giraffe jump from rock to rock.

"He left home young," Judy says. "And after that, truth be told, we don't know much about his life either. He's so secretive that way."

"And when he was a boy he was a troublemaker," Connie says. "You'll have your hands full with little Lena if she takes after him in that sense. She does look like him quite a bit, but I see your face in her too. My Billy certainly didn't have those round blue eyes."

John wondered if Lena's eyes would darken from the color she was born with, but they've stayed the same color as his, probably set for life now. He looks at Connie and notices that she has blue eyes.

"Billy didn't have a happy childhood though. I think that made all his behavior worse. She's not growing up like that."

John nods.

Connie remembers herself. "Oh I mean, Billy's was nothing as bad as your childhood. I heard about some of those awful things they did to you. Just awful. It's hard to believe the company still exists."

"Yeah but it's only a shell of itself now," Judy says. "Billy hated them. Becca worked for Vought, you know. He was convinced they were behind her death."

John nods stiffly.
