"What's the giraffe's name?" John asks, actually eager to get off the topic of Billy's past now, even though he's curious to hear certain bits and pieces.

"Aunt Judy, what's the giraffe's name?" Lena echoes the question.

"I didn't name him, sweet pea, you can name him whatever you like."

Lena has a very serious furrowed brow thinking face. "I name him…. Spot. Because he has spots."

"She's so clever!" Connie exclaims, and John can't help but be a little bit proud too. 

He has the giraffe on his knee, moving the toy around and putting on a voice to pretend it's talking. Lena gets so immersed in this imaginary play, and John wonders if he was already talking to his imaginary friend at this age. "Hi Lena, I'm Spot. Want to be friends?"

"I want to be friends! Best friends!" Lena shouts, a little over the top and John has to shush her.

She snatches the giraffe out of his hands and starts to hug it violently. 

"Gentle hugs! Only gentle," John reminds her and sees her let up on the squeezing.

"We've been thinking of getting her a P-U-P-P-Y," John says to the two women, spelling out a word he doesn't want Lena to overhear. "But I'm waiting for her to learn to be more consistently gentle."

As if on cue, Lena flings the giraffe high in the air, clearly heading toward the lake. John launches himself in the air and catches the giraffe before it has a chance to get lost under the surface. Lena erupts into peals of laughter.

"It's not funny," John says. "You have to play nicely with things or you won't play with them at all." He lands back in his chair and puts the giraffe on the table.

"Oh you can't be so harsh on her," Judy says. "She's what? Just turned two? It's just a silly toy. I can sew another one for her."

"I need her to practice being gentle before it counts," John says.

Lena approaches the table, hands behind her back, which John knows is a sign she realizes she overstepped boundaries.

"Yes?" he addresses her.

"Can I play with Spot?" she asks.

"Are you going to throw him in the lake?" John asks her in turn.

She shakes her head no vigorously, and John hands it back to her.

"She's acting out more than usual. She's trying to impress you both," John says.

"Of course!" Judy smiles. "New people in the house, who're going to laugh at all the silly things she does. Relax."

And although John feels a smidgen of resentment over being told to relax by someone who could get accidentally pulverized by his daughter, it does give him a bit of permission to stop feeling judged about his parenting.

Billy emerges from the house with seasoned ground beef and proceeds to grill, John just grateful that the conversation is unlikely to return to the subject of Becca again now that he's outside.

"It's a really lovely place you two've got here," Connie says, looking around. "I saw some of it on Instagram, but mostly the indoors. The outdoors– I never realized the Catskills were so pretty. It's really like you're on holiday out here!"

"Thanks," John says, watching Lena run around making the giraffe 'fly' in a sinusoid pattern around the backyard. "We were looking for something remote for her early years. I'm partial to this kind of setting. Woods, lakes."

"Does it get cold in the winter?" Judy asks.

"Only affects me," Billy says as he waits for the first batch to cook on one side. "The two of them though… they can go make snow angels naked and be none the worse for it."

"We still have our apartment in New York for when we need it," John says. "But I like raising her out here."

"Certainly more room to run around and play," Judy says.

"Daddy can I have a tomahto?" Lena approaches Billy as he slices up other burger components.

"Yes, you may," Billy says, handing her a slice of the beefsteak tomato he just cut and she runs off, munching on it.

"She speaks to Billy in British, did you hear?" Judy nudges Connie.

Billy smirks. "Oh don't say that. John gets upset about it."

"I don't get upset about it. I just correct her if she's talking to me. That's what happens when you raise a child in seclusion."

"You sound a little upset about it…" Billy laughs but John throws a glare his way and he seems to catch on that this isn't something John wants to discuss with guests at the table.

Lena comes bounding back repeating "Luvvie" over and over again, and the way she tugs at her pants, John knows what she's asking, and takes her inside the house to go potty.

They have lunch, and the conversation is pleasant, although Lena often gets bored and wants more attention directed at her by the adults. John picks his battles and doesn't scold her for asking for more and more ketchup, and then eating it by dipping her finger into the puddle of it on her plate. At some point she turns to him and tugs on his sleeve.

"Luvvie is lunch over?"

John looks down at her, not sure what she wants. "What do you mean is it over? The grownups are still eating." Although at this point, the grownups have mostly moved on to drinking wine and beer that Billy brought out of the fridge.

Lena looks at him and purses her lips impatiently, as if she can't believe he forgot. "Can I have gestif biscuits?"

John rolls his eyes but smiles and nods.

"What an excellent memory you have," Aunt Judy praises her as she pulls out a long sleeve of the digestives. John eyes Lena, noticing how much she puffs up with praise. Maybe it's something innate in them, or maybe he and Billy have already inadvertently taught her to seek out approval and praise.

After having a few cookies, Lena gets antsy and rambunctious and climbs out of the chair she was sitting in to do sprints around them. John's not sure if he's tired from the tension of having guests or his period cramps, but he feels like he has a migraine coming on and Lena's squeals and laughter feel like they're making his head pound.

"Lena, it's time for your nap," he says, rubbing the bridge of his nose to stave off what feels like a migraine.

Lena doesn't stop running around, and when he stands up to catch her, takes off into the sky like a bullet.

"It's the sugar," Billy says. "You alright?"

"I'm fine," John says through gritted teeth and takes off after her. He lands back with Lena tucked under his arm, sounding a bit hysterical, laughing, crying, and kicking her feet, trying to extricate herself out of his hold on her.

"Leni, be good," Billy admonishes.

"I don't wanna nap! I don't wanna nap!" she yells, flailing her arms and legs.

Billy decides to come to the rescue. "Let's go put the giraffe down for a nap. Where's your giraffe? Where did he go?"

John lowers Lena to the ground, and she dutifully runs off to find the toy.

"Oh look how sleepy he is," Billy says once she brings the giraffe back to him, taking him and putting on a weird baby voice to yawn and say he's sleepy. "We gotta show him where the baby bed is, don't we?"

"He doesn't know!" Lena agrees.

"Can you show him where it is?" Billy says to her, then turns to John. "I'll take care of it. You go sit and rest."

"Be careful, she's hyper," John warns him, but he finds that Lena tends to act calmer around her other dad, as if she senses that there's just less leeway there. He heads back to sit with Jody and Connie as Billy takes Lena back into the house.

"Is he good with her?" Judy asks, and John nods.

"He was a real sweetheart after Lenny was born. Responsible too," Connie says. "Took right to taking care of him. Billy was only five and I could leave the two of them alone for hours and I knew Lenny was in good hands."

John nods, but wonders how often Billy was left in the capacity of babysitter when he was five.

"Is she taking up all of your time?" Connie asks. "Do you have any time left to yourselves?"

John shrugs and opens his mouth before closing it again, still thinking about what to say. "Billy drives to the city sometimes or works from home on the Vought lawsuits, but that's almost all wrapped up by now."

"Haven't you been doing something with politics?" Judy asks. "Feels like I see you on the news once in a while."

John wrinkles his nose. "Politics? No. I make a little side-money with social media, and the occasional public speaking when I need it, but I've been trying to keep all those commitments to a minimum until Lena's a little older."

"But didn't you fund all those renovations at that orphanage Vought used to run that was going to close?"

"Oh yeah, that facility was really rundown and sad. It's not too far from here," John says, gesturing in the vague direction. That was part of his recent goodwill tour, donating a large fraction of the money he was awarded from a civil suit against Vought into the orphanage that had become state-run. Maybe the philanthropy was something he was used to doing for show, but he did take a tour through the place and it chilled him to see the bleak conditions where the children were being raised. He donated the money without a second thought after visiting.

***

Lena acts more calm and like her old self again after Billy's relatives leave. John bathes her, and she plays with her bath toys quietly, not complaining even when water and shampoo get in her eyes as John washes her hair.

Right before bed is when John likes to practice 'lighting eyes' with her. When she's calm and relaxed, Lena just recently learned to power up her eyes at will.

John holds her rolled up in the towel and kisses her forehead. He caresses her face as he instructs her to light up her eyes, and they do it unison, looking at each other, on, off, on, off, on his instruction. At some point he'll start teaching her about sending the heat out and controlling the intensity, but for now he just wants her to have full control of the first step. Maybe it's bad of him to admit, but doing this makes him feel close to her– something only he and she share. It's something dangerous but it doesn't have to be if she's taught right. It's made him have fewer nightmares about her wreaking havoc with that power.

He changes Lena into pajamas and reads a short book to her, kissing her good night on the nose before turning off the light and heading back to the living room.

"Think I'm going to bed early," he tells Billy, feeling too weary to stay up.

Billy follows him into the bathroom, brushing his teeth alongside him, watching John take a piss and change out a tampon.  

"You doing okay?" he finally asks as John undresses for bed.

"Yeah, I'm fine. Why? Was I not acting friendly?"

Billy shakes his head. "No. I can just see that you're really tired."

"Well I do get tired worrying about Lena when there's people around."

"Eh, you shouldn't mind them. They're family. No need to put on airs around my mum. You can't even imagine how messy our home life was. This is like a fairytale compared to that."

"I'm not worried about them judging me, I worry about her doing something unpredictable."

"She's fine," Billy says, and John can't stand the dismissive tone, but is also grateful for how Billy always minimizes these worries. As if their daughter didn't break his finger when she couldn't even sit up on her own, and as if she didn't break his leg earlier this year when she came running into him full speed and happened to bash her head against his femur.

It's as if Billy reads his thoughts through his facial expression and adds, "You're doin' the best you can. She's behaving as well as any two year old I've seen. And she'll only get more consistent."

John sighs.

"I got zero worries about her around me mum and aunt. Zero," Billy says as he lies down next to him in the dark.

John squirms in discomfort and curls up in a fetal position.

"What is it? Cramps?" Billy asks, kissing his shoulder.

"Yeah. Started bothering me during the day and hasn't stopped."

"I see," Billy kisses further down his arm again. "I'll fix you a hot water bottle." 

The unspoken tension here is that although John's been hopeful to have another child, it's been almost ten months since they started trying again, to no avail. Every period feels doubly painful because it's yet another confirmed missed chance.

John won't complain about it out loud, though, because it sounds ungrateful and ridiculous. The birth was traumatic. Lena's a handful, and it's not like he's got everything under control. He should be fine with one and done. But somewhere deep inside him it feels wrong that Lena will grow up as an only child. He had always wanted a sibling so badly growing up.

Billy places the rubber hot water bottle on his belly. 

"Thank you," John says, turning onto his back again, waiting for the pain to subside or at least recede.

"Tomorrow's the anniversary," Billy says, and John nods. August 28th was the day his first child died. August 28th of the year after that was when Billy called him unsolicited, not knowing that would trigger a series of events that would lead them to become much more intimately acquainted. "You want to go visit his grave again this year?"

"Yeah, we should," John mumbles. After his body was discovered and photographed for evidence, Ryan was finally laid to rest in a cemetery near Scarsdale. They visited it the year before, when Lena was only one and tottering around, falling down often, but also intent on trying to touch every gravestone.

"I'll tell my mum to do something with Aunt Judy tomorrow, and we'll see them the day after. Sorry they'll keep visiting this week, but my mum hasn't seen me in years."

"You don't have to be sorry. I'm glad Lena has extended family. She loves them. I like them." John sighs. Even if he doesn't manage to have another child, Lena won't grow up as alone as he worried about. She has Billy's family. She has Billy's friends. And Compound V still hasn't been banned. Its proprietary formula and chemical synthesis got released to several laboratories that were doing animal studies now, seeing if they could tweak it to be safer or more consistent in its effects, although John doubts they'll discover anything that Vought hasn't already tried in the past decades. The major complaints about V now were from people obsessed with natural lifestyles (one of the leaked details about V was that the characteristic blue color came from ferric ferrocyanide, which although not toxic, sounded deadly) and from those who lamented that access to V had become even less democratized than it had been under Vought– now costing quite a bundle and requiring connections to obtain a dose for your child and no longer distributed somewhat randomly through rural and urban areas. But at least it was looking like Lena wouldn't be the last of her generation to have superpowers.

John starts to feel the urge, and weaves one of his legs between Billy's.

"Now? When you're in pain?" Billy asks, incredulous.

"Sometimes the pain goes away when we do it."

"Alright…" Billy gets up and fumbles for a towel from the closet in the dark. He lifts John's body and slides it underneath him, John not even bothering to float up and help, enjoying the sensation of being maneuvered and manhandled. He feels Billy pull the tampon out of him and slide inside. They only manage a few thrusts before John turns his head sharply to stare through the wall.

"Did she wake up?" Billy whispers, stopping his motions.

They stay silent until John relaxes again, satisfied that Lena's gone back to sleep.

"Feel like we're teenagers at your mum's house, trying to be ninja about it." Billy chuckles, resuming the thrusts, although he's gotten softer almost immediately in anticipation of being walked in on. "You used to be so loud before she was born. And now, not a peep out of you."

"Shut up," John hisses. "It's not like I enjoy it any less."

"That's good to hear. I need rave reviews you know," Billy says smiling. "Keep the ego fed."

"I'll give you a rave review," John whispers, digging his nails into Billy's back, dragging them down when he orgasms with a quiet whimper.

Billy rolls away when he's done, realizing he has to clean up a bit more than usual and gets up to go to the bathroom.

"Are you washing your dick in the sink?" John asks, annoyed when Billy comes back with a moist towel and a new tampon for John.

"How about a thank you that I didn't just roll over and smear blood all over the sheets, hmm?" Billy asks, but it's good natured. He wipes John down, and as a final touch inserts the new tampon inside him with only a little hesitation about how to do it.

"Thank you," John says, as requested, and gets a deep kiss in return. The cramps have stopped, at least temporarily, just as he had hoped.

Chapter 19: March 19, May 1, 2027

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

March 19, 2027

Butcher's picking up groceries while Lena skips around behind him, not really following Homelander's rule of 'feet on the ground in public' in any shape or form as she floats up periodically, twirling and flapping her arms. But Homelander's not here, and Butcher's not about to scold her if she's not disturbing any of the merchandise, and she knows that and dances around to her heart's content. It's the only big supermarket for miles and has been their go-to since they moved here, so just about everyone who works here knows them and smiles and waves at Lena. Butcher has no concerns letting her wander around the aisles.

He glances at the crumpled notepad sheet he jotted the grocery list on. 'SALTINES' is written across the top in Homelander's handwriting, and even though he often writes in all caps, it's appropriately urgent-looking this time. He started suffering with morning sickness much earlier and much more severely this time around. He usually recovers by the afternoon, but his mood has been pretty sour the past week, and just about the only thing he can stand to eat is those bland crackers. Butcher would probably just stay out of his way but it's hard with Lena sensing something being amiss and trying to be clingy with the grumpy parent. 

That was one reason to get her out of the house. Another was to take her to the diner over in Tannersville for breakfast because Homelander can't tolerate the smell of anything being cooked inside the house, even if it's just oatmeal– forget bacon and eggs.

"Daddy, what's a 'supe freak'?" Lena must have walked up behind him without him noticing, and Butcher freezes in his tracks.

"Where'dja hear that, sweetpea?"

"That guy said it." Lena is pointing through a bunch of store shelves, once again forgetting her poor dad's limited vision.

"Show me where he is so I can get a look," Butcher says, gritting his teeth, Lena leading him by the hand toward the checkouts. "That him?" he asks when she points at a man going through the checkout.

Lena smiles and nods.

"You stay right here and watch our basket," Butcher says, putting the groceries down on the floor. The man clearly noticed them and picks up the pace on getting out into the parking lot, but Butcher catches up with him.

"Whadja say to my daughter, you fucking wanker, eh?" Butcher yells as the man tries to escape into his pickup with out-of-state plates and gets his face slammed into the window instead, blood from his nose immediately smearing across the glass.

When Butcher walks back into the store he realizes the error of his ways when he sees Lena's amused face. "What's a wanker?" she asks, cracking up. She didn't budge from the spot he left her in, but of course she could see and hear everything.

"Someone who doesn't know what he's talking about," Butcher tells her. He breathes deeply to calm himself and stop seeing red, but even by the time they're back in the car, he can feel adrenaline still coursing through him. He hasn't punched someone in at least a couple of years now, but doing it brings him right back into a different era of his life, so much so that he absentmindedly reaches into his coat pocket expecting to find a box of cigarettes waiting for him. 

"Daddy, you hit that guy really hard!" Lena says, and Butcher doesn't know if he'd rather she didn't make note of it or if it's a good thing that she can tell that was something out of the ordinary. She's in the front seat, without a seatbelt, kneeling instead of sitting. Not like she needs to sit safely, and Butcher isn't going to make her follow weird protocols to conform to society.

"I did. Wasn't right. Don't ever do something like that," he mutters, forcing a smile and looking at her. "I just got angry."

"So what does 'supe freak' mean?" she asks and he bristles again but forces the bile back down his throat.

"Nothing nice. Don't say it. In fact, let's not talk about this anymore or mention it."

"You mean we shouldn't tell Luvvie?"

Butcher laughs dryly. "I'd prefer not to."

"Why?" she asks and doesn't get an answer as Butcher just starts out for home.

"Do you think Luvvie stopped being sick?"

"Don't know. We'll find out once we're home."

"I don't like the sound when he's sick," she says, frowning. "Why is Luvvie always sick?"

"He's fine. He just doesn't feel well in the morning sometimes."

"It's every day! He goes 'blearghghggh'." She does a pretty good impression of the sound that even Butcher can often make out without the aid of any superhearing from down the hall, so it must be very loud to her ears.

"Yeah. He feels like he needs to throw up. It ain't stomach flu or anything like that. He's alright."

"He smells different than he used to." Lena is still frowning. "I think Luvvie's keeping a secret from you."

"Is that right?" Butcher asks, trying not to look too amused, curious about what she thinks this secret is. "What secret is that?"

Lena shrugs. "Maybe he's eating biscuits at night. Maybe that's why his tummy hurts."

Butcher is amused. It's something Homelander always threatens will happen to Lena if she eats more than two or three. Maybe he's speaking from experience, she must figure.

The long driveway to their house is icy enough that Butcher's car probably can't take the incline while making a turn. He should probably get chains for his tires in the winter, but he's in denial about needing them. If it were up to him they'd live somewhere warmer, much warmer– maybe even tropical, but Homelander seems enamored with upstate New York.

"Do the honors for me, would ya, Leni?"

She knows exactly what he means and is only too happy to oblige, bounding out of the car into the snow and melting the ice without destroying the gravel underneath. Or at least not noticeably. Homelander's been teaching her to have fine temperature control and she manages it beautifully.

"I'm glad you're using our daughter to avoid shoveling or salting," Homelander shouts from upstairs when they walk in. His voice is muffled by a door, so he must still be in the bathroom.

"What's the point of having powers if you don't use 'em for good causes?" Butcher replies. "And she gets practice in."

"Just don't come crying to me if she sets your precious old Cadillac on fire."

Lena stares through the ceiling in the direction the voice is coming from. Butcher has stopped being unnerved by her being able to see through the entire house. He's made peace with her ability, and Homelander has had to make peace with putting a layer of zinc paint on the inner walls and floor of their bedroom. 'Now I can't see her either,' Homelander complained after they finished the job and painted over it to avoid the metallic look. 'So, like most parents whose child sleeps in a separate bedroom, then,' Butcher had to point out to him. 'What do you think will happen to her anyway?' Homelander clearly still has trauma about Ryan's death. Butcher knows he sometimes has nightmares reliving how he lost him, and he knows the cruel trick the mind can play in a dream, transposing one child for another. But Homelander agreed in the end, as long as they kept the outer walls and ceiling zinc-free.

Butcher turns on a TV show for Lena to watch, puts the groceries away and heads upstairs to see what the damage is.

"You sure you're alright?" Butcher asks, not for the first time that morning, looking at Homelander hunched over the toilet, looking like he's trying to heave but probably not having anything left in his stomach by this point in the day.

"Positive," Homelander says in a croaky shaky voice. Butcher crouches down beside him, wipes the sweat off his forehead and brushes his hair back out of his face. 

"Want a glass of water, maybe?"

"No. I just don't know why it's so much worse this time around." Homelander rises to his feet and stands over the sink, staring at himself in the mirror before rinsing his mouth out and starting to brush his teeth.

"Lena's gettin' concerned about you. We should probably tell her."

Homelander shrugs, toothbrush already in his mouth so Butcher can barely make out what he's saying. "I don't see what the rush is."

"I just don't want her peering through you one day and finding it for herself. I figure it might look a little hair-raising without knowing what it is, no?"

Homelander looks down, clearly looking through the floor at Lena, deep in thought, probably making sure she's engrossed with the cartoon she's watching and not listening in. Living with the two of them and with hardly anyone else ever around has slowly made Butcher feel like he's missing essential senses, almost as if he's disabled. But this is what he's signed up for.

"What, you worried she won't take it well?"

"I don't know," Homelander says. "She might not. I don't know how I'd have felt. I wanted a brother once I found out what those were. But I was older. And maybe I would have felt jealous if I had real parents."

Butcher shrugs. "Don't seem like that big of a deal to me, love. But you decide."

"Luvvie, Daddy hit a guy at the store!" Lena says as soon as Homelander makes his way down the stairs accompanied by Butcher, even as her eyes stay glued to the TV screen.

"Wow Lena. Snitch much?" Butcher had just managed to forget what happened during their grocery run.

"Snitch much," Lena repeats quietly to herself, chuckling, apparently amused by how it sounds. Butcher supposes he shouldn't have depended on a three year old keeping mum.

"Really." Homelander looks at Butcher questioningly.

"Yeah he pushed his face into the car and then blood came out, like plughsfh," Lena says, spreading her hands and making some strange sound effect that Butcher's sure he didn't hear, but maybe she did with her super hearing.

"Well I'm sure he had an excellent reason," Homelander says, giving Butcher the side eye. "You should never do it. Superpeople shouldn't ever hit anyone."

"Superpeople?" Lena asks, finally turning away from the cartoon. Butcher was wondering when they were going to have this conversation.

"Yeah, people like me. You. People who don't break easily. Who can fly, see through things." Homelander says, then thinks back to who else she may have met. "You remember Annie? Kimiko?"

Lena shakes her head.

"Yeah we haven't seen them in a while. Maybe we better get reacquainted," Homelander mutters to Butcher. "We're gonna need someone to babysit when…"

Butcher feels a little sick to his stomach remembering how the last birth went, and the fact that Homelander's already starting to lay out childcare plans makes it all the more real.

"And Daddy?"

"No, Daddy is a regular person. So are most people."

"Does supe mean superperson?" Lena asks, and Butcher sometimes hates how quickly she'll sometimes connect certain dots.

Homelander pauses. "It's not a nice word, but yes," he says, looking askance at Butcher again. "Let's not say that word."

Butcher puts his hands up in a silent 'wasn't me' gesture, and retires to the kitchen knowing Homelander will join him there.

"I had no intentions of her seeing any of that…" he starts explaining as soon as Homelander walks in.

"I didn't say anything," Homelander says, making a beeline for the fridge to pour himself a glass of milk. He downs it quickly, in a way that makes Butcher wonder how he doesn't get sick from that, of all things. "Just don't tell me I'm the reason she's violent," he adds, wiping his lips, and Butcher can't tell if he's smug or worried, or both.

"Cunt went and called her a slur and I just saw red. Maybe he said it under his breath, but she heard him. I wanted to kill him, truth be told," Butcher confesses.

"I understand." Homelander has a strangely blank expression on his face. 

Finally he adds. "A lot of supe haters out there. And now it's actually fashionable."

Butcher can't help but feel defensive that even at his peak supe hatred he never went around taunting children, but can't say a word knowing what he called Ryan to Becca's face.

Homelander sighs. "Vought needed to go. But we did lose a lot of the constant positive press we used to have. The Vicky thing certainly didn't help."

One of the fallouts of declassifying cases and cases of documents that had to do with Vought was a few closeted supes getting outed. And in the case of Victoria Neuman, it became obvious that she was behind one of the most gruesome scenes that took place on live television. She submitted herself to a long prison sentence, banking on parole hearings because there had been no protection in place for her. Now the climate has turned against supes in general.

"You decided to tell Lena what she is now, huh. Thought we had a good thing going."

Homelander shrugs. "She's going to learn the hard way sooner or later. You ran into some asshole at a grocery store in the middle of nowhere? You know how many things I hear random people mutter when I'm in the city?"

"And what do you want? The Medal of Self-Restraint?"

"Maybe," Homelander says, floating up to perch on the island counter and opening his legs in clear invitation.

"You gonna puke in my mouth if we kiss?" Butcher asks, slotting himself right against the edge of the counter, running his hands through Homelander's hair.

"Depends on how bad your flirting is about to get. I might."

May 1, 2027

NYT: From the New York Times, I'm Michael Barbaro, and this is The Daily. After months of testimony and investigation, and despite many ongoing suits against specific individuals on its executive team, Vought International proposed its own breakup in April of last year, just over a year ago. The fallout was swift, ripples cascading through the stock market, instability in every industry in which Vought was a major player, which ranged from food and beverage, to entertainment, to weaponry and law enforcement. Things still haven't completely settled.

One of the big mainstay symbols of the company is of course Vought Tower, also often referred to as Seven Tower. There was no talk of demolishing such a tall structure in the middle of a busy block of Manhattan, and the original plans to tear away the facade to remove the iconic numeral seven design were not popular with the public and got scrapped too. So it's here to stay as a landmark. Right now it's a mostly empty office space, but there are no plans to convert it into residential units. Other firms have already bought up the space and have begun slowly moving in and taking over most of the floors. But the top floors were set aside to open a museum documenting the rise and fall of Vought, and we finally got a sneak peak before it opens to the public. The museum opens May 1st, when this episode airs. We'll speak with the museum curator, Michael Saltzman, and his idea behind putting this together. But first we have John Butcher here in the studio with us to discuss the new museum. If that name doesn't ring a bell, he's the man who worked for Vought under the name Homelander for about two decades. John, welcome to the show.

JB: Thanks for having me.

NYT: I don't believe we've ever had the pleasure of having you on the show, so this is a milestone of sorts for us.

JB: I guess not? I did a bunch of interviews with the New York Times by phone back while the the investigation was still going on, but not for this podcast.

NYT: Well, we are very pleased to finally have a chance to speak with you about a subject that may be– hm– very close to your heart and I would imagine, quite fraught?

JB: Yeah, you can probably still consider it a tough period of adjustment for me, even though it's been a few years since the entire thing started unraveling. But I loved Vought, I was a believer in their mission, and I was their posterboy for a very large chunk of my life.

NYT: But then you also became the face of the government's investigation into Vought International. At least the most memorable parts of it.

JB: And that was quite painful, but probably by design. I never really intended to be the tip of the prosecution's spear for all that. But that's how it turned out. I had a unique story to share, being the only person who was raised by them– and you might say owned by them, for all intents and purposes. Or I seem to be the only one who survived being raised by them, I should say. But the prosecution wanted me there for other reasons too. I was still famous at that point, so it was inevitable the media coverage got fixated on my story.

NYT: [laughs] I think you're still famous.

JB: I think they originally planned it as a 'Permanent Exhibition', but the scope kept growing and they raised enough money to make it a museum.

NYT: Right. So they're building this museum on the top floors of Vought Tower. And they called you up at some point? We heard they consulted with you extensively, and that you had curatorial privileges?

"See?" Lena feels proud to be right.

Daddy walks into the living room and looks Lena up and down. "I got nothin' against her wearing it for trick or treating. It's Halloween after all. That's a proper terrifyin' costume."

"Ha. Ha." Luvvie says, and he's not actually laughing. He looks annoyed, and Lena doesn't really understand why. "Well I tried! She wants that one and won't even try this one on. We're raising a complete tomboy."

"What's a tomboy?" Lena asks as she flies up and sits on the ceiling upside down so the American flag cape is hanging down behind her head.

"It's someone who doesn't let anyone else tell 'em what to do. Who's livin' their life to the fullest," Daddy says. 

"Oh," Lena says, still not sure she understands why Luvvie's unhappy about it. "I'm sorry, Luvvie. I didn't want to be a tomboy and argue with you. I just like this costume better."

Luvvie shrugs. "Fine by me if your Daddy doesn't care."

"Now where'd she learn to be so polite with her apologies?" Daddy chuckles quietly. 

"Certainly not from you," Luvvie says, looking tired and grumpy. Lena knows she's not supposed to listen when they talk quietly to each other but she does anyway.

"Daddy, are you a tomboy?" she asks.

Daddy laughs in a way that makes Lena realize she's said something silly, but then he nods and says "I s'ppose I am." He reaches up and yanks lightly on the cape dangling upside down and she drops herself down into his arms.

"Lena. Settle down," Luvvie warns her, but she only beams and jumps out Daddy's arms and prances around the room, feeling the cape waving behind her. She stops in front of her parents, looks up at them and then points before doing her best impression. 

"You guys are the real heroes!"

Luvvie's eyes dart to Daddy's face which changes as soon as she says those words, but Lena can't put her finger on whether he's angry or not. It's like he's thinking about something else completely. 

"I'm not the one who let her watch those movie trailers," Luvvie mumbles.

"To ifinity and beyond!" Lena shouts hoping to distract them and change the mood in the room, and takes off flying around the room with one arm in a fist out in front.

"Infinity," Luvvie corrects her. "And Homelander never flew with his arm like that."

Lena thinks it's funny that Luvvie talks about 'Homelander' as if it wasn't really him at all but some other mysterious person. But he's still really famous for being him. Every time they go out in the city, people still call him by that name and he doesn't correct them, smiles and even stops to take pictures with them.

"Luvvie, can I bleach my hair to look like yours?" Lena asks after she admires herself in the mirror, holding up her hair strands. That's really the biggest missing piece to the costume.

Daddy arches his eyebrows but doesn't say anything.

"No, out of the question," Luvvie says, draping the small Starlight costume over the back of a chair and slowly sits down on the couch, lifting his legs with the adjustable footrest. Lena wonders if Luvvie's gotten meaner since getting pregnant because he doesn't feel well. Daddy says he'll go back to his old self after the baby comes out, but Lena's not sure she can remember what Luvvie was like before he was pregnant.

"Please?" Lena tries not to sound like she's whining because she knows Luvvie doesn't like it, but it's hard not to. "Why can't I?"

"Because bleaching hair is for grownups."

"How old do I have to be to bleach my hair?"

Luvvie shakes his head as if he can't believe she's asking this. "I don't know. Sixteen."

Sixteen might as well be never, Lena thinks morosely.

"When did they start bleaching yours?" Daddy asks.

"Too young. Lena, come here sweetheart. Stop pouting."

Lena shuffles toward him, trying to show him how unhappy she still is, but climbs on the couch to sit next to him. She'd climb into his lap, but there isn't much space there anymore.

Luvvie hugs her and kisses the top of her head. "Why do you want to ruin your beautiful brown hair?" he asks as he cards his fingers through it.

"Why don't you leave yours brown?" Lena asks.

"Because I've got a lot of grays and bleaching covers it up better than anything else."

"You have gray hair? Are you old, Luvvie?"

"Thank you for sounding surprised," Luvvie says and Lena doesn't really know what he means. "Besides, you have beautiful thick dark hair like Daddy's. Mine doesn't look like that."

"Daddy has gray hairs," Lena points out. "In his beard, and near his eyes."

"Yeah, so don't go bleaching yours before you go gray," Daddy says, coming over and tousling her hair too, sitting down beside them. Lena climbs into his lap and watches him run his hand across the big swollen belly peeking out where Luvvie's shirt has ridden up. Lena puts her hand on it too.

"You see the baby inside?" Daddy asks, and Lena thinks it's a silly question until she remembers that Daddy can't see inside things.

"Yeah. She's upside down inside Luvvie. And really really squished, like this–" Lena scrunches up her own body to demonstrate.

"That's a good thing, I s'ppose?" Daddy says, looking over at Luvvie who nods. 

"Are you gonna wear a costume, Luvvie?" Lena asks.

"What costume do you think is going to fit over all this…" Luvvie gestures at his protruding belly.

"You can be a pumpkin?" Lena suggests, and doesn't know why both of her parents start laughing.

"Jesus. Rock bottom," Luvvie says. "I don't know if I need a costume for that."

"You need an orange shirt," Lena points out.

"I don't have an orange shirt," Luvvie tells her.

"You can go as a sexy pumpkin," Daddy says in Luvvie's ear, and Lena's not sure what that word means, even though she's heard it before. "Just go with the entire belly hanging out."

"Talk about scary," Luvvie mumbles.

"You look exhausted, love. You sure you wanna tough it out and come trick or treating? I can take Lena."

Luvvie looks at Lena. "I really wanted to go to her first one. Who knows how many more before she shuns us and doesn't want us following her."

Lena's not sure what 'shuns' means. "I want you to come, Luvvie!"

"Lena, the baby's due any day now. Luvvie might not be up for it."

"No, I'll go," Luvvie says, sighing. "I just want to rest here for a bit."

"I'll bring you a glass of milk!" Lena announces. She notices Luvvie never says no to that, and it makes his mood better. She's proud she can get it all by herself, even if she has to fly up to reach the cupboard with glasses, and to hover over the counter to pour milk out of the gallon. Daddy always looks impressed, even if she's spilled milk on the counter and sometimes forgotten to put the gallon back into the fridge.

"Is the baby getting really heavy?" Lena asks when she resumes her old spot on Daddy's lap and hands Luvvie the tall glass.

"Heavy? Not really," Luvvie replies as he sips. "She's just taking up a lot of space inside me at this point. And still tries to stretch her legs."

"And she doesn't let you sleep?" Lena adds helpfully.

"Not well," Luvvie says. 

"That's because she sleeps all day! And she's eating all the food that's going in your tummy?"

"Well no, I wouldn't say that," Luvvie says, chuckling.

"Come out already baby!" Lena shouts leaning over the protruding belly and the baby stirs slightly. "Luvvie's tired because of you."

Luvvie claps his hand over her mouth, but it's gentle. "Shh. Leave her alone. She'll come out when she wants to."

"But you said I came out late and it hurt!"

Luvvie smiles. "It's supposed to hurt."

Lena stares through, watching the baby. "Why? Because your belly button rips open?"

"Come on, stop scarin' her," Daddy says. "Luvvie's the strongest man on earth. He can take anything. He'll be fine."

"Are you telling Lena or yourself?" Luvvie asks.

"Tell me about how I came out," Lena asks Daddy, impatient to hear the story again. She always wants more details than she gets.

"You didn't really wanna come out, was the problem. So it took more than a day," Daddy says.

"I was coming out of Luvvie's tummy for a whole day?!"

"Almost two days."

"Was there a lot of blood?" Lena asks, pressing her luck in case she gets answers.

Daddy nods. "Yes there was." And he's not smiling, so he's probably not joking.

"Now who's scaring her," Luvvie says. "It was fine. It was the best day of my life when you were born."

Lena frowns, thinking. "Even better than when we went to Disney World?"

Luvvie laughs. "Yes."

"Not the way I remember it," Daddy mumbles.

"It was hard the first time. Maybe it'll go easier the second time around." Luvvie sounds like he's trying to reassure Daddy.

Lena thinks about it for a moment. "What about Ryan?"

"What about Ryan?" Luvvie asks, and his face takes on a slightly sadder look which is why Lena doesn't like mentioning her older brother, but this is something she hasn't understood for a while.

"Wasn't Ryan your first time?"

Both of her parents sit in awkward silence. Daddy is the first one to break it with a laugh. "She's got ya there."

"What?" Lena asks. Every time they talk about Ryan her parents start acting strange. But they go to the cemetery to visit his grave sometimes. She doesn't understand why she can't ask about him if they're allowed to talk about him.

"Nothin' sweetie. You're just sharp as a tack." Daddy tousles her hair.

"Do we really have to revisit this?" Luvvie asks, looking uncomfortable. "Yeah Ryan was my first child. But I didn't – I didn't carry him inside me."

"Oh." Lena thinks for a moment, wondering if this really answered the question. "So you carried him, Daddy?" Maybe this made sense. Children that Daddy carried were boys, and children that Luvvie carried were girls.

Daddy looks at Luvvie as if asking a question, but Lena doesn't hear him say anything.

"No, Ryan was someone else's baby," Luvvie says, and Lena can hear his heartbeat speed up a little.

Lena's eyes widen. "Whose?"

"Someone Daddy and I both knew. But she's gone now," Luvvie says, and his face is so serious that Lena thinks that maybe she should stop asking questions, but she's wanted to know more about this for a long time, and this just raised more questions.

"Is that how you and Daddy met?"

"Yes it was, actually," Luvvie says, and that's one mystery Lena finally got out of them. She's asked them about this before, and they always gave her different answers. 'I met Luvvie in the circus', 'I met Daddy at a Christmas party', 'I met Luvvie exploring the sewer', 'I met Daddy at my boss's house.' None of it made any sense. But meeting through Ryan sounded true, somehow.

"And you fell in love when you met each other?" Lena asks.

"More or less," Luvvie says, each answer sounding short and tense.

"And then… I grew in your belly?" Lena asks, just because she's eager to finally get answers.

"Yep. In some order," Daddy says and Luvvie glares at him.

"Luvvie…" Lena has another question, now that she's heard all this. "Why did a baby start growing inside you?"

"What do you mean." Luvvie's voice isn't even a question. He sounds tense.

"Can a baby just start growing inside you any time?" Lena asks.

"What are you asking," Luvvie says, again, no question in his tone, and his face stony.

Lena looks down at the floor, sensing both of her parents are uncomfortable.

"You scared it might happen to you, Leni?" Daddy asks, chuckling.

Lena nods.

Luvvie's tone softens. "No, it only happens to grownups. Grownups who decide it's a good idea. It doesn't happen randomly."

"Did you decide it was a good idea to have me?"

"Yeah, we did," Daddy chimes in before Luvvie says anything, taking Luvvie's hand into his.

"And same for her?" Lena asks, pointing at the belly.

"Yep," Daddy says, and at least both of them have gone back to smiling.

"So you can make as many babies as you want?"

"Something along those lines," Luvvie says.

"Let's just focus on one at a time, Len," Daddy says. "It takes a lot out of Luvvie."

Lena nods solemnly, remembering the earlier days, when Luvvie kept throwing up, or when he was doubled over in pain from the baby visibly moving around inside him.

"What are you going to name her?" Lena asks, putting her chin in her hands and staring at the baby, even though the baby wasn't really doing anything interesting.

"Good question," Luvvie says. He asks Lena to put the empty glass into the sink, which Lena is only too happy to do before jumping back into Daddy’s lap.

"Yeah we had your name picked out ahead of time," Daddy says. Lena knows she was named after his brother Lenny, and she knows he's gone, but not much more detail than that.

"Did you have a brother, Luvvie?"

"Sadly I did not."

"Maybe we can name her… Pinky."

Luvvie quirks an eyebrow. "What?"

"Or Rubble."

"Is that from that Paw Patrol cartoon?" Daddy asks.

"Or…" Lena starts chuckling to herself during the pause. "We can name her Homelander."

"Just kidding," she adds mischievously. She loves making jokes, especially if it gets Daddy and Luvvie smiling.

"Pulling our leg, Lena?" Daddy asks and grabs her and turns her upside down while she's shrieking.

"I hate you doing that!" Luvvie grumbles. "She's going to kick you one of these days. All day long I tell her not to be hyper inside the house and then you come back from work and mayhem just… starts."

"I won't kick him, Luvvie!" Lena says, hanging upside down, her Daddy swinging her back and forth like a pendulum.

***

There's not much in the way of suburban houses to trick-or-treat at in the Catskills, so Billy is driving them down to White Plains where Annie and Hughie Campbell decided to settle down.

John looks out the window of the passenger seat, thinking about how flying over would have taken a few minutes. But no, Billy has his hangups about flying anywhere. 'What if your water breaks again' he said, as if the last time flying had anything to do with the timing of labor. 'And what if my water breaks while we're in White Plains, then what,' John retorted. 'Are you going to insist that we drive the hour back home? Or maybe we could walk, take the really scenic route?'

"Are we going trick or treating or just going to sit around with your friends while Lena's bored?" John asks. He knows he sounds grumpy, but he genuinely wants Lena to have an entertaining Halloween.

"They'll likely come walk around with us. What, you mind? I thought you and Annie were becoming besties?"

John shrugs.

When they get to the house, Butcher parks on the street while Lena runs up the lawn, apparently recognizing the place from visiting months ago, and doesn't hesitate to ring the doorbell with gusto.

"Just once is enough Lena," John calls after her. "They'll come to the door."

Hughie opens the door, and Lena hasn't met him yet, or at least not in her memory, so she steps back, apparently expecting Annie.

"Come on in," Hughie says looking at her and she relaxes and goes in trustingly. "Wow, you've grown a lot since I last saw you Lena!"

He holds the door open and there’s just that tiny spark of fear in his eyes when he sees John's face. Then they flick down to his belly before rushing away again, clearly trying not to stare.

"Luvvie's not fat, he's pregnant!" Lena helpfully announces to everyone as Annie comes out of another room and Billy joins them inside.

"Thanks for that, Lena. I have my own hype man now," John says.

"Are you ready to go trick or treating?" Annie asks in a slightly more animated voice than her usual, leaning down closer to Lena's eye level.

"Yeah, I've got a pumpkin bucket," Lena holds it up for them to see. "And a costume."

"Yeah, that's … quite a costume," Annie says. 

"It's Homelander. It's what Luvvie used to be at work. Homelander can fly and shoot lasers just like me."

"Wow. Where did you get such a costume?" Annie asks.

"Daddy," Lena says nonchalantly.

"You thought I was going to put that on her?" John asks.

Hughie raises his hands up and shakes his head as if to say they didn't mean anything by the question. "We just didn't know they still sell VCU stuff."

"Oh they sell heaps of 'em cheap at those Spirit Halloween popup stores," Billy says. "Vought's dead but characters are forever. It's that much easier to make this stuff in China without having to worry about licenses and copyright now. They had a ton of your Starlight outfits."

"The old version I hope?" Annie asks.

"Think they had both. Got Lena the one with the skirt."

Annie remembers herself. "Here, Lena, this is the first house you're visiting, so I'll give you some candy for your bucket."

"But I didn't say 'Trick or Treat'," Lena says, puzzled, as Annie drops a couple of mini KitKats in.

"You can still say thank you," John mutters under his breath, maybe quietly enough that others don't notice.

"Thank you Annie!" Lena exclaims, and goes off jumping around without waiting for the 'you're welcome'.

"Lena, feet on the floor in other people's houses," John reminds her.

"She's adorable," Annie tells him quietly. "Kind of uncanny when she's wearing all that. Sometimes I can't believe she's the product of you two."

"Let's go outside!" Lena shouts, and it's not clear if it's because she wants to go trick-or-treating or be allowed to jump around, but they all follow suit.

"Lena, no ringing any doorbells unless we've caught up with you," John says, sometimes weary of being the enforcer parent, because Billy's busy catching up with Hughie. At least Annie seems to be watching Lena like a hawk.

As they start making their way through the neighborhood, people look at Lena, smile, then look up and almost always recognize that it's The Super Formerly Known as Homelander standing on their walkway or lawn and their demeanor quickly devolves into fawning and nerves. John mimes to them that he doesn't want any attention paid to him, and certainly doesn't want people scrambling to get past Lena to take a selfie with him.

"I'm here with my child, I'm not taking selfies," he says, irritable. Maybe he should have stayed home after all. But when he lifts into the air and takes to drifting above the suburban rooftops, he thankfully becomes invisible to almost everyone, because people don't usually lift their face up. He watches Lena trick or treating in peace. Billy and the other two are still walking along the edge of the lawns, following her, and she's having the time of her life collecting candy. She doesn't even notice that he's hovering in the air above her watching her, because she's so engrossed by the trick or treating. He tenses when she catches up to a group of several other kids and approaches them. But then he sees her mingling with them like it's the most natural thing, striking up conversation immediately over what's in their candy buckets, complimenting them on their costumes. Friendly, just like he's taught her, John sighs in relief. Maybe he's drilled it into her, but it's nothing compared to how rigidly he was raised and media trained. He still watches closely, still fearing she'll do something outrageous or dangerous, but so far so good. None of them seem aware of who she is, despite the costume. 

They've made their way around several blocks in a loop before returning home, and John lands softly behind them.

"Luvvie, I got a LOOOOT of candy!" Lena tells him when she finally remembers his presence.

"And how many pieces are you allowed to have?"

"Three," Lena says dutifully, showing the number on her fingers. "And the rest we're going to give to the kids at the orphanage!"

"Wait, Red River?" Hughie asks.

"Yeah! We bring them treats sometimes" Lena says, beaming. "Luvvie brings me there to play. He buys them toys and clothes."

"That's all his impetus," Billy points back at John with his thumb when Hughie and Annie look skeptically impressed. John finds it annoying that everyone seems so shocked when he does something remotely charitable. He did use to save people in his Vought days, goddammit. He did donate money to various causes— although now he's not so sure where funds were coming from or whether they ever really went anywhere while he was with Vought. But why would it surprise anyone that he'd have personal interests in an orphanage for supers?

Lena squeezes her lips together into a thin line as she struggles to open the wrapper of a Reese's peanut butter cup and ends up flattening it into pulp in her hands instead. "Daddy, help me with this," she finally asks, accepting defeat.

"Sorry you had to watch from afar." Billy turns to John as he unwraps a new peanut butter cup for her.

"Oh I had a perfect view," John says, waving off his concern. "I think it's good that she didn't even notice I was there. And you got to hang out with your friends."

Billy peers at his face and John doesn't know what he sees there. "You been crying?" he asks him, quietly, under his breath.

"Oh." John wipes at his eyes. "Maybe. I just get a little emotional watching her get the childhood I always wanted to have. I don't know. It's hormones."

~~~

Lena falls asleep on the ride back home, laid out across the backseat, and John must admit there is something nice and soothing about just sitting and seeing the road and woods pass by in the darkness, the hum of the motor and the tires on the road drowning out many other sounds, like a cocoon. And if there's one nice thing about this ancient car Billy insists on driving it's that the front seat is like a bench, so Lena can sit between them when she wants, and John can raise the armrests and lie down with his head nestling in Billy's lap.

Billy glances down. "Ya tired?" he asks, quietly, so as not to wake Lena.

"No," John says dreamily. He looks up at the roof of the car and looks through to watch the stars remain stationary while trees whiz by.

"You sound a bit sleepy," Billy says, chuckling.

"Maybe I just like being in your lap," John says. "Or maybe it's easier to lie down than sit with a watermelon attached to you. Take your pick."

"Always welcome in my lap," Billy says, eyes staying on the road, while he runs his hand along the side of John's face.

"So did it live up to the hype?" Billy asks him after a long silence.

"What did? Trick-or-treating? Absolutely. Do you see how happy she is? And how friendly and kind, even with strangers? Annie was making some snide remark that she can't believe she's our daughter but sometimes I can't believe it either."

"You're acing bein' a parent, love. Job well done."

"I don't think I'm the only one doing the job."

"Eh. I help out in spots here 'n there. Couldn't do it all myself."

"Neither could I, I don't think." John turns and rubs his nose affectionately against his partner's torso.

"What else did you and Annie talk about for so long afterward?"

"Oh," John says, wondering if he should go into details since this isn't Billy's favorite subject. "We were just discussing how to get organized with a company again. How many supers we need, what sort of company might fit the bill, all that."

"Wow. So she's really on board."

John chuckles. "She said she never wants any of it to be called a 'team' and she'd never work with me on a 'team' ever again. So there's that. Guess she's got some kind of PTSD about it. But yes, she might be on board with the overall mission."

"And what's the overall mission? To hype supes up again?"

"Nooo…" John lilts in mock annoyance, but he values Billy's skepticism towards this. Deep down he too is afraid this might just become another very Vought-like enterprise. "The mission is to use superpowers for the common good. And to differentiate from Vought, there's gonna be no staged PR, no participation in any kind of armed conflict, strict no-kill objective on any assignment. And it doesn't all have to be just brawn, rescuing people out of burning buildings and all that. That might be my flashy specialty. But people like Sonnenberg? Doing lifesaving organ reconstruction instead of fixing noses on Long Island? That's a good look and just as flashy, honestly."

Billy sighs. "Yep, it's all about the look."

"Well, sorry. You know my motives. But my motives and the mission of this thing can be separate and coexist."

There's a silence.

"You don't believe I can organize something that's a net positive for the world?" John asks, and his voice sounds small even to his own ears.

"It's not even that," Billy says, and his hand alights on John's face again, without taking his eyes of the road. "I'm just imagining… we have our home life, sitting down to dinner, and then you get a call and go and rescue people out of a burning building or whatever you're planning."

"Yes. And?"

"I don't know. It's probably nonsense but I start thinking about something happening to you."

John can't help but laugh. "What could happen to me?"

Billy doesn't reply, eyes still on the road.

"Billy… come on. Let's not get irrational."

Billy turns the wheel rather sharply and pulls over on the shoulder of the road. Lena stirs from the sound of the tires on the rougher gravel, but doesn't wake up. Billy looks down at John. "I've seen ya in a world of pain. So sorry if I can't think of you as invincible. I'm gonna worry."

"Billy…" John smiles and reaches up to stroke the side of his face. "Billy, I'm so flattered your objection to this is that you're worried about me. But come on, I'm pretty unbreakable on the outside."

"But I understand," John adds, and Billy turns back into the road.

There's a long pause, and apparently Billy has nothing more to say about that tonight, so John changes the subject. "You had a dog, right?" 

"I… did," Billy says, tone obviously questioning why he's being asked.

"Did?"

"He passed a few years ago. He was old by any dog's standards, but definitely old for a bulldog. Kind of regret not spending more time with him towards the end there. Never brought him over from my aunt's because I wasn't sure how you and he would get along."

"What's that supposed to mean?" John asks, already slightly offended that Billy is making him sound high-maintenance.

"Terror, he was, you know… not how you Yanks like to keep your dogs."

"You'll have to explain," John says. "Apparently I'm not well-versed enough in dogs to know what you're talking about."

"He wasn't fixed, for one. Humped things. Chewed things up. Left slobber in places. Breathed loud in general. I wasn't sure it'd be a good match. And then once Lena was around, I wasn't sure he'd survive a toddler like that when he was old and arthritic. Not that he lived long after she was born."

"Well," John says. "I was thinking of getting her a puppy for Christmas. She keeps asking me for one."

Billy glances down at him, with a strange expression.

"What? You don't think she can be careful yet?"

Billy shakes his head, eyes still on the road. "No. I'm just not ready to add a puppy into the mix when we're about to have a new baby. And an older dog from the shelter can be a challenge with kids too."

"Fair enough. That's why I asked." John sighs. "I want to get her something nice this year. She's old enough to remember this one. And I don't want her feeling left out after the new baby."

"You know, I may not be remembering right at this point, but I gotta tell ya, I don't remember ever feeling left out or jealous for attention when my younger brother was born."

"I don't know if I trust your memory. And she called her sister ugly."

"You mean the time she called her 'weird-looking and slimy'? And that was months ago, so I believe her that those were true statements. Weren't any malice in it."

John sighs through his nose. "I hope so."

Billy's still driving. "You could get her a different pet. Get her a pair of rats."

"Rats?" John can't keep the skepticism out of his voice. "Are they good pets?"

"Good for what you want her to learn, probably."

 

December 25, 2027

They're all settled in, sitting on the floor near the Christmas tree that Lena helped decorate this year, about to open presents. It's such a perfect Rockwellesque scene that of course it doesn't last, and Billy gets a call that he decides he absolutely needs to take.

He goes into another room, as if that's going to be any real courtesy to John and Lena.

It's Marvin's voice on the other end. "I finally went through my mail today. You're shitting me with this card, Butcher. I'm dying."

"Tell him he's on speaker phone when he calls you at this house!" John raises his voice enough so Billy can hear him but that causes little Maryanne to stir in his arms.

"Look, ball-and-chain says watch yer language 'cause they've all got superhearing at this house."

"Ball and chain?" John asks, but apparently not loud enough for Billy to hear, or at least that he can pretend not to hear, and just continue talking.

"And it was his idea to stage the whole thing and then he mailed the cards out himself, so don't pin it on me."

"No man, I meant why the hell do you look like you're being held at gunpoint? You got a beautiful family, all sitting down calmly, and then there's you looming in the background looking like you're about to run away."

"I fucking had it that day. Johnny was seriously contemplating getting matching sweaters."

"So what? Butcher, why you always so embarrassed about doing normal wholesome things?"

"Call me strange, but I don't think sending pictures of yourself to other people is particularly normal."

"Says you. Annie and Hughie send a card every year."

"Well I'm sure they do. I ain't Hughie."

"And Kimiko texts me pictures of little Luc often, not just once a year."

"Look, I take pictures of my kids. I just don't feel like sending them out to the world. I'm a private person."

"Private person married to a celebrity."

"Yeah, well."

"So you did get married. Finally got it out of you."

"Why you acting like it's some kinda scoop? Yeah, we registered at the town hall a few years ago, yeah. Wasn't much sense in John getting a different last name when we were filing all the paperwork for him anyway. Wasn't a big deal."

"You're such a romantic, Butcher."

"Look, just because you don't get to send out Season's Greetings with Janine, don't mean everyone else wants to."

Marvin pauses on the other end of the line.

"Kind of a low blow, Billy," John says in judgmental singsong, hopefully not loudly enough to be heard on the other end of the line.

"Sorry mate. I didn't mean noth– Look, you spending time with her this winter break? How old is she now?"

"Smooth pivot," John mutters and realizes Lena is staring at him, probably wondering if he's talking to her and she's supposed to understand. "Daddy's going to come back soon, his conversations never last very long."

"Fuck you Butcher. She's a high school junior. And yeah I'm spending time with her. Half of the break and New Year's." Marvin finally says. "Going to be visiting colleges with her this summer."

"Ah yeah? Time fuckin' flies."

John sighs in frustration at how many inappropriate words are flying within Lena's earshot.

Lena runs off again.

Billy sits down next to him, wrapping one arm around John's shoulders and ghosting his fingertips over the baby's head very lightly.

Billy makes an incredulous face. "Whaddaya mean?"

'Maryanne' took much longer to be decided than 'Lena'. He mulled over 'Maggie' for a while, but Billy scrunched his nose when he explained that was Maeve's name. John didn't really see the harm in naming her after someone who was important to him and dead now, but Billy was not having it. Aside from that, John didn't have many ideas. It was getting down to the wire, and he went into labor before having settled on one. He asked Dr. Sonnenberg if she wanted to name the child, but she laughed and recused herself. He thought about just naming his child Sonya or Samantha as a tip of the hat anyway, but Billy vetoed anything resembling 'Sam' since that was his dad's name. Labor progressed much faster this time, but John still assumed it would be a long ordeal and tried to distract himself. He kept himself occupied by browsing names similar to Ryan. It felt wrong, or like some sort of joke to name his daughter Rianne or anything that close. He settled on Maryanne, still sneaking in Maggie, and fitting Ryan in as well. Billy agreed, but he may have just been eager to get John off of his phone and focused on the matter at hand. 

Billy had been more nervous that day than John had ever seen him. He wonders if he doesn't fully remember just how bad the first time went. This time things went as smoothly as one could probably hope. Little Maryanne didn't put up as much resistance as Lena had, and didn't laser him on her way out. Or maybe John's body has better memory than his mind does and got the job over and done with eight hours after the first contractions. He didn't fall unconscious, he lost a lot less blood or so Billy tells him, and he didn't run into any issues of milk supply this time around. By the time Hughie and Annie drove Lena back home two days later, the bedroom had been cleaned, and John was up and about as much as his bleeding and his achy weirdly loose hip joints would permit.

"Here you go." Lena shoves a pristine burp cloth towards them and Billy takes it, throws it over his shoulder and gently leans Maryanne over it.

"Yes, Boss," Billy says, giving her a very quick salute before bringing his hand back to the infant's head. Lena is highly amused.

Lena suddenly remembers herself. "Can we open presents now?!"

John nods as he slides to sit back on the floor.

Lena puts the bulky piece of furniture back on the floor gently, looking back at John for further instructions now.

Lena tears the paper, working for a while before she's fully unwrapped the gift.

"... Thank you. What is it?" she says. "Is it a… cage dollhouse?"

Lena turns back to look at him, wide-eyed. "Are you getting me a rabbit?!!" 

"Shh, yes. Maybe even two if you're good."

John waves him off. "We'll go to the shelter and adopt some. And you have to be very very responsible with them. You have to feed them, and clean the hutch, and not let them outside or they'll run away. And you have to be really careful with them. They're even more fragile than Daddy."

John shakes his head. "No, there's one last present. Bring Daddy that envelope from under the tree."

"Oh come on, you didn't have to get me things," Billy trails off as he opens the bulging envelope, and John watches his eyes run back and forth reading the reservation printouts.

"Ahem," John coughs loudly so Billy remembers himself and doesn't risk devastating Lena.

"What is it?" Lena pipes up, tugging on Billy's arm to lower the sheets of paper and let her see but losing interest once she realizes it's a bunch of gray pages and reading is required to decipher it.

Lena gasps. But then follows up "What's the Cayman Islands?"

"It's uh– islands with very nice beaches. In the Caribbean, where it's warm." 

"Have you been there before?" Lena asks.

"No. I haven't." Billy turns to John. "Are you- You sure you're ready to travel with her?"

John shrugs. "Don't see why not. I've got my portable feeding system. Need to pack a few things, but thought it'd be a nice break for you since you don't take vacations on your own."

"The novelty hasn't worn off yet." John smiles and turns to Lena. "So we'll be gone for a few days and then come back and get your rabbits, alright?"

Lena nods, hesitating a little bit about whether this is a fair deal or not.

Lena woke up so early that she ends up falling asleep earlier than her usual bedtime too.

"Well, Santa? How was I supposed to beat that gift? All I got you was new pajamas."

John shrugs. "You didn't need to get me anything. You've already given me two beautiful children."

"The pajamas are nice. Satin. Blue. You know what I like." John leans back on his elbows on the bed, then eyes the crib in their room. "But I won't say no to some nice and vigorous Christmas sex to top it off."

Billy cracks up. "To this day, you still treat me like a hooker."

"How do you wanna be treated?" John asks, tipping his head back as Billy starts kissing up and down his torso.

"Maybe later. Right now I want sex."

He watches Billy kiss his way down his abdomen, which still looks like it's been through something, the dark vertical line still there, and his abdominal skin still hasn't quite shrunk back into place. Who knows if it ever will at age forty six...

"Thanks for dropping by that night," Billy rasps, distracting John out of contemplating his body.

"Which night?" John says lazily, without thinking, and Billy doesn't answer because his mouth is temporarily full of cock. And then John realizes which night Billy's talking about, and leans back into the pillow, closes his eyes, overwhelmed with feeling loved and oh-so-lucky.

Chapter End Notes

That's it. Last chapter of the longest fic I've ever written.
Does "last chapter" mean I'll never write in this universe again? No, it doesn't. I reserve the right to revisit any parts of this timeline for Kinktober or Domaystic or any other challenges.
In fact, here are some 'deleted scenes' written earlier for Kinktober:
Cozy Corner Kinktober prompt #3: Breeding/pregnancy
Cozy Corner Kinktober prompt #13: Nursing/lactation

So why end? An ending is always a somewhat arbitrary point in the story. But I wanted the characters to go through THIS particular emotional arc in this fic, and that's why it ends here. When I started writing the mpreg it was important to me to explore the parenthood part too. I'm very reluctant to introduce OCs into fics, but I hope Lena Butcher was a fun character to show off the changes taking place in the two mains.
Thank you to every reader who commented at any point-- whether all along the way, or sporadically, or just once. I don't know if I can convey that every comment means a lot to me without embarrassing myself, but: every comment means a lot to me.
Also thank you to all the artists who have illustrated scenes from this fic-- that's always absolutely amazing to experience as a fic writer.
My self-indulgent Selfish Gene playlist is stored here.

That's it! Hope you enjoyed the ride!
